Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
6 min
The Qiyas of Oath Expiation: Why Specification Becomes Binding Only Upon Performance
Analogical reasoning and dispute resolution regarding specification of time parts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi qiyas linking specification of time in prayers to specification in oath expiation, and evaluate the dispute about specifying a particular part of time.

Core Idea
Specification of time becomes binding only upon actual performance, just as choosing an expiation becomes binding only upon executing it.

This passage introduces a powerful analogy: just as a person who breaks an oath may choose between feeding, clothing, or freeing a slave but the choice becomes binding only when he actually performs it, similarly, a person who intends to pray at a particular part of the time does not become bound to that part until he actually prays. This qiyas refutes the views of some Shafi'is and Hanafis who claim that a specific part of the time (first or last) is exclusively designated for performance. Understanding this analogy clarifies why any part of the expansive time is valid for ada (timely performance) and not qada.

Guided Path
1
Locate the Qiyas Analogy
Find the passage beginning with 'كالحانث في اليمين' (like the one who breaks an oath). This is the qiyas (analogy) used to support the ruling.
The analogy compares the specification of a part of time to the specification of a type of expiation.
2
Understand the Analogy's Structure
In oath expiation, the person has a choice (takhayyur) among three acts. Specifying one verbally or in intention does not make it binding until he performs it. Similarly, in prayers, specifying a particular part of time does not make that part binding until he performs the prayer in that part.
The key point: non-binding nature of specification before performance.
3
Identify the Dispute
The passage mentions that some Shafi'is claim the first part of time is exclusively for ada, and some Hanafis claim the last part is exclusive. The qiyas shows these views are incorrect because the command is expansive.
The dispute is about which part, if any, is obligatory to perform in.
4
Derive the Hanafi Position
The Hanafi position: any part of the expansive time is valid for ada. Specifying a part does not bind the performer; performance in any part is sufficient.
This is supported by the qiyas and the expansive nature of the command.

بيان موجب الأمر في حكم الوقت ابتنائه على العزيمة، فإن العزيمة في كل صلاة أن يؤدي في تمام الوقت، فالاحتراز عن الكراهة مع الإقبال على العزيمة مما لا يجتمع قط، فجعل هذا القدر من الكراهة عفوًا. حكمه: اشتراط نية التعيين أي من حكم هذا القسم الذي هو ظرف اشتراط نية التعيين بأن يقول: نويت أن أصلي ظهر اليوم ، ولا يصح مطلق النية؛ لأنه لما كان الوقت ظرفًا صالحًا للوقتي وغيره من النوافل، والقضاء يجب أن يعين النية.
ولا يسقط بضيق الوقت أي إذا ضاق الوقت عن التوسعة بسبب تقصيره إلى آخر الوقت، أو بسبب نومه أو نسيانه لا يسقط التعيين عن ذمته؛ لأنه إنما جاء الضيق بسبب العارض، وفي الأصل كان سعة.
مجموعي: وجبت كاملة على العزيمة: اعلم أن الأحكام المشروعة على نوعين عزيمة وهي: اسم لما هو أصل غير متعلق بالعوارض، ورخصة وهو ما يكون شرعه باعتبار العارض. (القمر) في كل صلاة : الكل ههنا إفرادي، ومن فهم أن الكل فقد شطط تأمل. (القمر) أن يؤدي إلخ لتوارد نعم الله تعالى على العبد، وقد جعل له ولاية صرف بعض الأوقات إلى حوائج نفسه رخصته. (القمر) عفوًا لكن بقيت مناقشة وهو: أنه إذا شرع العصر في الوقت الكامل ومدها إلى أن دخل الوقت الناقص، وفرغ قبل آخر الوقت فإن هذه الصلاة جائزة مع أنها لكمال سببها، وقد أديت بصفة النقصان وليس ههنا بناء على العزيمة كما هو الظاهر فتأمل. (القمر) الذي هو ظرف فيه مسامحة، والأولى أن يقال: الذي وقته ظرف (القمر) بأن يقول إلخ : أو ينوي بقلبه معينًا.(القمر) ظهر اليوم فيه إيماء إلى أن المراد بالتعيين تعيين فرض الوقت، ولو نوى فرض الظهر لا يكفي، لأن فرض الظهر يكون أداء وقضاء، فلا يتعين الأداء إلا بذكر فرض الوقت كذا قال ابن الملك، وفي "مشكاة الأنوار": أن نية الظهر المقرون باليوم تعيين وإن خرج الوقت وكذا المقرون بالوقت إن لم يخرج الوقت وفرض الوقت كظهر الوقت،
وإن نوى فرض الظهر ففي فتاوى العتابي الأصح أنه يجزئه؛ لأن كون الفائتة عليه محتمل ولا اعتبار به (القمر) ولا يسقط إلخ: دفع دخل مقدر تقريره أنه لما كان اشتراط نية التعيين لعلّة كون الوقت صالحا للوقتي وغيره، فيلزم منه أن لا يكون نية التعيين شرطًا إذا ضاق الوقت؛ لأن العلة المذكورة هناك مفقود، فأجاب بأن هذا الضيق لا يعتد به لكونه عارضا؛ لأن الوقت في الأصل متوسع فيشترط نية التعيين في صورة الضيق أيضا باعتبار أصل الوقت. (السنبلي) إذا ضاق الوقت أي بحيث لا يسع إلا هذا الفرض (القمر)
ولا يتعين بالتعيين إلا بالأداء أي إن عيّن أحد أول الوقت أو أوسطه، أو آخره لا يتعين بتعيينه اللساني أو القصدي إلا إذا أدى، ففي أي وقت أدى يكون ذلك الوقت متعينًا، وإن لم يؤد فيما عينه بل في جزء آخر لا يسمى قضاء.
كالحانث في اليمين، فإنه يتخير في كفارتها بين ثلاثة أشياء: إطعام عشرة مساكين، أو كسوتهم، أو تحرير رقبة، فإن عين واحدا منها باللسان أو بالقلب لا يتعين عند الله تعالى ما لم يؤده، فإذا أدى صار متعينًا، وإن أدى غير ما عينه أو لا يكون مؤديا.
لا يسمى قضاء: فإن الواجب في الموسع هو الأداء في جزء من الوقت وما قال بعض الشافعية: من أن الجزء الأول متعين للأداء، وفي غير الجزء الأول قضاء، وبعض الحنفية من أن الجزء الأخير متعين للأداء، فإن أدى في الأول يكون نفلاً يسقط به الفرض فخطأ، فإن الأمر وسع فكل جزء من أجزاء الوقت وقت لامتثال الأمر، فالتعيين بالأول أو بالأخير تضييق، وخلاف الأمر فتدبر. (القمر) فإنه يتخير في كفارتها إلخ وإذا لم يجد هذه الأشياء الثلاثة، فعليه صيام ثلاثة أيام كما ينطق به القرآن المجيد، فالخيار إنما هو في هذه الثلاثة لا فيها مع الصوم، فما في مسير" "الدائر" من أن الحانث مخير بين الإطعام والكسوة والتحرير والصوم، فليس بصحيح تأمل. (القمر) وإن أدى غير إلخ كما أنه عين أن يطعم عشرة مساكين، ثم بدأ له أن يحرر رقبة فهذا التحرير يكون أداء، وهذا بناء على أن الواجب في الواجب المخير أحد الأمور كما هو مقتضى كلمة "أو" . (القمر) إلا بكون إلخ في العبارة مسامحة والأولى أن يقول: إلا بكون الوقت في الأول ظرفا، وفي هذا الثاني معياراً . (القمر) فيطول : أي المؤقت بطول الوقت كما في الصيف. (القمر)
أو يكون الوقت معيارا له وسببًا لوجوبه کشهر رمضان عطف على قوله: إما أن يكون ظرفا وهو النوع الثاني من الأنواع الأربعة للمؤقت، ولا فرق بينه وبين القسم الأول إلا
بكون الأول ظرفا، وهذا معياراً والمعيار هو الذي استوعب المؤقت ولا يفضل عنه، فيطول
Topic of the Specific: Explanation of the imperative's implication regarding the ruling of time, built upon determination. Indeed, determination in every prayer is to perform it at the complete time. So avoiding dislike while focusing on determination can never combine. Thus this amount of dislike is made excusable. Its ruling: the condition of specifying intention, meaning from the ruling of this category which is a container, specifying intention is required, such that one says: 'I intend to pray Zuhr today', and absolute intention is not valid; because since time is a container suitable for the timely and other supererogatory prayers, and for make-up, intention must be specified. And it is not dropped due to tightness of time, meaning if time becomes tight for expansion due to his negligence until the end of time, or due to sleep or forgetfulness, specification is not dropped from his liability; because the tightness only came due to an accidental cause, and originally there was spaciousness. Al-Majmu'i: It became obligatory completely upon determination: Know that legislated rulings are of two types: determination, which is a name for that which is foundational, not attached to accidents; and concession, which is what is legislated considering an accident. (Al-Qamar) 'in every prayer': the word 'every' here is individual, and whoever understands 'every' as general has gone far, reflect. (Al-Qamar) 'to perform' etc. due to the succession of Allah's blessings upon the servant, and He has given him authority to spend some times for his own needs as a concession. (Al-Qamar) 'excusable' but a discussion remains: if one begins Asr at the complete time and prolongs it until the deficient time enters, and finishes before the last time, then this prayer is permissible even though its cause is complete and it was performed in a deficient manner, and there is no building upon determination as apparent, so reflect. (Al-Qamar) 'which is a container' has some imprecision, and better to say: 'whose time is a container'. (Al-Qamar) 'by saying' etc.: or he intends in his heart a specific one. (Al-Qamar) 'Zuhr of today' indicates that the intended specification is specification of the obligation of the time, and if he intends 'obligation of Zuhr' it is not sufficient, because the obligation of Zuhr can be performance or make-up, so performance is not specified except by mentioning the obligation of the time. Thus said Ibn al-Malik. And in Mishkat al-Anwar: that the intention of Zuhr coupled with 'today' is specification even if time has exited, and likewise coupled with 'time' if time has not exited, and 'obligation of the time' is like 'Zuhr of the time'. If he intends 'obligation of Zuhr', then in Fatawa al-Atabi the soundest is that it suffices him; because the possibility of a missed prayer upon him is only probable and not considered. (Al-Qamar) 'and it is not dropped' etc.: repelling an anticipated objection, its formulation: since the requirement of specifying intention is due to the cause that time is suitable for the timely and other prayers, it would follow that specifying intention is not a condition when time is tight, because the mentioned cause is absent. So he replied that this tightness is not considered because it is accidental; since time originally is expansive, so specifying intention is required in the case of tightness also considering the original time. (Al-Sunbuli) 'when time becomes tight' i.e., such that it does not accommodate except this obligatory prayer. (Al-Qamar) And it is not specified by specification except by performance: i.e., if one specifies the beginning, middle, or end of time, it is not specified by his verbal or intentional specification until he performs. So in whatever time he performs, that time becomes specified, and if he does not perform in the time he specified but in another part, it is not called make-up. Like the one who breaks an oath: he has a choice in its expiation among three things: feeding ten poor, or clothing them, or freeing a slave. If he specifies one of them verbally or in intent, it is not specified in the sight of Allah until he performs it. When he performs, it becomes specified, and if he performs other than what he specified, he is not considered performing. It is not called make-up: for the obligation in the expansive time is performance in any part of the time. And what some Shafi'is said that the first part is specified for performance and in other than the first part it is make-up, and some Hanafis that the last part is specified for performance, that if one performs in the first it becomes supererogatory by which the obligation is dropped, is incorrect. For the command was expansive, so every part of the time is a time for complying with the order. So specification of the first or last is a restriction and contrary to the command, so reflect. (Al-Qamar) 'he has a choice in its expiation' etc. And if he does not find these three things, then upon him is fasting three days as the Quran declares. So the choice is only among these three, not including fasting. So what is in the circulating statement that the breaker of oath is given choice between feeding, clothing, freeing, and fasting is not correct, reflect. (Al-Qamar) 'and if he performs other than' etc. For example, if he specified that he would feed ten poor, then it occurred to him to free a slave, this freeing is considered performance. This is based on the fact that the obligation in a categorized obligation is one of the things as required by the word 'or'. (Al-Qamar) 'except by being' etc. There is imprecision in the phrasing; better to say: except that in the first category time is a container, and in this second category it is a measure. (Al-Qamar) 'it prolongs' i.e., the time-bound obligation prolongs with the length of time as in summer. Or time is a measure for it and a cause for its obligation, like the month of Ramadan, coordinated with his saying: 'either it is a container' which is the second type of the four types for the time-bound. There is no difference between it and the first category except that the first is a container and this is a measure. The measure is that which encompasses the time-bound and does not exceed it, so it lengthens.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the section regarding the 'specific' topic in usul al-fiqh, focusing on the ruling of time for prayers and the requirement of specifying intention (ta'yin al-niyyah). The author begins by establishing that the ruling for obligatory prayers is built upon 'azima (determination) meaning one should perform the prayer at its complete optimal time. However, to avoid hardship, a slight degree of makruh (dislike) is excused. The key ruling discussed is that for time-bound prayers like Zuhr, one must specify the intention by saying 'I intend to pray Zuhr today' because the time is a container that can accommodate both the obligatory prayer and supererogatory prayers, as well as make-up prayers. Without specification, the intention is general and insufficient. This specification is not dropped even if time becomes tight due to one's own negligence, sleep, or forgetfulness, because the original time is expansive. The commentary then defines 'azima and rukhsah: 'azima is the foundational ruling not attached to accidental circumstances, while rukhsah is a ruling legislated considering an accident. The commentator Al-Qamar raises a subtle issue about performing Asr in the complete time but extending it into the deficient time—this is still valid despite being performed in a deficient manner, which shows the ruling is not strictly built on 'azima. Next, the passage clarifies that specification of intention does not become binding upon the specified part of time until one actually performs the prayer. This is analogous to the expiation for breaking an oath: one may choose between feeding, clothing, or freeing a slave, but the choice becomes binding only upon actual performance. Therefore, if a person intends to pray at the beginning of the time but ends up praying at the end, it is still considered ada (timely performance), not qada (make-up). The commentary then rejects the views of some Shafi'is (that the first part is specified for performance) and some Hanafis (that the last part is specified) as incorrect, because the command is expansive and any part of the time is valid for compliance. Finally, the passage introduces the classification of time-bound obligations into two categories: time as a container (zarf) for obligations like daily prayers where the time extends beyond the act, and time as a measure (mi'yar) for obligations like Ramadan fasting where the time exactly encompasses the act. The difference is that in the first category, the time is a container and the act may be shorter, while in the second, the act fills the entire time.

Key Terms
تخيير (takhayyur): Choosing among multiple permissible options; here, the choice in oath expiation.
تعيين (ta'yin): Specification; here, specifying a particular part of time or a particular expiation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the qiyas to oath expiation, when does the specification of a particular expiation become binding in the sight of Allah?
A) When the person verbally declares it.
B) When the person intends it in the heart.
C) When the person actually performs that expiation.
D) When the person recites the intention aloud.

Key Takeaway
Specification of a part of prayer time or a type of expiation does not become binding until actual performance, because the command is expansive and the choice is not finalized until executed.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

The Non-Binding Nature of Specification in Expanded Obligations
Ruling with illustration and refutation of opposing views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that specification of a particular time in an expanded obligation does not bind until performance, and distinguish it from the opposing Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Specifying a part of an expanded time does not bind; only performance determines compliance.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text addresses a common misunderstanding: when a duty has a wide time window, such as prayer, does verbally or mentally choosing a specific portion obligate you to perform in that portion? The Hanafi answer is clear: no. Only actual performance matters. The author uses the example of oath expiation and refutes both Shafi'i and some Hanafi positions that try to fix the obligation to the first or last part.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
State that specification (ta'yin) of a part of an expanded time does not bind; only actual performance (ada') makes that part the one in which the obligation is fulfilled.
The ruling is based on the expansive nature of the command.
2
Analyze the first example: oath expiation
The oath-breaker has a choice among three expiations. If he verbally or mentally chooses one, it does not become binding until he performs it. If he later performs a different one, that counts as his expiation.
Illustrates that specification does not bind until performance.
3
Analyze the second example: prayer time
If a person specifies the first part of the prayer time but prays later, the prayer is still ada' (performance), not qada' (makeup). The specification does not restrict the valid time.
The command is expansive, so every part is equally valid.
4
Examine the opposing views and Hanafi refutation
Some Shafi'is say the first part is specified for ada'; some Hanafis say the last part is specified. The author refutes both: specifying restricts the expansive command, which is wrong.
The Hanafi position is that specification contradicts the command's breadth.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a person specifies the first part but prays later, the Hanafi ruling is that it is ada', while the Shafi'i view would call it qada'. The difference affects whether any compensation is required.
The Hanafi view gives the worshiper full flexibility within the time.

بيان موجب الأمر في حكم الوقت ولا يتعين بالتعيين إلا بالأداء أي إن عيّن أحد أول الوقت أو أوسطه، أو آخره لا يتعين بتعيينه اللساني أو القصدي إلا إذا أدى، ففي أي وقت أدى يكون ذلك الوقت متعينًا، وإن لم يؤد فيما عينه بل في جزء آخر لا يسمى قضاء.
كالحانث في اليمين، فإنه يتخير في كفارتها بين ثلاثة أشياء: إطعام عشرة مساكين، أو كسوتهم، أو تحرير رقبة، فإن عين واحدا منها باللسان أو بالقلب لا يتعين عند الله تعالى ما لم يؤده، فإذا أدى صار متعينًا، وإن أدى غير ما عينه أو لا يكون مؤديا.

لا يسمى
بل في جزء آخر إلخ يعني العبد مختار في أن يؤدي في أي جزء من الوقت شاء، ولا حق له في تعيين جزء منه؛ لكونه تغييرًا لحكم الشرع، فلا يعتد بتعيينه إلا بالأداء، فإن الجزء الذي أدى فيه صار متعينا بالأداء كما أن الحانث إذا عين شيئا من موجبات الكفارة لا يعتد بتعيينه حتى إذا أدى خلاف ما عينه سابقا يصير مؤديا، فكذلك إذا عين جزء من الوقت للصلاة، ثم أدى بعد ذلك الصلاة في غيره يصير مؤديا لا قاضيًا. (السنبلي) قضاء: فإن الواجب في الموسع هو الأداء في جزء من الوقت وما قال بعض الشافعية: من أن الجزء الأول متعين للأداء، وفي غير الجزء الأول قضاء، وبعض الحنفية من أن الجزء الأخير متعين للأداء، فإن أدى في الأول يكون نفلاً يسقط به الفرض فخطأ، فإن الأمر ،وسع فكل جزء من أجزاء الوقت وقت لامتثال الأمر، فالتعيين بالأول أو بالأخير تضييق، وخلاف الأمر فتدبر. (القمر) فإنه يتخير في كفارتها إلخ وإذا لم يجد هذه الأشياء الثلاثة، فعليه صيام ثلاثة أيام كما ينطق به القرآن المجيد، فالخيار إنما هو في هذه الثلاثة لا فيها مع الصوم، فما في مسير" "الدائر" من أن الحانث مخير بين الإطعام والكسوة والتحرير والصوم، فليس بصحيح تأمل. (القمر) وإن أدى غير إلخ كما أنه عين أن يطعم عشرة مساكين، ثم بدأ له أن يحرر ،رقبة فهذا التحرير يكون أداء ، وهذا بناء على أن الواجب في الواجب المخير أحد الأمور كما هو مقتضى كلمة "أو " . (القمر) إلا بكون إلخ في العبارة مسامحة والأولى أن يقول: إلا بكون الوقت في الأول ظرفا، وفي هذا الثاني معياراً . (القمر) فيطول : أي المؤقت بطول الوقت كما في الصيف. (القمر)
Chapter on the Specific (al-Khass). 155. Explanation of the imperative's implication regarding the ruling of time: it is not specified by specification except by performance. That is, if one specifies the first part of the time, its middle, or its end, it is not specified by his verbal or intentional specification until he performs. So in whatever time he performs, that time becomes specified, and if he does not perform in what he specified but in another part, it is not called qada (compensation). Like the one who breaks an oath: he has a choice in its expiation between three things: feeding ten poor people, or clothing them, or freeing a slave. If he specifies one of them verbally or in his heart, it is not specified with Allah until he performs it. When he performs, it becomes specified, and if he performs other than what he specified, he is not considered performing. Or the time is a standard (miyar) for it and a cause for its obligation, like the month of Ramadan – this is connected to his saying: 'either that it is a container (zarf)' – this is the second type of the four types of time-bound obligations. There is no difference between it and the first type except in the first being a container and this being a standard. The standard is that which encompasses the time-bound act and does not exceed it, so it lengthens. It is not called... 'but in another part etc.' means the servant is free to perform in any part of the time he wishes, and he has no right to specify a part of it because that would be a change to the legal ruling. So his specification is not considered except by performance. For the part in which he performed becomes specified by performance, just as when the oath-breaker specifies something from the expiation options, his specification is not considered; when he performs contrary to what he specified earlier, he becomes a performer. Similarly, if he specifies a part of time for prayer, then after that he prays in another part, he becomes a performer, not a compensator. (al-Sunbulī) 'Compensation': because the obligation in the expanded (musawwa') is performance in a part of time. And what some Shāfi‘īs said – that the first part is specified for performance and in other than the first part it is compensation – and some Ḥanafīs – that the last part is specified for performance, so if he performs in the first it would be supererogatory (nafl) that fulfills the obligation – is wrong. For the command is expansive, so every part of the time is a time for obeying the command. So specification by the first or the last is a restriction and contrary to the command, so reflect. (al-Qamar) 'He has a choice in its expiation etc.' And if he does not find these three things, then he must fast three days, as the Noble Qur’an states. So the choice is only among these three, not including fasting. So what is in 'Musīr al-Dā’ir' – that the oath-breaker is given a choice between feeding, clothing, freeing, and fasting – is not correct; ponder. (al-Qamar) 'And if he performs other than etc.' Just as he specified to feed ten poor people, then it occurred to him to free a slave, this freeing is considered performance. This is based on the fact that the obligation in a choice-based obligation (wājib mukhayyar) is one of the matters, as is the implication of the word 'or'. (al-Qamar) 'Except that etc.' In the expression there is leniency. It would be better to say: except that the time in the first is a container, and in this second it is a standard. (al-Qamar) 'It lengthens': i.e., the time-bound act lengthens with the length of time, as in summer. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter on al-Khass (the Specific) in a Hanafi usul work. It explains the principle that when a duty has an expanded time frame (wajib muwassa'), specifying a particular portion of that time via speech or intention does not legally bind the person to that portion; only actual performance in a portion makes that portion the one in which the duty is fulfilled. The author illustrates with two examples: 1) A person who swears an oath and must perform one of three expiatory acts—feeding ten poor, clothing them, or freeing a slave. If he verbally or mentally chooses one, it is not binding until he actually does it. If he later does a different one, that counts as his expiation. 2) The expanded time for prayer: if a person says 'I will pray in the first part of the time' but actually prays later, the prayer is still ada' (performance), not qada' (makeup). The author then refutes two incorrect views: some Shafi'is claim the first part is obligatory for performance and later parts are qada'; some Hanafis claim the last part is obligatory and performing earlier makes the prayer nafl that fulfills the fard. Both are wrong because the command is expansive—every part of the time is a valid time for compliance; specifying a part contradicts the expansive nature of the command. The passage also clarifies that the choice in expiation is among the three acts (feeding, clothing, freeing) only; if one cannot do any, then fasting three days is required, but fasting is not an optional alternative alongside the three. This is based on the verse (Qur'an 5:89). The author notes that the description of time as 'container' vs. 'standard' is a slight inaccuracy; the first type of time-bound duty uses time as a container (zarf, i.e., the act fits within it), while the second type (like Ramadan fasting) uses time as a standard (miyar, i.e., the act's length varies with the time).

Key Terms
الموسع (al-muwassa'): A duty (wajib) with an expanded time frame, such as prayer within its time period
تعيين (ta'yin): Specification of a particular part of time or option by speech or intention
أداء (ada'): Performance of a duty within its designated time

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person specifies verbally that he will perform the maghrib prayer in the first part of its time, but then prays just before the time ends, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) His prayer is qada' because he violated his specification
B) His prayer is ada' and valid, and his specification is not binding
C) His prayer is nafl and does not fulfill the fard
D) He must repeat the prayer in the first part

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, specification of a time in an expanded obligation does not bind; compliance is determined by actual performance.

Cause of Obligation for Fasting Ramadan: Hanafi Internal Dispute
Different opinions on the cause of Ramadan fasting obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five opinions regarding the cause (sabab) for the obligation of fasting Ramadan and apply the majority position to a subsidiary case.

Core Idea
The cause of Ramadan's obligation is not the entire month but each day's first part, according to the majority.

This passage from Noor al-Anwaar delves into a classic Hanafi usul debate: what exactly triggers the obligation to fast each day of Ramadan? While it may seem that the entire month is the cause, Hanafi scholars analyzed the relationship between cause and effect, the nature of night, and the independence of each day's fast, producing five distinct opinions. The majority position resolves logical and practical inconsistencies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context: time as cause, container, or standard
Recognize that in this usul discussion, time can function as a cause (sabab), a container (zarf), or a standard (miyar). The passage specifies that Ramadan's time is both a standard and a cause.
The author notes that time as a condition (shart) for performance is obvious and not discussed here.
2
List the five opinions on the cause
The text presents five views: (1) entire month, (2) days only excluding nights, (3) first part of the month for the whole month, (4) last part of the night for each day, (5) first part of each day.
Each opinion has its own reasoning and textual/literal evidence.
3
Analyze the evidence for each opinion
For each opinion, consider the logical and textual arguments mentioned in the commentary. For example, the entire month view relies on attribution (idafa) and Qur'an 2:185, but is criticized because the first day's fast would precede its cause.
Pay attention to the rebuttals: e.g., night contradicts fasting, so it cannot be a locus for performance.
4
Identify the majority view and its justification
The text states that the view 'the first part of each day is a cause for its fasting' is chosen by the majority (al-mukhtar 'inda al-aktharin). Its justification: each day is an independent act of worship, and night is incompatible with fasting.
This view avoids the logical problem of cause preceding effect and respects the nature of fasting.
5
Apply the majority view to a test case
Consider the scenario: a person is eligible on the first night of Ramadan, then becomes insane before dawn and recovers after the month. According to the majority view (first part of day 1 is the cause for day 1), does he owe qada for the entire month? Yes, because the cause for day 1 triggered obligation before insanity. According to other views, the result may differ.
This case is mentioned in the commentary from al-Talwih, illustrating the practical consequence (thamarah) of the khilaf.

Source Text

(القمر) فقيل: الشهر إلخ قلت السبب الشهر كله كما اختاره السرخسي، ولكن نقل منه إلى منه إلى جزء منه رعاية للمعيارية كما قلنا في باب الصلاة رعاية للظرفية. (السنبلي) الشهر كله إلخ [ ووجه هذا: أن إضافة الصوم يكون إلى الشهر والإضافة دليل السببية ] سبب للصوم وفيه أنه يلزم حينئذ تقدم الشيء أي صوم أول يوم من رمضان على سببه، وهو مجموع الشهر واللازم باطل (القمر) الأيام فقط إلخ : [ ووجه هذا أن كل ما يكون سببًا للشيء يكون محلاً لأداء ذلك الشيء، ومحل الأداء صوم الأيام دون الليالي]
دون الليالي فإن الليل ينافي الصوم، فكيف يكون سببًا لوجوب الصلاة، وفيه أن سببية الليل لا تقتضي أن يجوز
الأداء في الليل كما أسلم في آخر الوقت، فهو سبب لوجوب الصلاة، ولا يكون الأداء فيه كذا قيل. (القمر) ثم قيل إلخ هذا القول قد اختاره الشارح في التفسير الأحمدي" . (القمر) الجزء الأول إلخ ووجه هذا: أن وجود الأهلية في الجزء الأول من اليوم الأول من الشهر معين لوجوب القضاء تمام الشهر بتقدير حدوث الجنون، فعلم أن السببية في الجزء الأول بلا اشتباه سبب إلخ ولهذا يجب الصوم على من سبب إلخ ولهذا يجب الصوم على من كان أهلاً في أول ليلة من الشهر، ثم جن قبل الإصباح، وأفاق بعد مضي الشهر حتى يلزمه القضاء كذا في "التلويح". (القمر) وقيل إلخ: وقيل: إن سبب وجوب كل صوم الجزء الأخير من الليل من ذلك اليوم، فإن السبب لابد له من أن يتقدم على المسبب.(القمر) أول كل يوم إلخ أي الجزء الأول من كل يوم سبب لصومه، وهو المختار عند الأكثرين؛ لأن صوم كل يوم
منفرد عبادة فيتعلق كل بسبب، والليل ينافي الصوم، فلا يصلح سببًا لوجوب الصوم، وفيه ما مرّ آنفا. (القمر) اكتفاء إلخ فإن كل ما هو مؤقت، فالوقت شرط لأدائه، وهذا معلوم ضرورة بخلاف السبب والمعيار، فإن الوقت قد
لا يكون سببًا كما في الصوم المنذور المعين، وقد لا يكون معياراً كوقت الصلاة ، فلذلك خصهما بالذكر. (القمر)
And it is a cause for its obligation as well, and there is disagreement about it. It was said: the entire month is a cause for fasting. And it was said: the days are the cause of obligation only, not the nights. Then it was said: the first part of the month is a cause for the obligation of fasting the entire month. And it was said: the first of each day is a cause for its fasting separately. And we have mentioned all of this in 'al-Tafsīr al-Aḥmadī'. And he did not mention here its being a condition for performance, although it is also a condition for performance, relying on context. 'And it is a cause etc.' because of the attribution of fasting to the month, like our saying 'fasting of Ramadan'. The principle in complete specification is that the attributed (al-mudāf) is established by the attributive (al-mudāf ilayh), and due to His saying, exalted: 'So whoever among you witnesses the month, let him fast it' (Qur'an 2:185). So witnessing the month is the cause for the obligation of fasting (al-Qamar). 'Also' i.e., just as time in the first type is a cause for obligation. (al-Qamar) 'It was said: the month etc.' I say: the cause is the entire month, as chosen by al-Sarakhsī, but he transferred from it to a part of it, observing the principle of being a standard (mi'yār') as we said in the chapter on prayer, observing the principle of being a container (zarfiyya). (al-Sunbulī) 'The entire month etc.' [The justification for this: that the attribution of fasting is to the month, and attribution is evidence of causality.] It is a cause for fasting, but it entails that the thing, i.e., the fasting of the first day of Ramadan, precedes its cause, which is the entire month, and the necessary consequence is false. (al-Qamar) 'The days only etc.' [The justification for this: that everything that is a cause for something is a locus (maḥall) for performing that thing, and the locus for performance is fasting during the days, not the nights.] Without the nights, for the night contradicts fasting. So how could it be a cause for the obligation of fasting? But it is said that the causality of the night does not require that performance be allowed in the night, just as the end of the time is a cause for the obligation of prayer, but performance is not done in it. (al-Qamar) 'Then it was said etc.' This statement has been chosen by the commentator (al-shāriḥ) in 'al-Tafsīr al-Aḥmadī'. (al-Qamar) 'The first part etc.' The justification for this: that the presence of eligibility (ahliyya) in the first part of the first day of the month is a determinant for the obligation of making up (qadā') the entire month in case of insanity occurring, so it is known that causality in the first part is without doubt. And for this reason, fasting is obligatory on one who was eligible on the first night of the month, then became insane before dawn, and regained sanity after the month passed, so that he must make it up – as in 'al-Talwīḥ'. (al-Qamar) 'And it was said etc.' And it was said: the cause of the obligation of each fast is the last part of the night of that day, for the cause must precede the effect. (al-Qamar) 'The first of each day etc.' i.e., the first part of each day is a cause for its fasting, and it is the chosen view according to the majority, because the fasting of each day is a separate act of worship, so each is connected to a cause, and the night contradicts fasting, so it is not suitable as a cause for the obligation of fasting. In it there is what has just passed. (al-Qamar) 'Relying on context etc.' For everything that is time-bound, time is a condition for its performance, and this is known necessarily, unlike the cause and the standard. For time may not be a cause, as in a vowed fast (naḏhr mu'ayyan), and it may not be a standard, like the time of prayer. Therefore, He specified them (the cause and standard) for mention. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage discusses the different opinions within the Hanafi school regarding the exact cause (sabab) that triggers the obligation to fast in Ramadan. The context is the classification of time-bound duties: some time is a container (zarf) for the act, some is a standard (miyar), and some is a cause (sabab). For Ramadan, time is both a standard and a cause. The author lists five views: (1) The entire month is the cause (chosen by Sarakhsi, but criticized because the first day's fast would precede the cause). (2) Only the days (not nights) are the cause, since night contradicts fasting and cannot be a locus for performance. (3) The first part of the month is the cause for the entire month's obligation (chosen by the commentator in 'al-Tafsīr al-Aḥmadī'); evidence: if one is eligible at the first night and then becomes insane, he must make up the entire month, showing the cause is at the beginning. (4) The last part of the night of each day is the cause (so it precedes the fast). (5) The first part of each day individually is the cause (preferred by the majority, because each day is an independent worship). The passage also notes that time being a condition (shart) for performance is obvious, so the author does not mention it explicitly, unlike the cause and standard which may be absent in some cases (e.g., a vowed fast has no particular time cause; prayer time is not a standard because prayer duration doesn't vary). The discussion shows the refinement of usul analysis in determining the precise cause of obligation.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): The cause or trigger that makes an obligation incumbent
شهر رمضان (shahr Ramaḍān): The lunar month of Ramadan, to which fasting is attributed
المعيارية (al-mi'yāriyya): The property of time being a standard that encompasses the act without excess
إضافة (idāfa): Grammatical attribution that suggests causality in Hanafi usul

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi position mentioned in this text, what is the cause (sabab) for the obligation of fasting each day of Ramadan?
A) The entire month of Ramadan
B) The days of the month excluding nights
C) The first part of each day
D) The last part of the previous night

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school refined the cause of Ramadan fasting from the general month to the first part of each day, avoiding logical inconsistencies and providing a precise operative cause.

Types of Time-Bound Fasting and Niyyah Conditions
Defines categories of mu'aqqat acts and rules for intention specification and lapse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three categories of time-bound fasting (mu'aqqat) and state the rules of intention specification (niyyat al-ta'yin), night intention (tabyit), and lapse (fawat) for each.

Core Idea
Time-bound fasting divides into three types: each has distinct intention and lapse rules.

This passage classifies fasting obligations based on how time relates to them: as container, standard, or neither. Understanding this classification is essential for applying the correct conditions for intention (niyyah) and knowing when a missed fast can be made up versus when it is permanently lost. We will unpack the definitions, the rulings on intention specification and night intention, and a key difference with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding fidya for delayed qada.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Recognize the tripartite distinction based on the role of time: (1) time as container (zarf) and cause (sabab), (2) time as standard (mi'yar) and cause, (3) time neither container nor cause but merely a day for fasting.
Category 1 includes daily prayers and Ramadan fast. Category 2 includes specified vow (nadhr mu'ayyan). Category 3 includes qada, kaffarah, and absolute vow (nadhr mutlaq).
2
Distinguish rulings on ta'yin (specification)
Note which categories require intention of specification: category 3 requires ta'yin; categories 1 and 2 do not (absolute intention suffices).
For category 2, intention of supererogatory also works; for category 1, no ta'yin at all.
3
Determine requirement of tabyit (night intention)
Apply that category 3 requires tabyit; categories 1 and 2 do not. Reason: everything besides Ramadan is a place for nafl, so tabyit prevents defaulting to nafl.
Tabyit means making intention during the night before dawn.
4
Evaluate possibility of fawat (lapse)
Understand that categories 1 and 2 can lapse if time passes (requires qada), while category 3 does not lapse until death; any time before death is valid for performance.
Hanafi position: no fidya for delaying qada; contrary to Shafi'i.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مبحث الخاص

بيان موجب الأمر في حكم الوقت وإنما يخالفه في بعض أحكامه وهو اشتراط نية التعيين وعدم احتمال الفوات، ولذا قيده به، والظاهر أن النذر المعين شريك لرمضان في كون الأيام معيارا له، وسببًا للوجوب بعد ما أوجب على نفسه في هذه الأيام، وإن قالوا بأن النذر سبب للوجوب. والحاصل أن النذر المعين شريك لرمضان في بعض الأحكام، ولقضاء رمضان في بعض آخر فألحق بأيهما شئت، وصاحب "المنتخب الحسامي جعل النذر المعين من جنس صوم رمضان ولم يذكر قضاء رمضان والنذر المطلق من أقسام الأمر المقيد، بل هو مطلق من قبيل الزكاة
عن الوقت
وصدقة الفطر، ومن أدخلهما في المقيد نظر إلى أنهما مقيدان بالأيام دون الليالي وهذا تمحل.
وإنما يخالفه إلخ توضيحه أن النذر المعين يخالف النذر المطلق في بعض الأحكام، وهو أن نية التعيين شرط في النذر المطلق لا في النذر المعين، فإنه يصح بمطلق النية، وبنية صوم النفل ؛ وذلك لأن الوقت متعين في النذر المعين، وغير معين في النذر المطلق، وأن النذر المطلق لا يحتمل الفوات بل كلما أدى يكون أداء بخلاف النذر المعين، فإنه أدى في غير الوقت المعين لا يكون أداء، وأما قضاء رمضان فيشترط فيه نية التعيين ولا يحتمل الفوات أيضًا، فالنذر المطلق يشابه قضاء رمضان في هذه الأحكام، ولذا قيد المصنف النذر بالمطلق و لم يطلق النذر. (القمر) اشتراط إلخ ففي المطلق نية التعيين شرط واحتمال الفوات معدوم والمعين بخلافه (السنبلي) شريك لرمضان: أي هو من النوع الثاني فلا يرد أن النذر المعين نوع علي حدة، فصارت الأنواع للمقيد خمسة (المحشي) في بعض الأحكام وهو كون الوقت سببًا للوجوب وإن كان بعد إيجاب نفسه.(القمر) في بعض آخر وهو عدم كون الوقت في نفسه سببًا للوجوب . (القمر) من جنس صوم رمضان: أي من جنس ما صار الوقت معيارا له سببًا لوجوبه . (القمر) مطلق إلخ باعتبار أنه مطلق عن الوقت المحدود أي لم يتعلق أداؤه بوقت محدود على وجه يفوت الأداء بفوته (السنبلي) ومن أدخلهما : أي قضاء رمضان والنذر المطلق. (القمر) مقيدان إلخ : فالمراد من المؤقت ما لا يؤدي إلا ببعض الأوقات دون بعض. (القمر) وهذا تمحل: فإن الصوم من حيث إنه صوم ما شرع إلا في اليوم، فلم يجز في الليل؛ لعدم شرعيته لا لعدم وقت القضاء، دقيق النظر يحكم بأن قضاء رمضان والنذر المطلق ليسا من أقسام المؤقت بالمعنى المذكور سابقا. (القمر) وهذا تمحل إلخ لأن المراد بالمقيد ما يكون متعينًا في وقت يفوت بفوته على ما سبق، والنذر المطلق ليس من
أقسام المقيد بهذا المعنى وإن كان مقيدًا بالنظر إلى الأيام. (السنبلي)
مبحث الخاص
١٦٢
بيان موجب الأمر في حكم الوقت وتشترط فيه نية التعيين ولا يحتمل الفوات، بخلاف الأولين أي يشترط في هذا القسم الثالث من المؤقت نية التعيين بأن يقول : نويت للقضاء والنذر، ولا يتأدى بمطلق النية، ولا بنية النفل أو واجب آخر.
كذا يشترط فيه التبييت أي النية من الليل؛ لأن ما سوى رمضان كله محل للنفل، فيقع جميع الإمساكات على النفل ما لم يعين من الليل الصوم العارضي، وهو القضاء والكفارة والنذر المطلق، بخلاف النذر المعين، فإنه يتأدى مطلق النية ونية النفل، ولكن لا يتأدى بنية واجب آخر ولا يشترط فيه التبييت؛ لأنه معين في نفسه كرمضان لا يقع الإمساك المطلق
من القضاء والكفارة
النذر المعين
إلا عليه ما لم يصرفه إلى واجب آخر، وأيضًا لا يحتمل هذا القسم الثالث الفوات؛ بل كلما صام له يكون مؤديا ؛ لأن كل العمر محل له عندنا، وعند الشافعي له: إن لم يقض رمضان
حتى جاء رمضان آخر تجب عليه الفدية مع القضاء جبرًا له على التكاسل والتهاون. بخلاف القسمين الأولين وهما الصلاة والصوم فإنهما يحتملان الفوات إذا لم يؤدهما في الوقت المعهود، فيكون قضاء.
نية التعيين إلخ لعدم تعيين الوقت للقضاء والنذر المطلق، واحتمال الوقت صوم النفل، وهو صوم الوقت؛ لأن ما سوى رمضان كله محل النفل كذا في "الدائر". (السنبلي) ولا يحتمل الفوات إلى أي بالتأخير لعدم تعيين الوقت؛ إذ الوقت غير معين إلى أن يموت بخلاف الصلاة وصوم رمضان؛ لتوقيتهما بالوقت والعمر ههنا كالوقت
قمه. (السنبلي) بخلاف الأولين إلخ أي صلاة الوقت وصوم الوقت فإنهما يحتملان الفوات لتوقيتهما.(السنبلي) فإنه يتأدى إلخ كما أن صوم رمضان يتأدى مطلق النية ونية النفل (القمر) ولكن لا يتأدى إلخ: فرقًا بين إيجاب العبد وإيجاب الله تعالى. (القمر) بل كلما صام له إلخ فيه إيماء إلى أن المراد بعدم احتمال الفوات عدم القضاء له،
فإنه كلما صام كان أداء لا قضاء وليس المراد أنه لا يفوت أصلاً، فإن الفوات قد يتحقق بالموت.(القمر)
الأولين: أي ما كان الوقت فيه ظرفا وسببًا، وما كان الوقت فيه معيارا وسببا. (القمر)
Section on al-Khas 171: Explanation of the obligating factor of the command regarding the ruling of time. It differs from it in some of its rulings: requiring the intention of specification and the absence of possibility of lapse. Therefore he restricted it with it. And it appears that the specified vow shares with Ramadan in that the days are a standard for it and a cause for obligation after he has obligated it upon himself in these days, even though they said that the vow is a cause for obligation. The summary: the specified vow shares with Ramadan in some rulings and with qada of Ramadan in others, so attach it to whichever you wish. The author of al-Muntakhab al-Husami made the specified vow of the same type as the fast of Ramadan and did not mention qada of Ramadan, and the absolute vow is from the categories of the time-bound matter; rather it is absolute of the type of zakat concerning time and sadaqat al-fitr. Whoever includes both of them in the time-bound considers that they are restricted to days without nights, and this is a forced interpretation. 'And it differs from it etc.' its clarification: that the specified vow differs from the absolute vow in some rulings, namely that intention of specification is a condition in the absolute vow but not in the specified vow; for it is valid with absolute intention and with intention of supererogatory fast. That is because the time is specified in the specified vow and not specified in the absolute vow, and the absolute vow does not admit of lapse; rather whenever one performs it, it is performance. Contrary to the specified vow: if performed outside the specified time it is not performance. As for qada of Ramadan, intention of specification is required in it and it also does not admit of lapse. So the absolute vow resembles qada of Ramadan in these rulings, therefore the author restricted the vow to the absolute and did not leave the vow unrestricted. (al-Qamar) 'Requiring etc.' so in the absolute, intention of specification is a condition and the possibility of lapse is absent, while the specified is contrary. (al-Sunbuli) 'Shares with Ramadan' i.e. it is of the second type, so it is not objected that the specified vow is a separate type; thus the types of the time-bound become five. (al-Muhashi) 'In some rulings': that time is a cause for obligation even if it is after obligating oneself. (al-Qamar) 'In some others': that time in itself is not a cause for obligation. (al-Qamar) 'Of the same type as the fast of Ramadan' i.e. of the type where time has become a standard for it and a cause for its obligation. (al-Qamar) 'Absolute etc.' in the sense that it is unrestricted regarding the specified time, i.e. its performance is not tied to a specified time in a way that performance is lost by its passing. (al-Sunbuli) 'Whoever includes both' i.e. qada of Ramadan and absolute vow. (al-Qamar) 'Restricted etc.' so the meaning of 'time-bound' is what cannot be performed except in some times and not others. (al-Qamar) 'This is a forced interpretation' because fasting as such is only prescribed daytime, so it is not valid at night; due to lack of its prescription, not due to lack of time for qada. Precise consideration judges that qada of Ramadan and the absolute vow are not from the categories of time-bound in the previously mentioned sense. (al-Qamar) 'This is forced etc.' because the meaning of 'time-bound' is what is specified in a time that is lost by its passing as per what preceded, and the absolute vow is not from the categories of time-bound in this sense even if it is restricted with regard to days. (al-Sunbuli) Section on al-Khas 162: Explanation of the obligating factor of the command regarding the ruling of time. And intention of specification is required in it and it does not admit of lapse, contrary to the first two (categories). i.e. in this third category of time-bound acts, intention of specification is required, by saying 'I intend for qada and the vow', and it is not fulfilled by absolute intention, nor by intention of supererogatory or another obligatory act. Likewise, tabyit (night intention) is required in it, because everything other than Ramadan is a place for supererogatory acts; so all abstentions fall on supererogatory unless one specifies from the night the temporary fast, which is qada, expiation, and absolute vow. Contrary to the specified vow: it is fulfilled by absolute intention and intention of supererogatory, but it is not fulfilled by intention of another obligatory act. Nor is tabyit required in it; because it is specified in itself like Ramadan: absolute abstention does not apply except to it as long as one does not divert it to another obligatory act. Also, this third category does not admit of lapse; rather whenever one fasts for it, he is performing it; because for us, all of life is a place for it. According to al-Shafi'i: if one does not make up Ramadan until the next Ramadan arrives, fidya is obligatory along with qada as a deterrent for laziness and negligence. Contrary to the first two categories which are prayer and fasting: they admit of lapse if not performed in the usual time, so they become qada. 'Intention of specification etc.' because the time is not specified for qada and absolute vow, and the time is possible for supererogatory fast, which is the fast of the time; because everything other than Ramadan is a place for supererogatory. (al-Sunbuli) 'It does not admit of lapse' i.e. by delay, because the time is unspecified until death, unlike prayer and fast of Ramadan due to being time-bound; here life is like the time. (al-Sunbuli) 'Contrary to the first two' i.e. time-bound prayer and time-bound fast: they admit of lapse due to being time-bound. (al-Sunbuli) 'It is fulfilled etc.' just as the fast of Ramadan is fulfilled by absolute intention and intention of supererogatory. (al-Qamar) 'But it is not fulfilled etc.' as a distinction between obligation from the servant and obligation from Allah. (al-Qamar) 'Rather whenever one fasts for it etc.' in it there is a hint that what is meant by not admitting of lapse is that there is no qada for it; for whenever one fasts it is performance, not qada. It does not mean that it is not lost at all, because loss may occur by death. (al-Qamar) 'The first two' i.e. where time is a container and a cause, and where time is a standard and a cause. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a usul al-fiqh discussion defining the categories of time-bound (mu'aqqat) fasting obligations and the rulings of intention (niyyah) and lapse (fawat). The text distinguishes three types: (1) where time is both container (zarf) and cause (sabab), like the five daily prayers and the fast of Ramadan; (2) where time is a standard (mi'yar) and cause, like the specified vow (nadhr mu'ayyan); (3) where time is neither container nor cause, but the obligation is due to a reason like qada, kaffarah, or absolute vow (nadhr mutlaq). The main discussion focuses on the conditions for niyyah: for the first type, intention of specification is not required; for the second (specified vow), absolute intention suffices; for the third (qada, kaffarah, absolute vow), intention of specification is required along with tabyit (night intention). The text also notes that the third type does not admit of fawat (lapse) because any time before death is valid for performance, unlike the first two which are lost if the time passes. A difference with Imam al-Shafi'i is mentioned regarding qada of Ramadan if delayed until the next Ramadan. The author clarifies that the absolute vow is not truly time-bound in the sense of being lost by passing time, but is restricted to days of fasting, not nights.

Key Terms
نية التعيين (niyyat al-ta'yin): Intention that specifies the particular obligation being performed, e.g., 'I intend qada of Ramadan'.
النذر المعين (al-nadhr al-mu'ayyan): A vow tied to a specific time, e.g., 'I will fast on Friday'.
النذر المطلق (al-nadhr al-mutlaq): A vow not tied to a specific time, e.g., 'I will fast for three days'.
التبييت (al-tabyit): Making the intention during the night before the fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which type(s) of fasting do not require tabyit (night intention)?
A) Ramadan and specified vow (nadhr mu'ayyan)
B) Qada and absolute vow (nadhr mutlaq)
C) Ramadan and qada
D) All types require tabyit

Key Takeaway
The tripartite classification of time-bound fasting dictates whether intention specification, night intention, and the possibility of lapse apply.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

The Third Category of Muwaqqat: Intention and Fawat Rules
Explains the third category of time-bound obligations and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the third category of time-bound obligations (muwaqqat), apply the requirements of niyyat al-ta'yin and tabyt, and evaluate the Hanafi position that such obligations do not admit of fawat, contrasting with the Shafi'i view on fidyah for delayed qada.

Core Idea
Obligations with unspecified time require specific intention but cannot be missed—any performance counts as ada.

The Hanafi usul classifies time-bound obligations (muwaqqat) into three categories. The first two (prayer and Ramadan fast) are tied to specific times and can be missed, requiring qada. The third category—qada fasts, kaffara fasts, and unconditional vows (nadhr mutlaq)—has no fixed time but must be performed. This passage explains the unique requirements for this category: the intention must specify the type of fast and must be made at night, because any day outside Ramadan defaults to nafl. Moreover, this category never becomes qada; any performance is ada because the entire lifespan is its time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the third category of muwaqqat
Find the description of the third category in the text: obligations where the time is not specified, such as qada, kaffara, and nadhr mutlaq. Note that it contrasts with the first two types whose times are defined.
The passage explicitly contrasts with 'the first two' (prayer and Ramadan fast).
2
Extract the conditions for validity
List the two conditions: intention of specification (niyyat al-ta'yin) and night intention (tabyt). Understand why these are needed: without specification, the fast defaults to nafl because every day outside Ramadan is a place for nafl.
The text says: 'يشترط فيه نية التعيين' and 'يشترط فيه التبييت'.
3
Analyze the fawat rule
The passage states this category does not admit of fawat (being missed). Clarify that 'not admitting fawat' means that whenever one performs it, it is ada, not qada. However, it can be missed by death.
Al-Qamar explains: 'ليس المراد أنه لا يفوت أصلاً، فإن الفوات قد يتحقق بالموت'.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Note the Shafi'i ruling: if one delays qada of Ramadan until the next Ramadan, fidyah is required along with qada. The Hanafi position holds no fidyah, using the lifespan as the time for qada.
The dispute is recorded in the text: 'وعند الشافعي له: إن لم يقض رمضان حتى جاء رمضان آخر تجب عليه الفدية مع القضاء'.

Source Text

مبحث الخاص
بيان موجب الأمر في حكم الوقت وتشترط فيه نية التعيين ولا يحتمل الفوات، بخلاف الأولين أي يشترط في هذا القسم الثالث من المؤقت نية التعيين بأن يقول : نويت للقضاء والنذر، ولا يتأدى بمطلق النية، ولا بنية النفل أو واجب آخر. كذا يشترط فيه التبييت أي النية من الليل؛ لأن ما سوى رمضان كله محل للنفل، فيقع جميع الإمساكات على النفل ما لم يعين من الليل الصوم العارضي، وهو القضاء والكفارة والنذر المطلق، بخلاف النذر المعين، فإنه يتأدى مطلق النية ونية النفل، ولكن لا يتأدى بنية واجب آخر ولا يشترط فيه التبييت؛ لأنه معين في نفسه كرمضان لا يقع الإمساك المطلق من القضاء والكفارة النذر المعين إلا عليه ما لم يصرفه إلى واجب آخر، وأيضًا لا يحتمل هذا القسم الثالث الفوات؛ بل كلما صام له يكون مؤديا ؛ لأن كل العمر محل له عندنا، وعند الشافعي له: إن لم يقض رمضان حتى جاء رمضان آخر تجب عليه الفدية مع القضاء جبرًا له على التكاسل والتهاون. بخلاف القسمين الأولين وهما الصلاة والصوم فإنهما يحتملان الفوات إذا لم يؤدهما في الوقت المعهود، فيكون قضاء. نية التعيين إلخ لعدم تعيين الوقت للقضاء والنذر المطلق، واحتمال الوقت صوم النفل، وهو صوم الوقت؛ لأن ما سوى رمضان كله محل النفل كذا في "الدائر". (السنبلي) ولا يحتمل الفوات إلى أي بالتأخير لعدم تعيين الوقت؛ إذ الوقت غير معين إلى أن يموت بخلاف الصلاة وصوم رمضان؛ لتوقيتهما بالوقت والعمر ههنا كالوقت قمه. Section on al-Khass. Explanation of the implication of the command regarding the ruling of time. It requires intention of specification and does not admit of being missed, contrary to the first two. That is, in this third category of time-bound, intention of specification is required, such that he says: I intended for qada and nadhr, and it is not performed by absolute intention, nor by intention of nafl or another wajib. Similarly, tabyt (night intention) is required because everything besides Ramadan is a place for nafl, so all fasts fall as nafl unless he specifies from the night the contingent fast, which is qada, kaffara, and mutlaq nadhr, unlike mu'ayyan nadhr, for it is performed by absolute intention and intention of nafl, but not by intention of another wajib, and tabyt is not required because it is specified in itself like Ramadan; the absolute fast from qada and kaffara does not fall except upon it as long as he does not divert it to another wajib. Also, this third category does not admit of fawat; rather, whenever he fasts for it, he is performing it, because the entire lifespan is a place for it according to us, while according to al-Shafi'i, if he does not make up Ramadan until another Ramadan comes, fidyah is obligatory along with qada as a compulsion for his laziness and negligence. Contrary to the first two categories, which are prayer and fasting (of specific time), they admit of fawat if not performed in the prescribed time, then become qada. Intention of specification etc. because the time for qada and mutlaq nadhr is not specified, and the time is prone to nafl fasting, which is fasting of the time; because everything besides Ramadan is a place for nafl, as stated in al-Da'ir. (al-Sunbuli) And it does not admit of fawat, i.e., by delay, because the time is not specified; the time is unspecified until death, contrary to prayer and the fast of Ramadan because they are timed by the time, and the lifespan here is like time. (al-Sunbuli) Contrary to the first two etc., i.e., the prayer of time and the fast of time, they admit of fawat because they are timed. (al-Sunbuli) It is performed etc. just as the fast of Ramadan is performed by absolute intention and intention of nafl (al-Qamar). But it is not performed etc.: distinction between the obligation of a servant and the obligation of Allah. (al-Qamar) Rather, whenever he fasts for it etc., there is an indication that what is meant by not admitting of fawat is that there is no qada for it, for whenever he fasts it is performance not qada, and it is not meant that it cannot be missed at all, for fawat may occur by death. (al-Qamar) The first two: i.e., what the time is a container and cause in it, and what the time is a measure and cause in it. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage addresses the third category of time-bound obligations (muwaqqat). The category comprises obligations where the time is not specified but contingent, such as qada fasts, kaffara fasts, and unconditional vows (nadhr mutlaq). The ruling states that for these, the intention must specify the type (niyyat al-ta'yin) and must be made at night (tabyt). This is because any day outside Ramadan is potentially a nafl fast, so without specification, the fast defaults to nafl. Additionally, this category does not admit of being missed (fawat) because the entire lifespan is the time for performance; thus, any fast kept for it counts as ada (on-time performance), not qada. The passage contrasts this with the first two categories: prayer and the fast of Ramadan (or other time-specific fasts), which are tied to specific times and can be missed, thereby requiring qada. It also distinguishes the unconditional vow (nadhr mutlaq) from the conditional vow (nadhr mu'ayyan), which is like Ramadan in that it does not require specification or tabyt. The text also notes the Shafi'i position that if one delays qada of Ramadan until the next Ramadan, fidyah is due, whereas in the Hanafi school no fidyah is required. The commentary by al-Sunbuli and al-Qamar further clarifies that 'not admitting of fawat' does not mean it can never be missed entirely—death can cause it to be missed—but that if one performs it, it is always ada, not qada.

Key Terms
نية التعيين (niyyat al-ta'yin): Intention that specifies the type of fast, e.g., qada or nadhr
تبييت (tabyt): Making the intention at night before dawn
فوات (fawat): Missing the opportunity to perform the act in its prescribed time, necessitating qada
مؤقت (muwaqqat): An obligation tied to a specific time or time frame
النذر المطلق (al-nadhr al-mutlaq): An unconditional vow to perform an act without specifying a time
النذر المعين (al-nadhr al-mu'ayyan): A vow specifying a particular time for the act

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a condition for the validity of a qada fast according to the third category of muwaqqat?
A) The intention must be made at night
B) The intention must be absolute
C) The intention can be for nafl
D) No intention is required

Key Takeaway
The third category of muwaqqat requires specification of intention and night intention, and any performance counts as ada because the entire lifespan is its time.

The Mushkil Time: Hajj as Both Container and Measure
Definition and analysis of the fourth muwaqqat type

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the mushkil type of muwaqqat, explain its dual nature using the time of Hajj, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding temporal restriction and expansion.

Core Idea
The time for Hajj is both a container and a measure—this ambiguity defines the mushkil category.

In the previous lessons, we learned about time-bound obligations (muwaqqat) where the time is either purely a container (zarf) or purely a measure (mi'yar). Now we encounter a fourth type where the time is ambiguous—mushkil—displaying features of both. The sole example in the Hanafi usul tradition is the time for Hajj. This passage explores the two angles that create this ambiguity and notes a difference of opinion between the two major disciples of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this category sharpens our analysis of how time interacts with obligations, especially for once-in-a-lifetime duties.

Guided Path
1
Recall the two pure types of muwaqqat
First, remind yourself of the container (zarf) time, which is surplus and can accommodate multiple acts, and the measure (mi'yar) time, which is exactly filled by a single act. This background is necessary to see the hybrid nature of mushkil.
Prayer times are containers; fasting times are measures.
2
Understand the meaning of mushkil in this context
Note that mushkil here does not refer to the technical level of textual clarity (the fifth level in the hierarchy of textual categories). Instead, it indicates ambiguity in the nature of the time. The passage says the time resembles both a container and a measure from different perspectives.
The commentary by al-Qamar emphasizes that this is not the istilahi (technical) mushkil.
3
Analyze the two angles of Hajj's time
The first angle: The specified months (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah) are surplus because the actual rites are performed only on a few days, making it a container. However, only one Hajj can be performed in that period, making it a measure. The second angle: Hajj is obligatory once in a lifetime. If one lives many years, the time is expansive (container); if one dies before the second year, it is restrictive (measure). Trace these arguments step by step.
Contrast with salah: one prayer time can host multiple different prayers.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf considered the restrictive aspect (tadyiq) – if you miss the first year, you must perform it then. Muhammad considered the expansive aspect (tawsi') – you can delay to later years. This difference stems from which perspective of the time they emphasize.
The passage does not give a tarjih; both positions are recorded.
5
Evaluate the commentary's critique
The commentary by al-Qamar raises a point: the entire lifetime is the actual time for Hajj, which is surplus, so the measure aspect may be weak. This is a reflection for deeper analysis. Consider whether the time is truly a measure or only appears so due to the limitation of performing Hajj only once in a lifetime.
This critique does not reject the classification but enriches it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو يكون مشكلًا يشبه المعيار والظرف كالحج عطف على ما سبق، وهو النوع الرابع من أنواع المؤقت يعني أو يكون وقت المؤقت مشكلاً أي مشتبه الحال يشبه المعيار من وجه، والظرف من وجه ونظيره وقت الحج، فإنه مشكل بهذا المعنى، وذلك من وجهين: الأول: أن وقت الحج: شوال وذو القعدة وعشرة ذي الحجة، والحج لا يؤدى إلا في بعض عشرة ذي الحجة، فيكون الوقت فاضلاً، فمن هذا الوجه يكون ظرفًا، ومن حيث أنه لا يؤدى في هذا الوقت إلا حج واحد يكون معيارا ، بخلاف الصلاة، فإنه في وقت واحد يؤدى صلاة مختلفة، والثاني: أن الحج لا يفرض في العمر إلا مرة واحدة، فإن أدرك العام الثاني والثالث يكون الوقت موسعًا يؤديه في أي وقت شاء، وإن لم يدرك العام الثاني يكون الوقت مضيقًا لابد له أن يؤدي في العام الأول؛ لكن أبا يوسف له اعتبر جانب التضييق ومحمد محله اعتبر جانب التوسع على ما قال المصنف له. مشكلاً: اسم فاعل من الإشكال بمعنى الاشتباه. (القمر) كالحج التحقيق أن هذا القسم الرابع لا فرد له سوى وقت الحج، فإيراد الكاف نظراً إلى الإمكان الصرف لما عداه. (القمر) على ما سبق: أي على قوله: إما أن يكون الوقت ظرفًا. (القمر) وقت المؤقت إلخ إيماء إلى أن ضمير أو يكون راجع إلى الوقت وجعله راجعا إلى المؤقت كما في "التنوير" لبحر العلوم أي) مولانا عبد العلي لا يخلو عن انتشار، فإن ضمير "يكون" في الجمل السابقة راجع إلى الوقت. (القمر) أي مشتبه إلخ إيماء إلى أنه ليس المراد في كلام المصنف بالمشكل المشكل الاصطلاحي (القمر) وذلك أي إشكال وقت الحج. (القمر) شوال إلخ فلا يحرم ليحج قبل هذه الأشهر، فلو أحرم قبلها كره تحريما. (القمر) يكون معيارا فيه أن العام الواحد بعض وقت الحج والحج هو الواجب العمري، فكل العمر وقته، وهو فاضل، فلا شائبة فيه للمعيارية، وكون بعض الوقت معيارا لا يستلزم كون جميع الوقت معيارا تأمل. (القمر) يكون الوقت مضيقا إلخ سلمنا أن هذا الوقت مضيق لكن لا يلزم منه كون الوقت للحج معيارا، فإن وقت الحج العمر كله وهو فاضل تأمل. (القمر)
Or it may be problematic resembling the measure and the container, like Hajj, as a conjunction to what preceded, and it is the fourth type of time-bound obligations. Meaning, the time of the time-bound may be problematic, i.e., ambiguous, resembling the measure from one aspect and the container from another aspect. Its example is the time of Hajj, for it is problematic in this sense. This is from two angles: First: the time of Hajj is Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah, but Hajj is only performed in part of the ten days, so the time is surplus; from this aspect it is a container. And from the perspective that only one Hajj is performed in this time, it is a measure, contrary to prayer, for in one time different prayers are performed. Second: Hajj is only obligatory once in a lifetime. If he reaches the second and third year, the time is expansive—he may perform it whenever he wishes. If he does not reach the second year, the time is restrictive—he must perform it in the first year. However, according to Abu Yusuf, he considered the aspect of restriction, and according to Muhammad, he considered the aspect of expansion, as the author said for him. 'Mushkilan' is the active participle from ishkal meaning ambiguity. (al-Qamar) Like Hajj: the verification is that this fourth category has no instance other than the time of Hajj, so bringing the 'kaaf' (like) is to indicate the possibility of applying it to others. (al-Qamar) According to what preceded: i.e., based on his statement: either the time is a container... (al-Qamar) The time of the time-bound etc. is an indication that the pronoun in 'or it may be' refers to the time, and making it refer to the time-bound as in 'al-Tanwir' by Bahr al-Ulum (i.e., Mawlana Abd al-Ali) is not free from weakness, for the pronoun in the previous sentences refers to time. (al-Qamar) That is, ambiguous etc. indicates that what is meant by problematic in the author's words is not the technical problematic term. (al-Qamar) That is, the ambiguity of Hajj time. (al-Qamar) Shawwal etc., so it is unlawful to perform Hajj before these months, so if one enters ihram before them, it is makruh tahriman. (al-Qamar) It is a measure in that a single year is part of the Hajj time and Hajj is the lifetime obligation, so the entire lifespan is its time, and it is surplus, so there is no aspect of measure in it, and the fact that some of the time is a measure does not entail that all of the time is a measure, reflect. (al-Qamar) The time is restrictive etc.: we concede that this time is restrictive, but it does not necessarily follow that the time for Hajj is a measure, for the time of Hajj is the entire lifespan and it is surplus, reflect. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage defines the fourth category of muwaqqat: time that is problematic (mushkil), meaning it has aspects of both a container (zarf) and a measure (mi'yar). The sole example is the time of Hajj. Two angles demonstrate its ambiguity: (1) the actual Hajj time (Shawwal through the 10th of Dhu al-Hijjah) is surplus because only a few days are used for the rites, so it resembles a container; however, only one Hajj can be performed in this period, so it also resembles a measure. This contrasts with prayer, where multiple prayers can be performed in a single time. (2) Hajj is obligatory only once in a lifetime; if one lives long enough, the time is expansive, but if not, it is restrictive. The Hanafi imams differ: Abu Yusuf emphasizes the restrictive aspect (tadyiq), while Muhammad emphasizes the expansive aspect (tawsi'). The commentary by al-Qamar clarifies that this category is unique to Hajj, that the term 'mushkil' is not used in the technical usul sense, and critiques the idea that Hajj time is truly a measure by noting that the entire lifespan is the time and it is surplus.

Key Terms
مشكل (mushkil): Problematic or ambiguous, resembling both container and measure
معيار (mi'yar): Measure; a time that is filled by a single act, e.g., only one Hajj in the specified period
ظرف (zarf): Container; a time that is surplus and can accommodate multiple acts or be vacant
وقت الحج (waqt al-hajj): The time for Hajj: Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah
تضييق (tadyiq): Restriction; the view that Hajj time is limited and requires immediate performance
توسعة (tawsi'): Expansion; the view that Hajj time is broad and allows delay

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which Hanafi imam emphasized the restrictive aspect of Hajj time?
A) Abu Hanifa
B) Abu Yusuf
C) Muhammad al-Shaybani
D) Zufar

Key Takeaway
The time for Hajj is problematic (mushkil) because it exhibits both container-like and measure-like features, leading to a legitimate intra-Hanafi difference on whether it is restrictive or expansive.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
