Disbelievers Are Addressed by the Commands of Shariah
Explaining whether disbelievers are addressed by the commands of Shariah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that disbelievers are obligated by the commands of Shariah in faith, worldly punishments, transactions, and Hereafter accountability, and derive this from the Quranic proof in Surah al-Muddathir.

Core Idea
Disbelievers are addressed by the commands of Shariah for faith, punishments, transactions, and are accountable in the Hereafter.

This passage addresses a foundational usul question: Are disbelievers addressed by the legal commands of Shariah? The Hanafi position is clear: they are obligated in multiple domains, from faith to worldly punishments to transactions, and crucially, they are held accountable in the Hereafter for neglecting the obligations of Islam. We will dissect the reasoning and the Quranic proof provided.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central claim
The author states that disbelievers are addressed by the command (al-kuffar mukhaṭabūn bi-l-amr). Identify the three domains in which they are obligated: faith, worldly punishments, and transactions.
The passage also includes accountability in the Hereafter as a separate domain.
2
Distinguish the types of obligation
Break down the four categories: (1) faith (al-iman) – the command to believe is primarily for disbelievers; (2) worldly punishments (al-uqubat) – hudud and qisas apply to them; (3) transactions (al-mu'amalat) – they deal with us in sale, lease, etc., except wine and pork; (4) Hereafter accountability – they are punished for abandoning belief in obligations.
Note the nuance: for believers, the command to faith means firmness; for disbelievers, it is initial obligation.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
The author cites Surah al-Muddathir (74:42-44): 'What led you into Saqar? They said: We were not of those who prayed, nor did we feed the poor.' Understand how this verse proves that disbelievers are punished for neglecting prayer and charity, implying they were commanded to perform them.
This is a dalil naqli (textual evidence) with qati thubut but zanni dalala regarding the exact obligation.
4
Analyze the Hanafi view on hudud
The passage highlights that according to Abu Hanifa, hudud are deterrents (zawajir), not expiations. This strengthens the argument that disbelievers are more deserving of punishments, as the deterrent purpose applies universally.
The Shafi'i view (hudud as expiations) would weaken this point, but the Hanafi position is preferred (al-mukhtar).
5
Synthesize the overall position
Conclude that disbelievers are fully addressed by the commands of Shariah in this world and the next. The jizya ensures their protection in transactions, but their obligations remain.
This rule has practical implications for how Muslims interact with non-Muslims in penal and commercial contexts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم لما فرغ المصنف عن مباحث المطلق والمؤقت شرع في بيان كون الكفار مأمورين بالأمر أو لا، فقال: والكفار مخاطبون بالأمر بالإيمان وبالمشروع من العقوبات بالمعاملات؛ لأن الأمر بالإيمان في الواقع لا يكون إلا للكفار، وأما للمؤمنين كما في قوله تعالى: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا آمِنُوا، فإنما يراد به الثبات على الإيمان، والاستقامة عليه، (النساء: ١٣٦) أو مواطاة القلب للسان أو نحو ذلك، وكذا هم أليق بالعقوبات؛ لأن العقوبات وهي الحدود والقصاص إذا كانت تجري على المسلمين لأجل انتظام العالم، ومصلحة البقاء، والزجر عن المعاصي، فالكفار أولى بهما سيما عند أبي حنيفة بيه؛ لأن الحدود والكفارات عنده زاجرة للناس عن الارتكاب لا ساترة، ومزيلة للمعصية، وأما المعاملات فهي دائرة بيننا وبينهم، فينبغي أن نتعامل معهم حسب ما تعاملنا بيننا في البيع والشراء والإجارة وغيرها سوى الخمر والخنزير فإنهما مباحان لهم لا لنا وإليه أشار عليها بقوله: "الخمر لهم كالخل لنا، والخنزير لهم كالشاة لنا، وإنما بذلوا الجزية ليكون دماؤهم كدمائنا وأموالهم كأموالنا. و بالشرائع في حق المؤاخذة في الآخرة بلا خلاف يعني أن الكفار مخاطبون بالشرائع، وهي الصيام والصلاة والزكاة والحج في حق المؤاخذة في الآخرة باتفاق بيننا وبين الشافعي، فهم يعذبون بترك اعتقاد الفرائض والواجبات كما يعذبون بترك اعتقاد أصل الإيمان؛ لقوله :تعالى مَا سَلَكَكُمْ فِي سَفَرَه قَالُوا لَمْ نَكُ مِنَ الْمُصَلِّينَ ، وَلَمْ نَكُ نُطْعِمُ الْمِسْكِينَ (المدثر : ٤٤٤٢) من العقوبات أي التي تدفع مفاسد الدنيا. (القمر) والمشروع من العقوبات وهي الحدود كحد الزنا وحد السرقة وحد القذف. (القمر) لا ساترة ومزيلة إلخ المشهور في كتب أصولنا: أن الحدود زواجر وعند الشافعية سواتر وكفارات، لكن في البدائع: تصريح بأن الحدود كفارات بعض الكفارة قاله في باب التعزير (السنبلي) وإنما بذلوا الجزية إلخ جواب سؤال مقدر تقريره أن الكفار لما كانوا في المعاملات مثلنا سوى الخمر والخنزير فلم خصوا بالجزية دوننا، فأجاب الشارح بما حاصله أن فائدة الجزية تعود إليهم، حفاظة دمائهم وأموالهم في الدنيا فقط. (السنبلي) في حكم إلى مرتبط بقوله: وبالشرائع. (القمر) بلا خلاف متعلق بقوله: مخاطبون وناظر أي جميع ما تقدم من الأمور الأربعة كذا قيل. (القمر) لقوله تعالى إلخ أورد الآية دليلاً على أنهم مخاطبون بالعبادات في حق المؤاخذة في الآخرة على ما هو المتفق عليه، وقد حقق في موضعه أن محل الاتفاق ليس هو المؤاخذة في الآخرة على ترك الأعمال، بل على ترك اعتقاد الوجوب، فالآية متمسك للقائلين بالوجوب في حق المؤاخذة على ترك الأعمال أيضا، ولذا أجاب عنه الفريق الثاني بأن المراد لم نكن من المعتقدين فرضية الصلاة، فيكون العذاب على ترك الاعتقاد. (السنبلي) ما سلككم إلخ هذه مقولة المسلمين من الكفار يقولون لهم ما أدخلكم في جهنم أيها الكفار. (القمر) لم أجده في كتب الحديث الحاضرة عندي، وهو من قول صاحب "الهداية"، فلعله ظنه الشارح حديثًا. [إشراق الأبصار ۸]
Then when the author finished from discussions of the absolute and the temporally specified, he began to explain whether disbelievers are commanded by the command or not, and he said: The disbelievers are addressed by the command with faith and with what is prescribed from punishments and transactions; because the command to faith in reality is only for disbelievers, and as for believers as in His statement, 'O you who have believed, believe,' it is intended only for firmness in faith and uprightness upon it, or harmony of the heart with the tongue or similar. Likewise, they are more fitting for punishments because punishments, which are hudud and qisas, are carried out on Muslims for the order of the world, benefit of survival, and deterrence from sins, so the disbelievers are more deserving of them especially according to Abu Hanifa; because hudud and expiations with him are deterrents for people from committing acts, not covers, and removers of sin. As for transactions, they circulate between us and them, so we should deal with them as we deal among ourselves in sale, purchase, lease, and other things except wine and pig, for they are permissible for them not for us. And he pointed to it with his saying: 'Wine for them is like vinegar for us, and pig for them is like sheep for us. They only pay jizya so that their blood becomes like our blood and their wealth like our wealth.' And with the laws concerning accountability in the Hereafter without dispute means that the disbelievers are addressed with the laws, which are fasting, prayer, zakat, and hajj concerning accountability in the Hereafter by agreement between us and al-Shafi'i. Thus they are punished for abandoning belief in the obligations and duties just as they are punished for abandoning belief in the core faith due to His statement: 'What led you into Saqar? They said: We were not of those who prayed, nor did we feed the poor.' (al-Muddathir: 42-44).
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on whether disbelievers are addressed by the commands of Shariah. The commentator explains that they are indeed obligated with the command to believe and with the prescribed punishments and transactions. The reasoning is that the command to faith is primarily for disbelievers, as believers are already commanded to firmness. Disbelievers are more deserving of punishments because these serve to deter from sin, and in the Hanafi view, hudud are deterrents (zawajir) rather than expiations (sawatir). The transactions between Muslims and disbelievers are similar, except for wine and pork which are permissible for them. Regarding the Hereafter, there is consensus that disbelievers are accountable for abandoning the pillars of Islam, as evidenced by the Quranic verse where the inhabitants of Hell are questioned about their neglect of prayer and charity. The commentator emphasizes that the agreement is on punishment for abandoning the belief in obligation, not necessarily for the acts themselves.

Key Terms
الكفار مخاطبون بالأمر (al-kuffār mukhāṭabūn bi-l-amr): Disbelievers are addressed by the commands of Shariah, meaning they are obligated to fulfill the commands in terms of belief, penalties, and transactions in this world, and are accountable for abandoning them in the Hereafter.
الحدود (al-ḥudūd): Fixed penalties prescribed by Shariah for specific crimes (e.g., zina, theft, qadhf). They serve as deterrents (zawajir) in the Hanafi view, not expiations.
سقر (saqar): A name for Hell mentioned in Quran 74:42-44. The passage uses this verse as proof that disbelievers are questioned about their neglect of prayer and charity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Hanafi: hudud are expiations; Shafi'i: hudud are deterrents
B) Hanafi: hudud are deterrents; Shafi'i: hudud are expiations
C) Both schools agree hudud are expiations
D) Both schools agree hudud are deterrents

Key Takeaway
Disbelievers are addressed by the commands of Shariah in four domains: faith, worldly punishments, transactions, and Hereafter accountability; the Hanafi view of hudud as deterrents supports their application to disbelievers.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Are Kuffar Obligated to Perform Acts of Worship?
Disputes whether kuffar are addressed by sharia for worldly acts and afterlife punishment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi view from the opposing view on whether kuffar are addressed by sharia commands for worship, and apply the proof of Quran 74:42-44 to each position.

Core Idea
Unbelievers are punished in the Hereafter not for failing to perform acts of worship, but for failing to believe in their obligation.

This lesson explores a key usul dispute: do kuffar fall under the obligation to perform acts of worship like prayer and zakat? The text from Noor al-Anwar examines the proof from Quran 74:42-44 and the different interpretations. We'll see how the Hanafi school, particularly the Bukhara scholars, interprets the verse metaphorically, and why the opposing view (Iraqi Hanafis and Shafi'is) is considered a fallacy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed point
Both Hanafis and Shafi'is agree that kuffar are held accountable in the Hereafter for abandoning belief in the obligations (prayer, zakat, etc.). This is stated as 'bila khilaf'.
The agreement is limited to belief in obligation, not performance.
2
Locate the disputed point
The dispute is whether kuffar are also obligated to perform those acts (ada') in this world. Some Iraqi Hanafis and most Shafi'is affirm this; the Bukhara Hanafis deny it.
The passage calls the opposing view a 'great fallacy'.
3
Follow the opposing proof
The opposing school uses the apparent meaning (zahir) of Quran 74:42-44, where the people of Hell say they did not pray or feed the poor, implying punishment for the act itself.
This is the strongest dalil for the performance obligation view.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response uses ta'wil (metaphorical interpretation): the verse means they did not believe in the obligation. Evidence includes the Meccan context (zakat not yet fard) and inconsistency with Shafi'i's own stance on validity and qada.
The response also notes that the literal reading would imply validity of kuffar's acts, which Shafi'i does not hold.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under the Hanafi view, kuffar are punished only for disbelief in obligation; under the opposing view, they are also punished for non-performance, though qada is not required after Islam.
The Hanafi tarjih is the metaphorical interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

بيان موجب الأمر في حق الكفار
الحدود والقصاص إذا كانت تجري على المسلمين لأجل انتظام العالم، ومصلحة البقاء، والزجر عن المعاصي، فالكفار أولى بهما سيما عند أبي حنيفة بيه؛ لأن الحدود والكفارات عنده زاجرة للناس عن الارتكاب لا ساترة، ومزيلة للمعصية، وأما المعاملات فهي دائرة بيننا وبينهم، فينبغي أن نتعامل معهم حسب ما تعاملنا بيننا في البيع والشراء والإجارة وغيرها سوى الخمر والخنزير فإنهما مباحان لهم لا لنا وإليه أشار عليها بقوله: "الخمر لهم كالخل لنا، والخنزير لهم كالشاة لنا، وإنما بذلوا الجزية ليكون دماؤهم كدمائنا وأموالهم كأموالنا. و بالشرائع في حق المؤاخذة في الآخرة بلا خلاف يعني أن الكفار مخاطبون بالشرائع، وهي الصيام والصلاة والزكاة والحج في حق المؤاخذة في الآخرة باتفاق بيننا وبين الشافعي، فهم يعذبون بترك اعتقاد الفرائض والواجبات كما يعذبون بترك اعتقاد أصل الإيمان؛ لقوله :تعالى مَا سَلَكَكُمْ فِي سَفَرَه قَالُوا لَمْ نَكُ مِنَ الْمُصَلِّينَ ، وَلَمْ نَكُ نُطْعِمُ الْمِسْكِينَ أي العبادات (المدثر : ٤٤٤٢) الحدود كحد الزنا وحد السرقة وحد القذف. (القمر) لا ساترة ومزيلة إلخ المشهور في كتب أصولنا: أن الحدود زواجر وعند الشافعية سواتر وكفارات، لكن في البدائع": تصريح بأن الحدود كفارات بعض الكفارة قاله في باب التعزير (السنبلي) وإنما بذلوا الجزية إلخ جواب سؤال مقدر تقريره أن الكفار لما كانوا في المعاملات مثلنا سوى الخمر والخنزير فلم خصوا بالجزية دوننا، فأجاب الشارح بما حاصله أن فائدة الجزية تعود إليهم، حفاظة دمائهم وأموالهم في الدنيا فقط. (السنبلي) في حكم إلى مرتبط بقوله: وبالشرائع. (القمر) وهي بلا خلاف متعلق بقوله : مخاطبون وناظر أي جميع ما تقدم من الأمور الأربعة كذا قيل. (القمر) لقوله تعالى إلخ أورد الآية دليلاً على أنهم مخاطبون بالعبادات في حق المؤاخذة في الآخرة على ما هو المتفق عليه، وقد حقق في موضعه أن محل الاتفاق ليس هو المؤاخذة في الآخرة على ترك الأعمال، بل على ترك اعتقاد الوجوب، فالآية متمسك للقائلين بالوجوب في حق المؤاخذة على ترك الأعمال أيضا، ولذا أجاب عنه الفريق الثاني بأن المراد لم نكن من المعتقدين فرضية الصلاة، فيكون العذاب على ترك الاعتقاد. (السنبلي) ما سلككم إلخ هذه مقولة المسلمين من الكفار يقولون لهم ما أدخلكم في جهنم أيها الكفار. (القمر) لم أجده في كتب الحديث الحاضرة عندي، وهو من قول صاحب "الهداية"، فلعله ظنه الشارح حديثًا. [إشراق الأبصار ۸]

مبحث الخاص
١٦٧
بيان موجب الأمر في حق الكفار
أي لم نك من المعتقدين للصلاة المفروضة، والزكاة المفروضة هكذا قالوا، وقد فسرته في "التفسير الأحمدي" بأطنب وجه وأشمله.
وأما في وجوب الأداء في أحكام الدنيا فكذلك عند البعض يعني أنهم مخاطبون بأداء العبادات في الدنيا أيضا عند البعض من مشايخ العراق، وأكثر أصحاب الشافعي حبه، وهذه مغلطة عظيمة للقوم؛ لأن الشافعي لم يقل بصحة أدائها منهم حالة الكفر، ولا بوجوب قضائها بعد الإسلام، فما معنى وجوب الأداء في الدنيا، فلذا أوّلوا كلامه بأن معنى الخطاب في حقهم آمنوا ثم صلوا، فيقدر الإيمان مقتضى تبعًا للعبادات، وثمرته أنهم يؤاخذون عنده في الآخرة بترك فعل الصلاة كما يعذبون بترك اعتقادها اتفاقا، فلو لم يكونوا مخاطبين بأداء العبادات أي لم نك إلخ فيه أن هذا المعنى مجازي، والمجاز لا يثبت إلا بدليل، وأما ظاهر الآية فيدل على أن الكفار يعذبون بترك فعل الصلاة والزكاة فهو حجة للشافعي لله ومشايخ العراق، وقال بحر العلوم إن التأويل بالصلاة الواجبة والزكاة الواجبة بعيد، فإن الآية مكية، والزكاة إنما فرضت بالمدينة وما سواها من الإطعام مندوب، فكيف ينتهض سببًا لسلوك النار بل سبب سلوكهم كونهم كافرين وبينوا كفرهم بالكناية أي ذكر لوازمه وأماراته، والمعنى والله أعلم. ما تسألون عن سلوكنا النار مع أنه لم يكن فبينا علامة من علامات المؤمنين من الصلاة والإطعام بل علامات الكفار، والخوض معهم، وتكذيب يوم الدين، إلا أن يثبت وجوب صدقة ما سوى الزكاة قبل الهجرة فحينئذ يكون لهذا الاستدلال وجه. (القمر) وقد فسرته إلخ ليس في التفسير "الأحمدي" أمر زائد في هذا المبحث على ما في هذا الشرح، ولذا ما نقلت عبارته . (القمر) وأكثر أصحاب الشافعي والشافعي كذا قال ابن الملك. (القمر) أدائها إلخ ضميره وكذا ضمير قضائها راجع إلى العبادات (القمر) كلامه: أي كلام الشافعي وهو مخاطبون بأداء العبادات في الدنيا. (القمر) فيقدر إلخ لا يقال: إن الإيمان رأس الطاعات، فكيف يثبت وجوبه تبعًا للعبادات؛ لأنا نقول : إن وجوب الإيمان ثابت بالأوامر المستقلة فهو ثابت عبارة واقتضاء ولا محذور فيه، إنما المحذور لو لم يكن ثبوته عبارة (القمر) مقتضى إلخ فإن الإيمان شرط لأداء جميع العبادات، وهذا كما أن الجنب يجب عليه الصلاة بشرط الطهارة، فكذا يجب على الكفار العبادات بشرط الإيمان. (القمر) ومرته أي ثمرة وجوب العبادات أداء على الكفار عند الشافعي له (القمر) عنده أي عند الشافعي، وكذا عند أن الكفار مشايخ العراق، وأما عند مشايخ بخارا فهم يعذبون بترك اعتقاد وجوب العبادات لا بترك أداء العبادات. (القمر)
Section of the Specific [al-Khas] 177. Explanation of the implication of the command with respect to unbelievers. Hudud and qisas, if they are executed upon Muslims for the sake of world order, the benefit of survival, and deterrence from sins, then the unbelievers are more entitled to them, especially according to Abu Hanifa, because hudud and expiations according to him are deterrents for people from committing [sins], not covering [sins], and they remove sin. As for transactions, they are conducted between us and them, so we should deal with them as we deal among ourselves in buying, selling, leasing, and other things, except wine and swine, for they are permissible to them but not to us. And the author pointed to this by his saying: 'Wine is to them as vinegar is to us, and swine is to them as sheep is to us. And they only pay jizya so that their blood is like our blood and their wealth is like our wealth.' And by the sharia rulings regarding accountability in the Hereafter, without disagreement, meaning that unbelievers are addressed by the sharia rulings, which are fasting, prayer, zakat, and hajj, regarding accountability in the Hereafter, by agreement between us and al-Shafi'i. So they are punished for abandoning belief in the obligations and duties just as they are punished for abandoning belief in the foundation of faith, due to His statement, the Exalted: 'What led you into Saqar?' They said: 'We were not of those who prayed, nor did we feed the poor' i.e., the acts of worship. (Al-Muddaththir 74:42-44). Hudud like the hadd of adultery, hadd of theft, hadd of slander. (al-Qamar: 'not covering and removing etc.' The well-known in our books of usul is that hudud are deterrents, and according to the Shafi'is they are coverings and expiations, but in al-Bada'i' there is an explicit statement that hudud are expiations, some of the expiation, he said it in the chapter of ta'zir. (al-Sunbuli: 'And they only pay jizya etc.' is an answer to an implied question: since the unbelievers are like us in transactions except wine and swine, why are they singled out for jizya without us? The commentator answered that the benefit of jizya returns to them, preserving their blood and wealth only in this world. (al-Sunbuli: 'in the ruling to' connected to his saying: 'and by the sharia rulings.' (al-Qamar: 'and they are' 'without disagreement' is attached to his saying: 'addressed' and it means all the four matters mentioned, thus it is said. (al-Qamar: 'due to His statement etc.' He adduced the verse as proof that they are addressed by acts of worship regarding accountability in the Hereafter, as is agreed upon. And it was verified in its place that the point of agreement is not accountability in the Hereafter for abandoning deeds, but for abandoning belief in obligation. So the verse is a support for those who hold obligation regarding accountability for abandoning deeds also. Therefore, the second group answered that what is meant is 'we were not among those who believed in the obligation of prayer', so the punishment is for abandoning belief. (al-Sunbuli: 'What led you etc.' This is the speech of Muslims to the unbelievers, they say to them: What made you enter Hell, O unbelievers? (al-Qamar: 'I did not find it in the books of hadith present with me, and it is from the statement of the author of al-Hidaya, perhaps the commentator thought it was a hadith. [Ishraq al-Absar 8] [Page 168] Section of the Specific 167. Explanation of the implication of the command with respect to unbelievers. That is, we were not among those who believed in the obligatory prayer and the obligatory zakat. Thus they said, and I have interpreted it in al-Tafsir al-Ahmadi in the most extensive and comprehensive manner. As for the obligation of performance in the rulings of this world, it is likewise according to some, meaning that they are addressed with the performance of acts of worship in this world also, according to some of the Iraqi shaykhs and most of al-Shafi'i's companions. And this is a great fallacy to the people, because al-Shafi'i did not say that their performance is valid in a state of disbelief, nor did he say that they must make up for it after Islam. So what is the meaning of obligation of performance in this world? Therefore, they interpreted his statement to mean that the address to them is 'Believe, then pray', so faith is implied as a prerequisite following the acts of worship, and its result is that they are held accountable in the Hereafter for abandoning the act of prayer just as they are punished for abandoning belief in it, by agreement. For if they were not addressed with the performance of acts of worship … (the text continues with commentary).
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage is a classic usul dispute regarding whether non-believers (kuffar) are addressed by the sharia rulings (mukhattabun) for both worldly performance and afterlife accountability. The author, commenting on the matn of Noor al-Anwar, explains that there is consensus (ijma) between Hanafis and Shafi'is that kuffar are accountable in the Hereafter for failing to believe in the obligations (fara'id) like prayer and zakat. The proof is the Quranic verse (74:42-44) where the inhabitants of Hell are asked why they entered, and they reply that they were not of those who prayed nor fed the poor. The Hanafi position, as represented by Abu Hanifa, distinguishes between hudud/qisas (which apply to kuffar as deterrents) and acts of worship. For worship, the disagreement is about whether kuffar are obligated to perform them in this world (adā' fī al-dunyā). Some Iraqi Hanafi scholars and most Shafi'is hold that they are obligated, but the commentator rejects this as a fallacy (maghlata). He argues that Shafi'i himself did not consider their acts valid while in kufr, nor require qada after embracing Islam. The commentator concludes that the correct Hanafi view (of the Bukhara scholars) is that kuffar are punished in the Hereafter only for abandoning belief in obligation, not for failing to perform the acts. The verse is interpreted metaphorically: 'we were not of those who prayed' means 'we were not believers in the obligation of prayer'. The commentary also addresses a subtle point about the Meccan revelation of the verse — zakat was only made obligatory in Medina, so the verse's mention of feeding the poor might be recommended (mandub) rather than obligatory, which weakens the evidence for performance obligation.

Key Terms
الخاص (al-khas): The specific; a term in usul al-fiqh meaning a word that indicates a specific individual or group, as opposed to 'amm (general). Here it refers to the section discussing rulings specific to kuffar.
موجب الأمر (muwijib al-amr): The implication or requirement of a command; what the command necessitates in terms of obligation upon those addressed.
الكفار (al-kuffar): Non-believers; those who reject the faith of Islam. In this context, the discussion is whether they are addressed (mukhattabun) by the sharia rulings for acts of worship and worldly penalties.
المؤاخذة (al-mu'akhadha): Accountability; being held responsible and punished for failing to fulfill obligations. Here it refers to punishment in the Hereafter for not believing in or performing acts of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi Bukhara position, what is the reason kuffar are punished in the Hereafter regarding acts of worship?
A) For not performing the acts of worship themselves.
B) For not believing that those acts are obligatory.
C) For not paying jizya.
D) For not accepting the prophethood of Muhammad.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, kuffar are addressed by sharia regarding accountability in the Hereafter only for belief in obligation, not for worldly performance of acts of worship.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
beginner

Definition of Nahi and Its Implications
Definition of nahi and its relation to amr, including implication of ugliness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define nahi (prohibition) in Hanafi usul, identify its components, and explain its implication of ugliness (qubh).

Core Idea
Nahi is a demand to cease, placed for tahrim, and it reveals the innate ugliness of the act.

Having completed the examination of amr (command), the author now turns to its counterpart: nahi (prohibition). Like amr, nahi is a category of khass (specific) speech, defaulting to a legal ruling—here, tahrim (prohibition). But nahi carries a distinctive feature: it implies the ugliness (qubh) of the act it prohibits. This lesson unpacks the definition of nahi and its core characteristics, setting the foundation for how prohibitions function in Hanafi legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition's core components
The author defines nahi as 'قول القائل لغيره على سبيل الاستعلاء لا تفعل'. Break this into: speaker (قائل), addressee (غير), mode (استعلاء), and content (لا تفعل). Note that 'لا تفعل' represents any form demanding cessation.
The definition parallels that of amr, replacing 'افعل' with 'لا تفعل'.
2
Understand nahi as a type of khass
The passage states that nahi like amr is from al-khass (the specific). This means the word 'نهي' is a specific term placed for a specific meaning—tahrim. It is not a general term; it has a dedicated legal connotation.
In Hanafi usul, khass texts are definitive in their indication unless overridden.
3
Analyze the implication of ugliness (qubh)
The passage asserts that nahi necessitates (يقتضي) the attribute of qubh in the prohibited act. Importantly, the prohibition does not create ugliness; it reveals an inherent ugliness that the Wise (al-Hakim) only prohibits what is evil (فحشاء) and abominable (منكر).
This is a key theological point: ugliness is intrinsic, not arbitrary.
4
Recognize the scope of the definition
The author addresses a potential objection: the definition seems limited to the second person imperative ('لا تفعل'), but it actually covers all forms expressing a demand to abstain—including absent, speaker, passive, etc. The phrase 'لا تفعل' is a representative of the category.
Thus 'اضرب' with a negative particle also qualifies as nahi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بحث النهي ولما فرغ المصنف عن مباحث الأمر شرع في مباحث النهي، فقال: ومنه النهي وهو قول القائل لغيره على سبيل الاستعلاء "لا تفعل" يعني أن النهي الخاص كالأمر في كونه من الخاص؛ لأنه لفظ وضع لمعنى معلوم، وهو التحريم وباقي القيودات كما مضى في الأمر، غير أنه أي الألفاظ وضع قوله لا تفعل مكان قوله: "إفعل" وهو يشمل المخاطب والغائب والمتكلم، والمعروف والمجهول، وأنه يقتضي صفة القبح للمنهي عنه ضرورة حكمة الناهي، والحكيم إنما ينهى عن الفحشاء والمنكر كما أن الحسن في جانب الأمر كذلك، ثم أن في النهي تقسيما بحسب أقسام القبح. مقتضى للأمر كما مر النهي: وهو في اللغة: المنع. [فتح الغفار: ۹۳] النهي: أي ما صدق عليه النهي من الصيغ كلا تضرب وأمثاله، فإن من الخاص مسمى النهي لا لفظ النهي . (القمر) لا تفعل وما في "التحرير" أولى، وهو لا تفعل استعلاء حتمًا. [فتح الغفار: ٩٤] وهو التحريم وقد يستعمل للنهي مجازاً لغير التحريم كالإرشاد نحو قوله تعالى: ولا تسألوا عَنْ أَشْيَاء إِنْ تُبْدَ لَكُمْ تَسُؤْكُمْ (المائدة: ١٠١)، والدعاء نحو: لا تكلني إلى نفسي.(القمر) كما مضى إلخ فالقول مصدر يراد به المقول، فإن مسمى النهي لفظ فلا يحمل عليه القول المصدري، والمراد بالغير أعم من أن يكون غيراً حقيقة أو اعتبارًا كما في نهي المتكلم نفسه، وهذا بحسب اللغة، وأما عند الأصوليين نهيا، فالمراد بالغير عندهم الغير الحقيقي، والمراد بالاستعلاء: أنه يعد المتكلم نفسه عاليا، سواء كان فهو لا يسمى عاليا في الواقع، أو لا. (القمر) وهو يشمل إلخ: دفع دخل مقدر، وهو: أن التعريف غير جامع لعدم شموله للنهي الغائب والمتكلم معروفًا كان أو مجهولاً؛ إذ ليس فيها لا تفعل وحاصل الدفع أن المراد بقوله: "لا" تفعل كل ما كان دالاً على طلب الكف من مبدأ الاشتقاق على سبيل الحتم فقوله لا تفعل يشمل إلخ. (القمر) وأنه إلخ يعني أن النهي يقتضى صفة القبح للمنهي عنه بمعنى أن ذلك الفعل المنهي عنه قبيح في نفس الأمر، وتعلق النهي به بين قبحه، فالله تعالى نهى عن الشيء؛ لكونه قبيحا، فكأنه قال: هذا الشيء قبيح فلا تفعلوه، وليس أن النهي يثبت القبح ويوجبه ولذا لم يقل المصنف : وإنه يثبت صفة إلخ (القمر)
Section on Prohibition: When the author finished the discussions of command, he began the discussions of prohibition. He said: Among them is prohibition, which is the statement of a speaker to another in a position of superiority: 'Do not do'. This means that the specific prohibition, like the command, is from the specific; because it is a word placed for a known meaning, which is prohibition (tahrim) and the remaining restrictions as mentioned in command. Except that the wording 'Do not do' is placed in the place of 'Do'. It includes the addressee, the absent, the speaker, the known, and the unknown. And that it implies the attribute of ugliness for the prohibited thing by necessity of the wisdom of the prohibitor. The wise one only prohibits evil and abomination just as goodness is on the side of command. Then there is a division in prohibition according to the divisions of ugliness. (Commentary)...
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage is a definition and exposition of 'nahi' (prohibition). The author defines nahi as a statement from a superior to an inferior demanding cessation. It parallels the definition of amr (command) but with the opposite wording ('do not do' instead of 'do'). The passage clarifies that nahi applies to all grammatical persons and forms, not just the second person imperative. A key point is that nahi implies the ugliness (qubh) of the prohibited act; the prohibition does not create the ugliness but reveals it. The commentary also addresses potential objections, such as the definition excluding prohibitions directed to oneself or absent parties, and explains that the term 'لا تفعل' is a representative of all forms expressing a demand to abstain.

Key Terms
النهي (an-nahi): A verbal demand to cease an action, issued from a superior to an inferior, implying the act's ugliness.
الاستعلاء (al-isti'la'): The speaker considering himself in a superior position, regardless of actual status.
القبح (al-qubh): Innate ugliness of an act, which the prohibition reveals but does not create.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the default legal implication of a definitive nahi?
A) Karahah (dislike)
B) Tahrim (prohibition)
C) Ibahah (permissibility)
D) Nadb (recommendation)

Key Takeaway
Nahi is a specific (khass) demand to cease, defaulting to tahrim, and it reveals but does not create the ugliness of the prohibited act.

The Four Types of Ugliness in Prohibited Acts
Classification of the ugliness of prohibited acts into four types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any prohibited act into one of the four categories of ugliness (qabih li-aynihi or li-ghayrihi, subdivided by convention/law or description/adjacent) and explain the basis for each category.

Core Idea
The ugliness of a prohibited act is either intrinsic or extrinsic, and further qualified by its epistemic source (reason or revelation) and ontological permanence (inseparable or adjacent).

In Hanafi usul, not all prohibitions are equal; the nature of the ugliness (qubh) of the prohibited act affects how we understand its obligation of avoidance. This passage from Nur al-Anwar presents a four-fold classification of qubh, dividing it into intrinsic and extrinsic, and then subdividing each by whether the ugliness is known through reason or revelation, and whether it is a permanent attribute or a circumstantial one. Mastering this classification is key to understanding the different levels of prohibition and their legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two primary categories
Identify whether the ugliness is inherent to the act itself (li-aynihi) or caused by an external factor (li-ghayrihi). This determines if the prohibition attaches to the essence of the act or to an accompanying circumstance.
Acts ugly in themselves are always prohibited; acts ugly due to something else may be permissible under different conditions.
2
Subdivide the first category into wad'an and shar'an
For acts ugly in themselves, determine if the ugliness is recognized by reason independent of revelation (wad'an) or known only through revelation (shar'an).
Wad'an ugliness is rationally discernible; shar'an ugliness is solely based on divine command.
3
Subdivide the second category into wasfan and mujawiran
For acts ugly due to something else, decide if the ugliness is an inseparable attribute of the act (wasfan) or a separable, occasional circumstance (mujawiran).
Wasfan ugliness is intrinsic to the act's description; mujawiran ugliness is contingent on external factors.
4
Apply to the given examples
Classify each example from the passage: kufr (qabih li-aynihi wad'an), selling a free person (qabih li-aynihi shar'an), fasting on the day of sacrifice (qabih li-ghayrihi wasfan), selling during the call to prayer (qabih li-ghayrihi mujawiran).
These examples illustrate the full spectrum of the classification.

بيان أقسام القبح أنه إما قبيح لعينه أو لغيره، وكل منهما نوعان، فصار المجموع أربعة على ما بينه تقسيم القبح المصنف بقوله : وهو أي المنهى المفهوم من النهي. إما أن يكون قبيحًا لعينه، أي تكون ذاته قبيحة بقطع النظر عن الأوصاف اللازمة، والعوارض المجاورة. وذلك نوعان : وضعًا وشرعاً أي الأول من حيث إنه وضع للقبيح العقلي بقطع النظر القبيح لعينه قبحه عن ورود الشرع والثاني : من حيث إن الشرع ورد بهذا، وإلا فالعقل يجوزه أو لغيره، عطف على قوله: لعينه. وذلك نوعان: وصفًا ومحاوراً، يعني أن النوع الأول ما يكون القبيح وصفًا للمنهي عنه أي لازمًا غير منفك عنه كالوصف والنوع الثاني ما يكون القبيح فيه مجاوراً للمنهي عنه في بعض الأحيان، ومنفكًا عنه في بعض آخر. كالكفر، وبيع الحر، وصوم يوم النحر، والبيع وقت النداء أمثلة للأنواع الأربعة على ترتيب أي الغير المفهوم إلخ هذا تسامح من الشارح، وتبعه صاحب مسير" الدائر"، فإن المنهي عنه مذكور صراحةً قريبا، فلا حاجة إلى جعل المرجع مذكورًا بعدم الصراحة، ثم اعلم أنه إنما اختار الشارح رجوع الضمير إلى المنهي عنه، لا إلى القبح رعايةً للأمثلة الآتية من قوله كالكفر إلخ، فإن هذه الأمور منهية عنها. (القمر) للقبيح العقلي: أي للمعنى القبيح الذي يمكن للعقل درك قبحه بقطع النظر عن ورود الشرع، وإن كان الشرع كشف عن قبحه أيضًا. (القمر) وإلا فالعقل إلخ : يعني أن العقل قاصر عن إدراك قبحه لكن الشارع كشف عن قبحه. (القمر) أو لغيره: أي يكون القبح للغير، ولقبحه يكون هذا المنهي عنه قبيحًا. (القمر) وذلك إلخ: أي القبيح لغيره نوعان بحسب انقسام الغير إلى الوصف والمجاور. (القمر) لازمًا إلخ إيماء إلى أنه ليس المراد بكون الغير وصفا للمنهي عنه أن يكون قائماً به حالاً ،فيه وإلا لم يكن الإعراض عن ضيافة الله تعالى وصفًا لصوم يوم النحر، بل المراد به: يكون الغير لازما له غير منفك عنه لا يتصور وجوده بدونه كما هو شأن الوصف الغير المجاور. (القمر) أن
Statement of the divisions of ugliness: That it is either ugly in itself or due to something else. Each of these has two types, so the total becomes four as explained by the author's division. He said: 'It' meaning the prohibited thing understood from the prohibition, either is ugly in itself, i.e., its essence is ugly disregarding necessary attributes and adjacent accidents. That has two types: convention and law. The first is that it is placed for the rationally ugly disregarding revelation; the second is that revelation has come with this, otherwise reason would permit it. Or due to something else, conjunction to his statement 'in itself'. That has two types: description and adjacent. Meaning the first type is that the ugliness is a description of the prohibited thing, i.e., inseparable like a description; the second type is that the ugliness is adjacent to the prohibited thing at times and separate from it at other times. Examples: kufr, selling a free person, fasting on the day of sacrifice, and selling during the call to prayer. These are examples of the four types in order. (Commentary)...
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage presents a classification of the ugliness (qubh) of prohibited acts according to Hanafi usul. The prohibited act can be ugly in itself (qabih li-aynihi) or due to something external (qabih li-ghayrihi). The former is subdivided into: (1) conventionally ugly (wad'an) – acts whose ugliness is recognized by reason independent of revelation, and (2) legally ugly (shar'an) – acts whose ugliness is known only through revelation, though reason might not deem them ugly. The latter is subdivided into: (1) descriptively ugly (wasfan) – where the ugliness is an inseparable attribute of the act, and (2) adjacent ugly (mujawiran) – where the ugliness is separable and only occurs occasionally. Examples given: kufr (ugly in itself, conventionally), selling a free person (ugly in itself, legally, as the act is not inherently evil but prohibited by sharia), fasting on the day of Eid al-Adha (ugly due to something else, descriptively, because the prohibition is inherent to the day), and selling at the time of the Friday call to prayer (ugly due to something else, adjacently, as the transaction itself is not ugly but due to the timing).

Key Terms
القبيح لعينه (al-qabih li-aynihi): Act whose essence is inherently ugly, irrespective of external factors.
القبيح لغيره (al-qabih li-ghayrihi): Act that is not intrinsically ugly but becomes ugly due to an external circumstance.
وضعاً (wad'an): Ugliness established by convention or rational discernment prior to revelation.
شرعاً (shar'an): Ugliness established solely by revelation; reason does not independently deem it ugly.
قبيح وصفاً (qabih wasfan): Ugliness that is an inseparable attribute of the act; the act cannot exist without this ugliness.
قبيح مجاوراً (qabih mujawiran): Ugliness that is an adjacent circumstance, separable from the act; the act can exist without it at other times.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of 'qabih li-ghayrihi wasfan' according to the passage?
A) Kufr
B) Selling a free person
C) Fasting on the day of sacrifice
D) Selling during the Friday call to prayer

Key Takeaway
The classification of ugliness into four types helps us understand the nature of prohibitions: whether they are intrinsic or extrinsic, rationally or legally known, and inseparable or adjacent.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Classification of Prohibited Acts (Qabih) into Intrinsic and Extrinsic
Explains the four-fold division of qabih (prohibited) in Hanafi usul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four categories of qabih in Hanafi usul and classify any prohibited act into its appropriate category by analyzing its cause.

Core Idea
Qabih is either inherently ugly or ugly due to an external factor; each is further divided by source or inseparability.

In Hanafi legal theory, understanding why an act is prohibited is essential for determining its legal effect and the possibility of abrogation or exceptional circumstances. This passage from Noor al-Anwar provides a precise classification of prohibitions based on their cause. By mastering this taxonomy, you will be able to analyze any prohibited act in terms of its intrinsic or extrinsic ugliness and apply the correct legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching division
The author divides qabih into two primary categories: ugly in itself (li-‘aynihi) and ugly due to something else (li-ghayrihi). Note that 'ugly' here means prohibited.
This division is based on the cause of prohibition: whether the act itself is inherently repugnant or becomes so due to an external factor.
2
Distinguish subcategories of intrinsic ugliness
Intrinsic ugliness is further divided into linguistic convention (wad‘an) – where the act is coined for a rationally repugnant meaning – and by revelation (shar‘an) – where the act is prohibited by divine law even though reason alone might not deem it ugly.
Disbelief (kufr) is the example for wad‘an; selling a free person is the example for shar‘an.
3
Distinguish subcategories of extrinsic ugliness
Extrinsic ugliness is divided into by description (wasfan) – where the external factor is inseparable from the act – and by adjacency (mujāwiran) – where the external factor is occasional and separable.
Fasting on the day of Sacrifice is wasfan; selling during the Friday call to prayer is mujāwiran.
4
Apply the classification to examples
Work through each example given in the passage: kufr (intrinsic by convention), bay‘ al-hurr (intrinsic by revelation), sawm yawm al-nahr (extrinsic by description), bay‘ waqt al-nida’ (extrinsic by adjacency). Justify each using the definitions.
The passage emphasizes that kufr cannot be abrogated, while extrinsic prohibitions may be lifted when the external factor is removed.
5
Analyze legal consequences
Consider the implications: acts in the first category (especially wad‘an) are universally and permanently prohibited; acts in the second category may be subject to exceptions (e.g., necessity) or abrogation. Identify the key factor that determines this.
The distinction between intrinsic and extrinsic is crucial for determining when a prohibition can be overridden.

اللف والنشر، فالكفر مثال لما قبح لعينه وضعًا؛ لأنه وضع لمعنى: هو قبيح في أصل وضعه، والعقل مما يحرمه لو لما يرد عليه الشرع؛ لأن قبح كفران المنعم مركوز في العقول السليمة. وبيع الحر: مثال لم قَبحَ لعينه شرعًا؛ لأن البيع لم يوضع في اللغة لمعنى هو قبيح عقلاً، وإنما القبح فيه لأجل أن الشرع فسر البيع بمبادلة مال بمال والحر ليس بمال عنده. وكذا صلاة المحدث قبيحة شرعًا؛ لأن الشارع أخرج المحدث من أن يكون أهلاً لأدائها. وصوم يوم النحر : مثال لما قَبحَ لغيره وصفًا، فإن الصوم في نفسه عبادة وإمساك الله تعالى.

Section on the Specific [Topic]. Explanation of the divisions of ugliness (prohibition). That it is either ugly in itself or due to something else, and each of the two has two types, so the total becomes four as the author explained in the division of ugliness by his statement: 'That is, the prohibited thing understood from the prohibition. Either it is ugly in itself, i.e., its essence is ugly regardless of necessary attributes and adjacent accidents.' And that is two types: by convention and by law, i.e., the first [is ugly] in that it is coined for the intellectually ugly regardless of revealed law, and the second in that revelation has come with it, otherwise the intellect would permit it. Or due to something else, coordinate to his statement 'in itself'. And that is two types: by description and by adjacency, meaning the first type is that in which the ugliness is a description of the prohibited thing, i.e., inseparable from it like a description, and the second type is that in which the ugliness is adjacent to the prohibited thing at some times and separable from it at other times. Like disbelief, sale of a free person, fasting on the day of Sacrifice, and sale at the time of the call [to Friday prayer] are examples for the four types in order. ... So disbelief is an example of what is ugly in itself by convention, because it was coined for a meaning that is ugly in its original coinage, and the intellect would prohibit it even if revelation had not come upon it, because the ugliness of ingratitude to the Benefactor is ingrained in sound intellects. Sale of a free person is an example of what is ugly in itself by law, because sale was not coined in language for a meaning that is intellectually ugly; rather the ugliness in it is because revelation interpreted sale as exchange of property for property, and a free person is not property according to it. Likewise, the prayer of one in a state of ritual impurity is ugly by law, because the lawgiver removed the one in impurity from being qualified to perform it. Fasting on the day of Sacrifice is an example of what is ugly due to something else by description, for fasting in itself is worship and abstaining [for the sake of] God Almighty. ...
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage from Noor al-Anwar is a detailed exposition of the classification of prohibited acts (qabih) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author divides qabih into four categories: (1) ugly in itself by linguistic convention (like disbelief and futile actions), (2) ugly in itself by revealed law (like selling a free person or praying without wudu), (3) ugly due to something else by description (like fasting on the day of Sacrifice), and (4) ugly due to something else by adjacency (like selling during the Friday call to prayer). The commentary explains that 'in itself' means the act's essence is inherently repugnant, while 'due to something else' means the act is bad because of an external factor. The subcategories 'by convention' refer to ugliness recognizable by reason alone, and 'by law' refers to ugliness known only through revelation. 'By description' means the external factor is inseparable from the act, like the day of Sacrifice being a time of feasting, making fasting inappropriate. 'By adjacency' means the ugliness is occasional and separable, like selling during the call to prayer. The passage clarifies that disbelief is inherently evil and cannot be abrogated, while selling a free person is prohibited because the free person is not considered property in Islamic law, except under necessity where the free person may be sold to fulfill a debt. The prayer of an impure person is invalid because purity is a condition of validity. These distinctions help jurists understand the nature of prohibitions and the possibility of abrogation or exceptional circumstances.

Key Terms
القبيح (al-qabīḥ): That which is prohibited (al-munha 'anhu), divided into intrinsic (li-‘aynihi) and extrinsic (li-ghayrihi) ugliness.
لعينه (li-‘aynihi): Ugliness inherent in the act itself, regardless of external factors; further divided into wad‘an (by linguistic convention) and shar‘an (by revelation).
لغيره (li-ghayrihi): Ugliness due to an external factor, either wasfan (descriptive/inseparable) or mujāwiran (adjacent/separable).
وضعاً (waḍ‘an): Ugliness recognized by rational judgment without revelation; the act is linguistically coined for a repugnant meaning.
شرعاً (shar‘an): Ugliness established only by revelation; reason alone would not deem it repugnant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of 'qabih li-‘aynihi shar‘an' (ugly in itself by revelation)?
A) Disbelief (kufr)
B) Selling a free person
C) Fasting on the day of Sacrifice
D) Selling during the Friday call to prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of qabih distinguishes between acts inherently prohibited and those prohibited due to external factors, which determines the possibility of abrogation and exceptional permissibility.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Three Types of Qubh (Prohibition/Evil) in Hanafi Usul
Classification of ugliness into three types in Hanafi usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any act into one of the three types of qubh (qabih li 'aynihi wad'an, qabih li 'aynihi shar'an, qabih li ghayrihi wasfan) and explain the legal consequences of each.

Core Idea
Prohibition is not monolithic: three types of qubh determine abrogability, validity, and make-up obligations.

This lesson introduces a foundational Hanafi usul classification of legal 'ugliness' (qubh). The text divides prohibits into three categories: intrinsic by linguistic placement, intrinsic by Shariah, and extrinsic by description. Understanding this taxonomy reveals why some prohibitions are immutable, while others are conditional or subject to change, and why some acts become invalid without requiring completion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Read the passage and note the three types of qubh: qabih li 'aynihi wad'an, qabih li 'aynihi shar'an, and qabih li ghayrihi wasfan. Observe the examples given for each.
The examples are: kufr (disbelief) for the first, selling a free person and prayer without wudu for the second, and fasting on the Day of Nahr for the third.
2
Analyze the basis of ugliness for each type
For each type, determine whether the evil is inherent in the act's linguistic meaning (type 1), defined solely by Shariah (type 2), or arises from a contingent attribute like time (type 3).
Type 1: evil is rationally recognized even without revelation. Type 2: evil exists only because the Lawgiver defined it as such. Type 3: the act itself is good, but a description (e.g., being on a day of hospitality) makes it ugly.
3
Understand legal consequences
For each type, determine the legal effects: type 1 cannot be abrogated; type 2 can be abrogated; type 3 results in invalidity without obligation to complete the act and no make-up required.
The passage discusses the differences regarding vows and prayer in disliked times to illustrate consequences.
4
Apply the classification to new scenarios
Using the criteria from the passage, classify other acts not mentioned (e.g., lying, invalid sale, prayer at sunrise) and justify your classification.
Focus on whether the ugliness is intrinsic or contingent.

اللف والنشر، فالكفر مثال لما قبح لعينه وضعًا؛ لأنه وضع لمعنى: هو قبيح في أصل وضعه، والعقل مما يحرمه لو لم يرد عليه الشرع؛ لأن قبح كفران المنعم مركوز في العقول السليمة. وبيع الحر: مثال لما قبح لعينه شرعًا؛ لأن البيع لم يوضع في اللغة لمعنى هو قبيح عقلاً، وإنما القبح فيه لأجل أن الشرع فسر البيع بمبادلة مال بمال والحر ليس بمال عنده. وكذا صلاة المحدث قبيحة شرعًا؛ لأن الشارع أخرج المحدث من أن يكون أهلاً لأدائها. وصوم يوم النحر: مثال لما قبح لغيره وصفًا، فإن الصوم في نفسه عبادة وإمساك عن المفطرات، وإنما يحرم لأجل أن يوم النحر يوم ضيافة الله تعالى، وفي الصوم إعراض عنها، وهذا المعنى لازم بمنزلة الوصف لهذا الصوم؛ لأن الوقت داخل في تعريف الصوم، ووصف الجزء وصف الكل، فصار فاسدًا، ولا يلزم بالشروع بخلاف النذر فإنه في نفسه طاعة، ولا فساد في التسمية، وإنما الفساد في الفعل، فيجب قضاؤه، وبخلاف الصلاة في الأوقات المكروهة فإنها وإن كانت من هذا القسم أيضًا لكن الوقت ينفك عن الصلاة. (القمر) وكذا صلاة المحدث الخ: قلت: وكذا بيع المضامين والملاقيح، فإن الصلاة حسنة في نفسها، لكن الشرع قصر أهليتها على حال الطهارة، فصلاة العبد مع الحدث عبث نحو كلام الطائر والمجنون. (السنبلي) بمال، لهذا صار بيع الحر قبيحًا شرعًا. (القمر) فإن الصوم إلخ: تقريره أن الصوم هو الإمساك عن المفطرات الثلاث من الصبح إلى الغروب مع النية، وهو في نفسه حسن، إلا أنه يحرم صوم يوم النحر لأجل الإعراض عن ضيافة الله تعالى وهذا المعنى أي الإعراض عن ضيافة الله تعالى بمنزلة الوصف لصوم يوم النحر، لأن هذا المعنى أي الإعراض عن الضيافة اتصل وصفًا بالوقت الذي هو محل أداء الصوم، وهو يوم عيد وضيافة والوقت داخل في تعريف الصوم وجزءًا له، ووصف الجزء وصف الكل، فصار فاسدًا، ولا يلزم بالشروع، فلا يجب إتمامه، بل يجب رفضه وإن رفضه لا يجب القضاء عليه، والسرّ أن وجوب الإتمام يكون لصيانة القدر المؤدى وهي ليست بواجبة لاشتمالها على الأمر القبيح. (القمر) داخل في تعريف الصوم: لأن الصوم عبارة عن الإمساك من الصبح إلى الغروب. (السنبلي) ووصف الجزء الخ: فإذا كان الجزء أي الوقت وهو ههنا يوم النحر موصوفًا بالقبح والنقص فبكون الكل أي الصوم أيضا موصوفًا به كما لا يخفى. (السنبلي) بخلاف النذر إلخ بأن قال: "الله على أن أصوم غدا" وكان الغد يوم النحر، وأما لو صرح بذكر المنهي عنه بأن يقول: " الله عليَّ أن أصوم يوم النحر " : فلا يصح هذا النذر على ما روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة، وأما على المختار يصح كذا في "الدر المختار". (القمر) ولا فساد إلخ أي لا فساد في تسمية الصوم؛ لأن المعصية وهو الإعراض عن ضيافة الله تعالى غير متصلة بهذه التسمية ذكرًا، إنما الفساد في فعل الصوم في يوم النحر، فلذا يفتى أنه لا يؤدي نذره بل يقضيه ولو صام خرج عن العهدة؛ لأنه أداه كما التزمه، ولا يخفى عليك ما فيه فإن قوله : "لا نذر في معصية وكفارته كفارة اليمين" رواه أبو داود وغيره صريح في أنه لا ينعقد النذر، وقوله : "لا وفاء لنذر في معصية الله" رواه أبو داود صريح في أنه لا وفاء له فلا فائدة في النذر في صوم يوم العيد والقضاء يتلو الوجوب والتأويل بأن المراد بالمعصية: المعصية لعينها كشرب الخمر لا ضرورة ملجئة إليه هذا ما أفاده أستاذ أساتذة الهند أي مولانا نظام الملة والدين في الصبح الصادق فتدبر . (القمر) هذا القسم: أي القبيح لغيره، فإن الصلاة حسنة في نفسها؛ لاشتمالها على أفعال حسنة من الركوع والسجود وغيرهما، ولا قبح في شرط من شروطها من الطهارة وستر العورة وغيرها والوقت كله في نفسه زمان صالح لظرفية الصلاة، إلا أن وقت الطلوع والغروب والاستواء وقت مقارنة الشيطان للشمس على ما جاء في الحديث، فلذا جاء القبح في الصلاة في هذه الأوقات. (القمر)
Section on the Specific. Explanation of the divisions of ugliness. Disjunction and conjunction, so disbelief is an example of what is ugly in itself by linguistic placement; because it was placed for a meaning that is ugly in its original placement, and the intellect prohibits it even if revelation had not come, because the ugliness of ingratitude to the Benevolent is ingrained in sound intellects. And selling a free person is an example of what is ugly in itself by Shariah; because selling was not placed in language for a meaning that is ugly by intellect, rather the ugliness therein is because the Lawgiver interpreted selling as exchanging property for property, and a free person is not property according to Him. Similarly, the prayer of one without ablution is ugly by Shariah, because the Lawgiver removed the one without ablution from being qualified to perform it. And fasting on the Day of Nahr is an example of what is ugly due to something else by description; for fasting is in itself an act of worship and abstaining, but it is prohibited because the Day of Nahr is the day of Allah's hospitality, and in fasting there is turning away from it, and this meaning is necessary like a description for this fasting; because time is included in the definition of fasting, and the description of the part is a description of the whole, so it becomes invalid, and it is not binding by commencement, unlike a vow, for it is in itself obedience, and there is no corruption in the naming, rather corruption is in the act, so its make-up is obligatory, and unlike prayer in disliked times, for although it is also of this category, the time is separable from the prayer. (al-Qamar) And similarly the prayer of one without ablution etc.: I say: And similarly selling of ad-dama'in and al-malaqih, for prayer is good in itself, but the Lawgiver limited its capacity to the state of purity, so the prayer of a slave with impurity is futile like the speech of a bird and a madman. (al-Sunbuli) With property, therefore selling a free person becomes ugly by Shariah. (al-Qamar) As for fasting etc.: Its explanation is that fasting is abstaining from the three nullifiers from dawn to sunset with intention, and it is in itself good, except that fasting on the Day of Nahr is prohibited because of turning away from Allah's hospitality, and this meaning, i.e., turning away from hospitality, is like a description for fasting on the Day of Nahr, because this meaning, i.e., turning away from hospitality, is connected as a description to the time which is the locus of performing fasting, which is a day of festival and hospitality, and time is included in the definition of fasting and is a part of it, and the description of the part is a description of the whole, so it becomes invalid, and it is not binding by commencement, so its completion is not obligatory; rather it must be abandoned, and if abandoned, its make-up is not obligatory, and the secret is that the obligation of completion is for the preservation of the performed act, and it is not obligatory because it includes that which is ugly. (al-Qamar) Included in the definition of fasting: because fasting is abstaining from dawn to sunset. (al-Sunbuli) And description of the part etc.: So when the part, i.e., the time, which here is the Day of Nahr, is described with ugliness and defect, the whole, i.e., the fasting, is also described with it, as is not hidden. (al-Sunbuli) Unlike the vow etc., such as when he says, 'I vow to fast tomorrow,' and tomorrow is the Day of Nahr. But if he explicitly mentions the prohibited thing, saying, 'I vow to fast on the Day of Nahr,' then this vow is not valid according to what al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa. But according to the chosen position, it is valid, as in al-Durr al-Mukhtar. (al-Qamar) And there is no corruption etc., i.e., there is no corruption in naming the fasting; because the sin, which is turning away from Allah's hospitality, is not connected to this naming in remembrance; rather corruption is in the act of fasting on the Day of Nahr. Therefore, it is fatwaed that he should not fulfill his vow but should make it up, and if he fasts, he exits from liability because he performed it as he committed himself. And it is not hidden from you what is in it, for his statement: 'No vow in disobedience and its expiation is the expiation of an oath' reported by Abu Dawud and others is explicit that the vow is not contracted, and his statement: 'No fulfillment of a vow in disobedience to Allah' reported by Abu Dawud is explicit that there is no fulfillment, so there is no benefit in vowing to fast on the day of Eid, and make-up follows obligation. And the interpretation that what is meant by disobedience is disobedience in itself like drinking wine without a compelling necessity – this is what was taught by the teacher of the teachers of India, our master Nizam al-Milla wa al-Din in al-Subh al-Sadiq, so ponder. (al-Qamar) This category: i.e., the ugly due to something else. For prayer is good in itself because it includes good actions like bowing and prostrating and others, and there is no ugliness in its conditions like purity and covering of private parts and others, and all times are in themselves suitable for prayer to occur within them, except that the time of sunrise, sunset, and noon [when the sun is at zenith] is the time of the devil's association with the sun as reported in hadith, so ugliness appears in prayer at these times. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage presents a foundational Hanafi usul classification of al-qubh ('ugliness' or 'evil' in the legal sense, i.e., prohibition or disqualification). The author (likely from Sharh al-Nur al-Anwar) divides qubh into three categories: (1) qabih li 'aynihi wad'an – ugly in itself by linguistic placement, exemplified by kufr; its ugliness is intrinsic to its lexical meaning and is rationally recognized even without revelation. (2) qabih li 'aynihi shar'an – ugly in itself by the Shariah, exemplified by selling a free person; the act itself is not linguistically or rationally evil, but the Lawgiver defined sale as exchange of property, and a free person is not property in the Shariah, thus the transaction becomes legally invalid. Another example is prayer without wudu; the prayer act is good, but the Lawgiver restricts its validity to a state of purity. (3) qabih li ghayrihi wasfan – ugly due to something else as a description, exemplified by fasting on the Day of Nahr. The act of fasting is intrinsically good, but because the time (Day of Nahr) is a day of Allah's hospitality, fasting at that time constitutes turning away from that hospitality. Since time is part of the definition of fasting, the description of the part (time as ugly) attaches to the whole (the fast), rendering it invalid. Thus such a fast is not binding upon commencement; one must abandon it and no make-up is required. The passage then contrasts this with a vow to fast on that day, where the naming is not corrupt but the act is corrupt, so the vow is not valid according to one narration, but on the chosen view it is valid but the person is advised not to perform it and to make it up. The discussion also compares with prayer in disliked times, where the time (sunrise, etc.) is separable from the act, preventing the ugliness from affecting the prayer itself. The Hanafi position on each point is emphasized, with references to authorities like al-Qamar, al-Sunbuli, al-Durr al-Mukhtar, and the Indian scholar Nizam al-Din in al-Subh al-Sadiq.

Key Terms
قبيح لعينه وضعًا (qabīḥ li ʿaynihi waḍʿan): Ugly in itself by linguistic placement: the ugliness is inherent in the word's meaning, recognized by reason even without revelation.
قبيح لعينه شرعًا (qabīḥ li ʿaynihi sharʿan): Ugly in itself by Shariah: the act is not rationally or linguistically evil, but the Lawgiver prohibits it by defining its legal parameters.
قبيح لغيره وصفًا (qabīḥ li ghayrihi waṣfan): Ugly due to something else as a description: the act itself is good, but a contingent attribute (like time or circumstance) attaches a description of evil, making it temporarily invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of 'qabih li ghayrihi wasfan' (ugly due to something else as a description)?
A) Disbelief (kufr)
B) Selling a free person
C) Fasting on the Day of Nahr
D) Prayer without wudu

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the category of qubh (qabih li ghayrihi wasfan) explains why some acts are prohibited not because of their essence but due to a contingent description, affecting rulings on completion and make-up.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
beginner
8 min
The Two Categories of Prohibition: Inherent Evil vs. Acquired Evil
Definition of the two types of prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between qabih li-aynihi and qabih li-ghayrihi and classify given prohibitions accordingly.

Core Idea
A prohibited act may be evil in itself or because of an external attribute that attaches to it.

In Hanafi usul, prohibitions are not all alike. Some acts are forbidden because they are inherently evil—their essence is always wrong. Others become prohibited because of a separate factor that can be distinguished from the act itself. This lesson introduces this fundamental classification using the examples of intercourse during menstruation and prayer in usurped land.

Guided Path
1
Define the two categories
Identify the two types: qabih li-aynihi (evil in itself) and qabih li-ghayrihi (evil due to an external attribute). Note that the act itself remains permissible in essence; the prohibition is due to a separable factor.
The term 'qabih' refers to the evil that makes an act haram.
2
Understand the separability condition
For an act to be qabih li-ghayrihi, the external factor must be separable from the act. The passage shows that harm can be separated from intercourse, and usurpation can be separated from prayer.
If the factor cannot be separated, the prohibition is li-aynihi.
3
Apply to examples
Classify: Intercourse during menstruation is qabih li-ghayrihi (prohibited due to harm). Prayer in usurped land is also qabih li-ghayrihi (prohibited due to usurpation). Killing, fornication, and drinking wine are qabih li-aynihi (inherently evil).

مبحث الخاص
بيان أقسام القبح
وطء الحائض مشروع من حيث إنها منكوحته، وإنما يحرم لأجل الأذى وهو مما يمكن أن ينفك عن الوطء بأن يوجد الوطء بدون الأذى، والأذى بدون الوطء، وكذا الصلاة في الأرض المغصوبة مشروعة في ذاتها، وإنما تحرم لأجل شغل ملك الغير، وهو مما ينفك عن الصلاة بأن توجد الصلاة بدون شغل ملك الغير، بل في ملك نفسه، ويوجد الشغل بدون الصلاة بأن يسكن فيه ولا يصلي.
ولما فرغ عن تقسيم النهي أراد أن يبيّن أنّ أيّ فهي يقع على القسم الأول، وأيّ لهي يقع على القسم الآخر، فقال: والنهي عن الأفعال الحسية يقع على القسم الأول والمراد بالأفعال الحسية ما يكون معانيها المعلومة القديمة قبل الشرع باقية على حالها لا تتغير بالشرع كالقتل والزنا، وشرب الخمر بقيت معانيها وماهياتها بعد نزول التحريم على هذه حالها، ولا يراد أن حرمتها حسية معلومة بالحس لا يتوقف على الشرع، فالنهي عن الأفعال عند الإطلاق وعدم الموانع يقع على القبح لعينه، إلا إذا قام الدليل على خلافه كالوطء حالة الحيض حرام لغيره مع أنه فعل حسي لقيام الدليل. وعن الأمور الشرعية يقع على الذي اتصل به وصفا عطفا على قوله: عن الأفعال الحسية أي والنهي عن الأمور الشرعية يقع على القسم الذي اتصل به القبح وصفا يعني يحمل على أنه قبيح لغيره، والمراد بالأمور الشرعية: ما تغيرت معانيها الأصلية بعد ورود الشرع بها كالصوم والصلاة والبيع والإجارة، فإن الصوم: هو الإمساك في الأصل، وزيدت عليه في الشرع أشياء. والصلاة: هو الدعاء زيدت عليه أشياء. والبيع مبادلة المال بالمال فقط زيدت عليها أهلية العاقدين، ومحلية المعقود عليه، وغير ذلك. والإجارة: مبادلة المال بالمنافع زيدت عليه معلومية المستأجر، والأجرة، لقيام الدليل: فإنه قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَيَسْأَلُونَكَ عَنِ الْمَحِيضِ قُلْ هُوَ أَذىً فَاعْتَزِلُوا النِّسَاءَ فِي الْمَحِيضِ (البقرة : ۲۲۲)، فهذا يدل على أن النهي عن الوطء حال الحيض لأجل الأذى المجاور ، وهو الأذى حتى لو قربها ووجد العلوق يثبت النسب اتفاقا. الحسية لا على القسم الأول ليرد أنه لا معنى لهذه العبارة. على أنه أي المنهي عنه إذا كان من الأفعال الشرعية وصفا وإنما خص الوصف دون المحاور عملاً بكمال القبح بقدر الإمكان؛ لأن الوصف غير منفك عن المنهي عنه، بخلاف المجاور كذا قيل، ثم اعلم أن هذا أكثر وأشهر وإلا فالنهي عن الأفعال الشرعية قد يقع على القسم الذي اتصل به القبح مجاوراً كالنهي عن الأرض المغصوبة كذا قال ابن الملك. أشياء وهي كون الإمساك إمساكا عن المفطرات الثلاثة، وكونه من الصبح إلى الغروب والنية أشياء كالركوع والسجود، والقعود والقيام وغيرها. أهلية العاقدين بأن يكون البائع والمشتري عاقدين مميزين. ومحلية المعقود عليه كأن يكون المبيع موجودًا فلا ينعقد بيع المعدوم، وأن يكون مملوكًا في نفسه، فلا ينعقد بيع الكلأ. وغير ذلك: كأن يسمع المتعاقدان كلامهما فإذا قال المشتري "اشتريت" و لم يسمع البائع كلام المشتري لم ينعقد البيع كذا في "العالمكيرية". معلومية المستأجر : أي يكون محل المنفعة معلوما، فلو قال آجرتك إحدى هاتين الدارين، أو أحد هذين العبدين لم يصح العقد. والأجرة أي معلومية الأجرة إذ لو لم تكن الأجرة معلومة لأدى الجهالة إلى المنازعة.
Section on the Specific
Explanation of the Categories of Evil
Intercourse with a menstruating woman is permissible insofar as she is his wife, but it is prohibited because of the harm, which can be separated from intercourse: intercourse can occur without harm, and harm can occur without intercourse. Similarly, prayer in usurped land is permissible in itself, but it is prohibited because of occupying the property of another, which can be separated from prayer: prayer can occur without occupying another's property (rather in one's own property), and occupying can occur without prayer (by residing without praying).
When he finished dividing prohibition, he wanted to explain which [type] falls under the first category and which under the second. So he said: "And prohibition concerning sensory acts falls under the first category." By sensory acts he means those whose original meanings known before the law remain unchanged by the law, such as killing, fornication, and drinking wine—their meanings and essences remained as they were after the prohibition descended. It is not intended that their unlawfulness is sensory and independent of the law. So, prohibition of acts, when unrestricted and without impediments, falls on [that which is] evil in itself, unless evidence indicates otherwise, like intercourse during menstruation being prohibited due to something else, although it is a sensory act, because of the evidence. And concerning shari' matters, it falls on that which is connected to it as an attribute—i.e., prohibition concerning shari' matters falls on the category that is connected to evil as an attribute, meaning it is interpreted as evil due to something else. By shari' matters he means those whose original meanings changed after the revelation of the law, such as fasting, prayer, sale, and lease. Fasting: originally it was mere abstention, and additional conditions were added by the law. Prayer: originally it was supplication, and additional elements were added. Sale: originally it was exchange of property for property, and additional conditions were added regarding the capacity of the contracting parties, the legality of the subject matter, etc. Lease: exchange of property for benefits, with additional conditions of knowledge of the lessee and the rent. Because of the evidence: Allah Most High said: "And they ask you about menstruation. Say: It is harm, so keep away from women during menstruation" (2:222). This indicates that the prohibition of intercourse during menstruation is due to the adjacent harm—it is harm even if he approaches and conception occurs, lineage is established by consensus. Sensory acts are not in the first category, otherwise this statement would have no meaning. It means the prohibited act, if from shari' acts, is [interpreted as] an attribute. He specified the attribute rather than the adjacent because of the complete evil as much as possible, since the attribute is inseparable from the prohibited act, unlike the adjacent. This is what is most common and well-known; otherwise, prohibition of shari' acts may fall on the category connected to evil as adjacent, like the prohibition of [prayer in] usurped land, as Ibn al-Malik said. Things: that abstention is from the three nullifiers, from dawn to sunset, and intention. Things: like bowing, prostration, sitting, standing, etc. Capacity of the contracting parties: that the seller and buyer be discerning. Legality of the subject matter: that the sold item exist (so the sale of a non-existent thing is not valid) and that it be owned in itself (so the sale of grass on common land is not valid). Other: that the two parties hear each other's speech—if the buyer says 'I bought' and the seller does not hear it, the sale is not concluded, as in al-Alamgiriyya. Knowledge of the lessee: meaning the place of benefit must be known, so if one says 'I lease you one of these two houses' or 'one of these two slaves,' the contract is not valid. The rent: meaning knowledge of the rent, because if the rent is unknown, it leads to dispute.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage is an extended commentary on the classification of prohibitions (nahy) into two types: those that are prohibited because they are evil in themselves (qabih li-aynihi) and those that are prohibited because of an external attribute (qabih li-ghayrihi). The author explains that sensory acts (af'al hissiyya) such as killing, fornication, and drinking wine remain essentially the same before and after revelation—their inherent evil is unchanged—so the prohibition targets the act itself. However, if evidence shows that the prohibition is due to an external factor, like the harm (adha) in intercourse during menstruation, then the act is evil due to something else (qabih li-ghayrihi). Similarly, shari' acts (umur shar'iyya) like prayer, fasting, sale, and lease have had their original meanings expanded by the law; their prohibition, if any, is typically due to an attribute that attaches to them, such as the unlawful usurpation in the case of prayer in usurped land. The commentary emphasizes that the prohibition of sensory acts is presumed to be qabih li-aynihi unless evidence indicates otherwise, while for shari' acts the presumption is qabih li-ghayrihi. The Quranic verse about menstruation is cited to illustrate that the prohibition of intercourse is due to the adjacent harm (al-adha al-mujawir), not the act itself. The passage also clarifies that the term 'sensory' does not mean the prohibition is known by the senses independently of revelation; rather, the acts themselves are sensory, but their prohibition is established by the law.

Key Terms
القبح لعينه (al-qubḥ li-aynihi): The prohibition is due to the inherent evil of the act itself, such that the act is always and in all circumstances evil.
القبح لغيره (al-qubḥ li-ghayrihi): The prohibition is due to an external attribute that attaches to the act, such that the act in itself is not evil, but becomes prohibited because of that attribute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification in this lesson, which of the following acts is prohibited due to an external attribute (qabih li-ghayrihi)?
A) Murder
B) Fornication
C) Prayer in usurped land
D) Drinking wine

Key Takeaway
Prohibited acts are classified into two categories: those evil in themselves (qabih li-aynihi) and those evil due to an external attribute (qabih li-ghayrihi), with the separability of the external factor being the decisive criterion.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

10 min
Applying the Categories: Sensory Acts vs. Shari' Acts
Application of the two categories to sensory and shari' acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a prohibited act as sensory or shari' and determine under which category of evil it falls, using evidence from the Quran and Hanafi methodology.

Core Idea
Sensory acts are presumed evil in themselves; shari' acts are presumed evil due to an attribute—unless evidence proves otherwise.

After establishing the two categories of qabih li-aynihi and li-ghayrihi, this lesson explores how they apply to different types of acts. The Hanafi school distinguishes between sensory acts, whose essences are unchanged by the law, and shari' acts, whose meanings are defined by the law. This determines the default classification of their prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish sensory from shari' acts
Sensory acts (af'al hissiyya) are those whose essences are known before revelation and remain unchanged (e.g., killing, fornication, drinking wine). Shari' acts (umur shar'iyya) have their original meanings altered by the law (e.g., prayer, fasting, sale, lease).
The classification is based on whether the law changes the act's meaning.
2
State the default rule for each
For sensory acts, the default is that prohibition falls on qabih li-aynihi—unless evidence indicates otherwise. For shari' acts, the default is that prohibition falls on qabih li-ghayrihi—meaning the evil is due to an attribute attached by the law.
This is a presumption (asl) in the absence of contrary evidence.
3
Identify exceptions
An exception to the sensory default: intercourse during menstruation is a sensory act but prohibited li-ghayrihi due to evidence (Quran 2:222). An exception to the shari' default: prayer in usurped land is a shari' act but its prohibition is due to the adjacent external factor (usurpation), not an inherent attribute of the prayer itself.
The evidence overrides the default presumption.
4
Analyze the Quranic evidence
The verse says 'Say: It is harm, so keep away from women during menstruation.' The harm (adha) is an external factor that is adjacent (mujawir) to the act, not an attribute of the act itself. This proves the prohibition is li-ghayrihi.
The harm is separable from the act, as explained in Lesson 1.
