Types of Azima: The Hanafi Taxonomy of Original Rulings
Defines azima and its four types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four types of azima (fard, wajib, sunna, mubah) based on the Hanafi criteria of disbelief, punishment, and reward, and identify the evidentiary basis (qat'i vs zanni) for fard and wajib.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, fard and wajib are distinct: fard's denier becomes a disbeliever, wajib's denier is punished but not a disbeliever.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar introduces the concept of 'azima' (determination) as the original rulings of Sharia, distinct from concessions (rukhsa). It then classifies these rulings into four hierarchical categories based on the consequences of denial and action. Understanding this taxonomy is foundational for Hanafi juristic reasoning, as it affects how obligations are proven and the weight of evidence required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two major categories of rulings
The passage opens with 'al-mashru'at 'ala naw'ayn: 'azima and rukhsa. Recognize that 'azima is the original ruling not tied to circumstances, while rukhsa is a concession due to circumstances like illness or travel.
This dichotomy is unique to Hanafi usul and sets the stage for the classification.
2
Analyze the definition of 'azima'
The author defines 'azima as 'isma' (name) for the original ruling that is not connected to 'awarid (accidents). Understand that 'azima includes both commands (like prayer) and prohibitions (like theft).
The definition emphasizes the inherent, circumstance-independent nature of 'azima.
3
Trace the logical division into four types
The passage divides based on two dichotomies: first, whether denying the ruling causes kufr; if yes => fard. If not, then check if leaving it is punished; if yes => wajib. If not, then check if doing it brings reward; if yes => sunna. If not => mubah.
This yields an exhaustive and mutually exclusive classification.
4
Apply the definitions to each type
For each type, state the exact consequence from the text: fard: denier becomes kafir; wajib: leaver punished but not kafir; sunna: doer rewarded, no punishment for leaving; mubah: no reward or punishment.
Memorizing these consequences is crucial for usul al-fiqh.
5
Connect fard and wajib to evidentiary strength
Though not explicit in the passage, the Hanafi principle is that fard is proven by qat'i (definitive) evidence, while wajib is proven by zanni (speculative) evidence. This underlies why they are separate categories.
This explains why denier of fard becomes a disbeliever: they reject a certain truth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الأحكام المشروعة
بيان العزيمة والرخصة
المشروعات على نوعين: عزيمة ورخصة. فالعزيمة وهي اسم لما هو أصل منها غير متعلّق بالعوارض، يعني لم يكن شرعها باعتبار العوارض كما كان شرع الإفطار باعتبار المرض، بل يكون حكمًا أصليًا من الله تعالى ابتداءً، سواء كان متعلقا بالفعل كالمأمورات، أو متعلقا بالترك كالمحرمات.
[أنواع العزيمة]
وهي أربعة أنواع؛ لأنها لا تخلو من أن يكفّر جاحدها أو لا. الأول: هو الفرض، والثاني: لا يخلو إمّا أن يُعاقب بتركه أو لا، الأول هو الواجب، والثاني: لا يخلو إما أن يستحق الثواب بفعله أو لا، الأول هو السنة، والثاني: هو المباح. فالفرض: ما يكفر جاحده. والواجب: ما يعاقب بتركه ولا يكفر تاركه. والسنة: ما يثاب بفعله ولا يعاقب بتركه. والمباح: ما لا يثاب بفعله ولا يعاقب بتركه.
Chapter on Enacted Rulings
Explanation of Determination and Concession
The enactments are of two types: determination and concession. Determination is the name for that which is original among them, not connected to circumstances, meaning its legislation was not due to circumstances as the legislation of breaking fast was due to illness, but rather it is an original ruling from Allah Almighty initially, whether it pertains to an act like commands or pertains to abandonment like prohibitions.
[Types of Determination]
And they are four types; because they never lack either that its denier is deemed a disbeliever or not. The first: it is the obligatory (fard). The second: it either is punished for leaving it or not, the first is the obligatory (wajib), the second: it either receives reward for doing it or not, the first is the supererogatory (sunna), and the second is the permissible (mubah). So fard: its denier becomes a disbeliever. Wajib: one is punished for leaving it but its abandoner is not deemed a disbeliever. Sunna: one is rewarded for doing it but not punished for leaving it. Mubah: one is not rewarded for doing it nor punished for leaving it.
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of 'azima' (determination) and its types, forming a foundational taxonomy of legal rulings in Hanafi usul. The author begins by stating that all legislated rulings are either azima or rukhsah (concession). Azima is described as the original ruling that is not dependent on accidental circumstances (عوارض) like travel or illness—contrasting with rukhsah which is granted due to such circumstances. The defining characteristic of azima is its inherent strength and lack of connection to external excuses.

Then the author enumerates the four types of azima based on the consequences of rejection and action. First, if denying the ruling leads to disbelief, it is 'fard' (obligatory). Second, if denying does not cause disbelief but leaving it incurs punishment, it is 'wajib' (obligatory but a notch lower). Third, if doing it brings reward but leaving is not punished, it is 'sunna' (recommended). Fourth, if neither reward nor punishment is attached, it is 'mubah' (permissible). The commentary elaborates that these categories stem from the strength of their proofs: fard is established by definitive evidence (qat'i), while wajib by speculative evidence (zanni). This hierarchy is unique to the Hanafi school, where fard and wajib are distinct categories; in other schools, they are often synonymous.

Key Terms
العزيمة (al-azima): Original ruling not tied to circumstances; includes fard, wajib, sunna, mubah
الفَرْض (al-fard): Ruling whose denier becomes a disbeliever; established by qat'i evidence
الواجب (al-wajib): Ruling whose leaver is punished but not deemed a disbeliever; established by zanni evidence
السنة (al-sunna): Ruling whose doer is rewarded, leaving is not punished
المباح (al-mubah): Ruling with no reward or punishment for action or inaction

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi taxonomy in this passage, what distinguishes fard from wajib?
A) Fard is established by definitive evidence and its denier is a disbeliever, while wajib is by speculative evidence and its leaver is punished but not deemed a disbeliever.
B) Fard is only for acts of worship, while wajib is for all other rulings.
C) Fard requires intention (niyya), while wajib does not.
D) There is no distinction; fard and wajib are synonyms.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi hierarchy of azima defines five levels of rulings (fard, wajib, sunna, mubah) based on evidentiary strength and consequences, with fard and wajib being distinct categories.

The Four Types of 'Azimah: Fard, Wajib, Sunnah, and Nafal
Describes the two categories of legal rulings and the four types of 'azimah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four types of 'azimah, explain the basis of their classification (denial, punishment, blame), and identify which category each primary legal ruling belongs to in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
'Azimah rulings are classified by the consequences: denial of fard causes kufr, leaving wajib brings punishment, leaving sunnah brings blame, and nafal has no blame.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the primary legal rulings (al-ahkam al-shar'iyyah) are divided into two overarching categories: 'azimah (original determinations) and rukhsah (concessions). This lesson focuses on 'azimah, which consists of four types: fard, wajib, sunnah, and nafal. These are distinguished based on the severity of consequences for denial, omission, and blame. Understanding this classification is fundamental to grasping the Hanafi hierarchy of legal obligations.

Guided Path
1
Understand the overall division of rulings
Legislated rulings are of two types: 'azimah (primary) and rukhsah (concession). 'Azimah is the original ruling, not based on contingencies.
Rukhsah will be covered later; this lesson only deals with 'azimah.
2
Identify the basis of classification for 'azimah
The four types are distinguished by three criteria: (1) whether the denier of the ruling becomes a kafir, (2) whether the abandoner is punished, and (3) whether the abandoner is blamed.
These are progressive: fard has the first, wajib has the second but not the first, etc.
3
Map each consequence to a category
Fard: denier becomes kafir. Wajib: abandoner punished, but denier not kafir. Sunnah: abandoner blamed but not punished. Nafal: no blame or punishment.
This classification is unique to Hanafi usul; other schools may define these differently.
4
Recognize the subdivisions of fard
Fard is further divided into fard qat'i (definitive) and fard zanni (speculative), and into fard 'ayn (individual obligation) and fard kifayah (collective obligation).
The main text mentions that fard is established by a proof with no ambiguity, but the commentary adds these subdivisions.
5
Understand that these four types cover all primary rulings
The four types are exhaustive for 'azimah. Other categories like haram and makruh are included by considering the aspect of abandonment (they fall under fard or wajib when viewed as prohibitions).
This will be elaborated in a subsequent lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الأحكام المشروعة
أنواع العزيمة

[أنواع العزيمة]
وهي أربعة أنواع؛ لأنها لا تخلو من أن يكفّر جاحدها أو لا. الأول: هو الفرض، والثاني: لا يخلو إمّا أن يُعاقب بتركه أو لا، الأول هو الواجب، والثاني: لا يخلو إما أن يستحق
القصد
يعني أن الأحكام إلخ لما كان المشروعات تطلق على العلل والأسباب والشروط والأحكام نبه الشارح ليه بهذا التفسير إلى أن المراد ههنا هي الأحكام المشروعة لا غير. (القمر) وهي اسم إلخ: اعلم أن العزيمة بهذا المعنى لا يلزمها الرخصة وقد يقال: إن الحكم إذا تغيّر بعذر فالمتغيّر عنه عزيمة والمتغيّر إليه رخصة، فالعزيمة بهذه المعنى يلزمها الرخصة. ثم اعلم أن هذه الأحكام الأصلية سميت عزيمةً لكونها في نهاية التأكيد. والعزم هو الكامل المؤكد. (القمر) غير متعلق بالعوارض: صفة كاشفة لقوله: أصل منها، أي من الأحكام المشروعة، وليس قيدا له؛ فإن كل أصل، أي ثابت ابتداءً من الشارع عليها فهو غير متعلّق بالعوارض، وإنما احتاج إلى الكشف؛ لأن الأصل يطلق على معانٍ فلا بد من كشف ما هو المراد ههنا . (القمر) يعني لم يكن إلخ تفسير لقوله: غير متعلّق إلخ. (القمر) العوارض وهي الموانع التي عهدت في الشريعة كالسفر والمرض وسيجيء بيانها. (القمر) وهي أربعة أنواع والرخصة أيضًا لا تخلو عن هذه الأنواع الأربعة؛ فإن هذه الأنواع لمطلق
الحكم، إلا أن العزيمة لما كانت أصلاً خصها المصنف له بالذكر ، ويعلم حال الرخصة بالمقايسة. (القمر) هو الفرض إلخ قال الطحطاوي : الفرض قسمان قطعي وهو ما ثبت بدليل قطعي موجب للعلم البديهي، ويكفر جاحده وظني وهو ما ثبت بدليل قطعي لكن فيه شبهة، ويسمى عمليا، وهو ما يفوت الجواز بفواته، وحكمه كالأول غير أنه لا يكفّر جاحده ثم قال بعد عبارة: وقد يطلق الفرض و يراد به ما يشمل القطعي والعملي، ويطلق الواجب ويراد به الفرض العملي أيضًا؛ ولهذا قال بعض المحققين: إنه أقوى نوعي الواجب وأضعف نوعي الفرض ثم الفرض من حيث هو قسمان :أيضًا فرض عين وفرض كفاية. فالأول: ما يلزم كل فرد ولا يسقط بفعل البعض كالوضوء مثلاً، والثاني: ما يلزم جملة المفروض عليهم دون كل فرد بخصوصه؛ فيسقط عن الجميع بفعل البعض كاستماع القرآن وحفظه ،وغيرهما طحطاوي على المراقي. (السنبلي)

تعريف الفريضة وحكمها
فصل في الأحكام المشروعة تاركه الملامة أو لا، فالأول هو السنة، والثاني هو النفل والحرام داخل في الفرض باعتبار
الترك، وكذا المكروه في الواجب والمباح مما ليس بمشروع بالمعنى الذي قلنا. أي تحريما تعريف الفريضة وحكمها ]
فالأول: فريضة وهي ما لا يحتمل زيادة ولا نقصانًا ثبتت بدليل لاشبهة فيه، فأعداد الركعات والصيامات وكيفيتهما كلها متعيّن بتعيين لا ازدياد فيه ولا نقصان، وثابت مقطوع لا يحتمل الشبهة ولا يقال إنه يتناول بعض المباحات والنوافل الثابتتين كذلك؛ لأن كلمة "ما" عبارة عن عزيمة معهودة لم يتناولها قطّ.
كالإيمان والأركان الأربعة وهي الصلاة والزكاة والصوم والحج.
والحرام إلخ: دفع دخل مقدر تقريره أن الحصر في الأربعة باطل لخروج الحرام والمكروه تحريما؟ وحاصل الدفع: أن الحرام كشرب الخمر داخل في الفرض بحسب الترك؛ فإن تركه فضل؛ لأن دليل الحرمة قطعي، والمراد بالفرض أعم من أن يكون فعله فرضًا أو تركه فرضًا والمكروه تحريما كأكل الضب داخل في الواجب بحسب الترك؛ فإن تركه واجب؛ إذ في دليله شبهة، والمراد بالواجب أعم من أن يكون فعله واجبًا أو تركه واجبا، بقى الكلام في المكروه تنزيها فأقول: إنه داخل في السنة؛ لأن ترك المكروه تنزيها سنة. (القمر) والمباح إلخ: دفع دخل مقدر تقريره: أن الحصر في الأربعة باطل لوجود قسم آخر سواها وهو المباح؟ وحاصل الدفع: أن المباح ليس بداخل في القسم؛ فإن المقسم هو المشروع بمعنى الذي شرعه الله تعالى لعباده كما قد مرّ آنفا من الشارح، والمباح ليس كذلك، وفيه أن هذا القول منسوب إلى بعض المعتزلة والأشهر عندنا أن المباح أيضا داخل في الحكم الشرعي بناءً على صدق تعريفه عليه، وهو خطاب الله تعالى المتعلّق بأفعال المكلفين اقتضاء أو تخييرا، فالأصوب أن يجاب عن الدخل بأن المباح داخل في النفل؛ فإن النفل على التقسيم المذكور هو الذي لا يكفّر جاحده ولا يعاقب بتركه ولا يستحق تاركه الملامة وهذا صادق على المباح أيضًا؛ فلا ينتقض الحصر لخروجه.(القمر) قلنا: أي الكفر عند الإنكار المعاقبة بالترك والملامة فريضة: قد عرفت المعنى اللغوي للفرض فتذكره. (القمر) بدليل لا شبهة فيه : الظاهر المتبادر من حيث إن وقوع النكرة تحت النفي يفيد العموم، أن الشبهة المنفية أعم أن تكون شبهة ناشئة من من دليل أو شبهة غير ناشئة من دليل القمر كذلك أي بدليل لا شبهة فيه، ولا يحتمل زيادةً ولا نقصانًا. (القمر) لأن إلخ: دليل لقوله : لا يقال إلخ. (القمر) كالإيمان: فإنه لا يزيد ولا ينقص في غير زمان الوحي وإن كان يزيد في زمان الوحي بزيادة متعلقاته. (القمر)
Chapter on legislated rulings: Types of determination ('azimah): That is, the legislated rulings that Allah legislated for His servants are of two types: one is 'azimah, and the second is rukhsah (concession). 'Azimah is a name for that which is an original (ruling) from them, not related to contingencies, meaning its legislation was not due to contingencies like the legislation of breaking fast due to illness, rather it is an original ruling from Allah initially, whether related to action like commanded matters, or related to avoidance like prohibitions. [Types of 'azimah] They are four types: because they are not free from (the possibility) that its denier is rendered an unbeliever or not. The first is fard (obligatory); the second: it is not free from (the possibility) that its abandoner is punished or not; the first of these is wajib; the second: it is not free from (the possibility) that its abandoner deserves blame or not; the first is sunnah, and the second is nafal. The commentary explains: ... (al-Qamari) ... al-Tahawi said: Fard is of two types: qat'i (definitive) which is established by a definitive proof leading to intuitive knowledge, and its denier is an unbeliever; and zanni (speculative) which is established by a definitive proof but with some ambiguity, called 'amali, and its omission invalidates the act, but its denier is not an unbeliever. ... Then fard is also of two types: fard 'ayn and fard kifayah. ... Definition of fard and its ruling: The first is fard, which does not admit increase or decrease, established by a proof with no ambiguity... Haram is included in fard with respect to abandonment... Makruh tahriman is included in wajib with respect to abandonment... Makruh tanzihan is included in sunnah... Mubah: some say mubah is not included, but the correct view is that mubah is included in nafal... (al-Qamari) ...
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of the primary legal rulings ('azimah) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author begins by stating that legislated rulings are of two types: 'azimah (primary rulings based on original intent) and rukhsah (concessions due to exigencies). He then explains that 'azimah rulings are original, not dependent on contingencies like travel or illness. The commentary clarifies that 'azimah and rukhsah are opposites but can be related: the original ruling is 'azimah, and its change due to an excuse is rukhsah. The core of the lesson is the four-fold classification of 'azimah based on the consequences of denial, punishment for omission, and blame: (1) Fard: its denier becomes an unbeliever; (2) Wajib: its abandoner is punished but denier is not an unbeliever; (3) Sunnah: its abandoner is blameworthy but not punished; (4) Nafal: no blame or punishment for leaving, and it includes recommended and permissible acts. The commentary by al-Tahawi further subdivides fard into qat'i (definitive) and zanni (speculative), and into fard 'ayn (individual obligation) and fard kifayah (collective obligation). The passage also addresses potential objections: how haram and makruh fit into this scheme. It explains that haram (like drinking wine) is considered fard with respect to its abandonment (since its proof is definitive), and makruh tahriman (like eating a certain animal with ambiguous proof) is considered wajib with respect to its abandonment. Makruh tanzihan is included in sunnah because its avoidance is recommended. Mubah is included in nafal because it shares the characteristic of no blame or punishment. The author uses scholarly references like al-Qamari and al-Tahawi (from his commentary on al-Maraqi) to support these classifications. The overall purpose is to provide a precise taxonomy of the five legal categories (ahkam al-khamsah) as understood in the Hanafi school, emphasizing the distinctions between fard and wajib (based on certainty of the proof) and the inclusion of other categories.

Key Terms
عزيمة ('azimah): A primary ruling not based on contingencies; original determination.
فرض (fard): A ruling established by a definitive proof; its denier becomes an unbeliever.
واجب (wajib): A ruling established by a proof with some ambiguity; its abandoner is punished but denier is not an unbeliever.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act whose abandoner is blameworthy but not punished.
نفل (nafal): A voluntary act with no blame or punishment for omission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of 'azimah has the characteristic that its denier becomes an unbeliever?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah
C) Fard
D) Nafal

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, 'azimah rulings are classified into four types based on the consequences of denial, punishment, and blame: fard, wajib, sunnah, and nafal, with fard having the strongest consequence (takfir upon denial).

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Including Haram, Makruh, and Mubah in the 'Azimah Classification
Explains how prohibitory rulings (haram, makruh) and permissible acts (mubah) are integrated into the four-type classification of 'azimah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Hanafi school logically includes haram under fard, makruh tahrimi under wajib, makruh tanzihi under sunnah, and mubah under nafal, and justify the integration based on the aspect of abandonment (tark).

Core Idea
Haram and makruh are included in the 'azimah types by considering the legal ruling on their abandonment: haram's abandonment is fard, makruh tahrimi's abandonment is wajib, makruh tanzihi's abandonment is sunnah, and mubah's lack of blame places it in nafal.

The previous lesson established that 'azimah rulings are of four types: fard, wajib, sunnah, and nafal. But what about prohibitions like haram and makruh? The Hanafi masters ingeniously integrate these by focusing on the 'abandonment' (tark) aspect. This lesson examines how the passage defends the four-fold classification against objections that it excludes haram, makruh, and mubah, demonstrating the richness of Hanafi legal taxonomy.

Guided Path
1
Recall the four types of 'azimah
Fard, wajib, sunnah, nafal are the four primary categories based on denial, punishment, and blame.
2
Identify the objection to the four-fold classification
Some might argue that the classification is incomplete because it does not explicitly include haram, makruh (tahrimi and tanzihi), and mubah.
This objection arises from a surface reading of the categories.
3
Understand the Hanafi response for haram
Haram is included in fard by considering the aspect of abandonment: leaving a haram act is fard (obligatory). Since the proof for haram is definitive (like drinking wine), its abandonment is a fard, and therefore haram falls under the fard category when viewed from the perspective of tark.
The term 'fard' here is general, covering both doing a fard and leaving a fard.
4
Understand the response for makruh tahrimi
Makruh tahrimi (e.g., eating a certain animal) has a proof with some ambiguity, so its abandonment is wajib. Hence, it is included in wajib.
Similarly, makruh tanzihi's abandonment is sunnah, so it falls under sunnah.
5
Understand the response for mubah
The passage presents two views: some say mubah is not included because it is not 'legislated' in the sense of being commanded or prohibited. However, the more correct view (according to most Hanafis) is that mubah is included in nafal because it shares the characteristic of no blame or punishment for doing or leaving.
This shows that the Hanafi school considers mubah as part of the legal framework.

فصل في الأحكام المشروعة
أنواع العزيمة
يعني أن الأحكام المشروعة التي شرعها الله تعالى لعباده على نوعين: أحدهما: العزيمة، والثاني الرخصة. فالعزيمة وهي اسم لما هو أصل منها غير متعلّق بالعوارض، يعني لم يكن شرعها باعتبار العوارض كما كان شرع الإفطار باعتبار المرض، بل يكون حكمًا أصليًا من الله تعالى ابتداءً، سواء كان متعلقا بالفعل كالمأمورات، أو متعلقا بالترك كالمحرمات.
[أنواع العزيمة]
وهي أربعة أنواع؛ لأنها لا تخلو من أن يكفّر جاحدها أو لا. الأول: هو الفرض، والثاني: لا يخلو إمّا أن يُعاقب بتركه أو لا، الأول هو الواجب، والثاني: لا يخلو إما أن يستحق
القصد
يعني أن الأحكام إلخ لما كان المشروعات تطلق على العلل والأسباب والشروط والأحكام نبه الشارح ليه بهذا التفسير إلى أن المراد ههنا هي الأحكام المشروعة لا غير. (القمر) غير متعلق بالعوارض: صفة كاشفة لقوله: أصل منها، أي من الأحكام المشروعة، وليس قيدا له؛ فإن كل أصل، أي ثابت ابتداءً من الشارع عليها فهو غير متعلّق بالعوارض، وإنما احتاج إلى الكشف؛ لأن الأصل يطلق على معانٍ فلا بد من كشف ما هو المراد ههنا . (القمر) يعني لم يكن إلخ تفسير لقوله: غير متعلّق إلخ. (القمر) العوارض وهي الموانع التي عهدت في الشريعة كالسفر والمرض وسيجيء بيانها. (القمر) هو الفرض إلخ قال الطحطاوي : الفرض قسمان قطعي وهو ما ثبت بدليل قطعي موجب للعلم البديهي، ويكفر جاحده وظني وهو ما ثبت بدليل قطعي لكن فيه شبهة، ويسمى عمليا، وهو ما يفوت الجواز بفواته، وحكمه كالأول غير أنه لا يكفّر جاحده ثم قال بعد عبارة: وقد يطلق الفرض و يراد به ما يشمل القطعي والعملي، ويطلق الواجب ويراد به الفرض العملي أيضًا؛ ولهذا قال بعض المحققين: إنه أقوى نوعي الواجب وأضعف نوعي الفرض ثم الفرض من حيث هو قسمان :أيضًا فرض عين وفرض كفاية. فالأول: ما يلزم كل فرد ولا يسقط بفعل البعض كالوضوء مثلاً، والثاني: ما يلزم جملة المفروض عليهم دون كل فرد بخصوصه؛ فيسقط عن الجميع بفعل البعض كاستماع القرآن وحفظه ،وغيرهما طحطاوي على المراقي. كالإيمان والأركان الأربعة وهي الصلاة والزكاة والصوم والحج.

(القمر) والمباح إلخ: دفع دخل مقدر تقريره: أن الحصر في الأربعة باطل لوجود قسم آخر سواها وهو المباح؟ وحاصل الدفع: أن المباح ليس بداخل في القسم؛ فإن المقسم هو المشروع بمعنى الذي شرعه الله تعالى لعباده كما قد مرّ آنفا من الشارح، والمباح ليس كذلك، وفيه أن هذا القول منسوب إلى بعض المعتزلة والأشهر عندنا أن المباح أيضا داخل في الحكم الشرعي بناءً على صدق تعريفه عليه، وهو خطاب الله تعالى المتعلّق بأفعال المكلفين اقتضاء أو تخييرا، فالأصوب أن يجاب عن الدخل بأن المباح داخل في النفل؛ فإن النفل على التقسيم المذكور هو الذي لا يكفّر جاحده ولا يعاقب بتركه ولا يستحق تاركه الملامة وهذا صادق على المباح أيضًا؛ فلا ينتقض الحصر لخروجه.(القمر) قلنا: أي الكفر عند الإنكار المعاقبة بالترك والملامة فريضة: قد عرفت المعنى اللغوي للفرض فتذكره. (القمر) بدليل لا شبهة فيه : الظاهر المتبادر من حيث إن وقوع النكرة تحت النفي يفيد العموم، أن الشبهة المنفية أعم أن تكون شبهة ناشئة من من دليل أو شبهة غير ناشئة من دليل القمر كذلك أي بدليل لا شبهة فيه، ولا يحتمل زيادةً ولا نقصانًا. (القمر) لأن إلخ: دليل لقوله : لا يقال إلخ. (القمر) كالإيمان: فإنه لا يزيد ولا ينقص في غير زمان الوحي وإن كان يزيد في زمان الوحي بزيادة متعلقاته. (القمر)
Chapter on legislated rulings: Types of determination ('azimah): That is, the legislated rulings that Allah legislated for His servants are of two types: one is 'azimah, and the second is rukhsah (concession). 'Azimah is a name for that which is an original (ruling) from them, not related to contingencies, meaning its legislation was not due to contingencies like the legislation of breaking fast due to illness, rather it is an original ruling from Allah initially, whether related to action like commanded matters, or related to avoidance like prohibitions. [Types of 'azimah] They are four types: because they are not free from (the possibility) that its denier is rendered an unbeliever or not. The first is fard (obligatory); the second: it is not free from (the possibility) that its abandoner is punished or not; the first of these is wajib; the second: it is not free from (the possibility) that its abandoner deserves blame or not; the first is sunnah, and the second is nafal. The commentary explains: ... (al-Qamari) ... al-Tahawi said: Fard is of two types: qat'i (definitive) which is established by a definitive proof leading to intuitive knowledge, and its denier is an unbeliever; and zanni (speculative) which is established by a definitive proof but with some ambiguity, called 'amali, and its omission invalidates the act, but its denier is not an unbeliever. ... Then fard is also of two types: fard 'ayn and fard kifayah. ... Definition of fard and its ruling: The first is fard, which does not admit increase or decrease, established by a proof with no ambiguity... Haram is included in fard with respect to abandonment... Makruh tahriman is included in wajib with respect to abandonment... Makruh tanzihan is included in sunnah... Mubah: some say mubah is not included, but the correct view is that mubah is included in nafal... (al-Qamari) ...
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of the primary legal rulings ('azimah) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author begins by stating that legislated rulings are of two types: 'azimah (primary rulings based on original intent) and rukhsah (concessions due to exigencies). He then explains that 'azimah rulings are original, not dependent on contingencies like travel or illness. The commentary clarifies that 'azimah and rukhsah are opposites but can be related: the original ruling is 'azimah, and its change due to an excuse is rukhsah. The core of the lesson is the four-fold classification of 'azimah based on the consequences of denial, punishment for omission, and blame: (1) Fard: its denier becomes an unbeliever; (2) Wajib: its abandoner is punished but denier is not an unbeliever; (3) Sunnah: its abandoner is blameworthy but not punished; (4) Nafal: no blame or punishment for leaving, and it includes recommended and permissible acts. The commentary by al-Tahawi further subdivides fard into qat'i (definitive) and zanni (speculative), and into fard 'ayn (individual obligation) and fard kifayah (collective obligation). The passage also addresses potential objections: how haram and makruh fit into this scheme. It explains that haram (like drinking wine) is considered fard with respect to its abandonment (since its proof is definitive), and makruh tahriman (like eating a certain animal with ambiguous proof) is considered wajib with respect to its abandonment. Makruh tanzihan is included in sunnah because its avoidance is recommended. Mubah is included in nafal because it shares the characteristic of no blame or punishment. The author uses scholarly references like al-Qamari and al-Tahawi (from his commentary on al-Maraqi) to support these classifications. The overall purpose is to provide a precise taxonomy of the five legal categories (ahkam al-khamsah) as understood in the Hanafi school, emphasizing the distinctions between fard and wajib (based on certainty of the proof) and the inclusion of other categories.

Key Terms
فرض (fard): A ruling established by a definitive proof; its denier becomes an unbeliever. In this lesson, fard also includes the abandonment of haram.
واجب (wajib): A ruling established by a proof with some ambiguity; its abandoner is punished but denier is not an unbeliever. Here, it includes abandonment of makruh tahrimi.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act whose abandoner is blameworthy but not punished. Here, it includes avoidance of makruh tanzihi.
نفل (nafal): A voluntary act with no blame or punishment for omission. Here, it includes mubah (permissible acts).
حرام (haram): A prohibition established by definitive proof; its performance is sinful, its avoidance is fard.
مكروه تحريما (makruh tahrimi): A prohibitory ruling with some ambiguity in its proof; its performance is sinful but its avoidance is wajib.
مكروه تنزيها (makruh tanzihi): A disliked act whose avoidance is recommended (sunnah); its performance is not sinful but discouraged.
مباح (mubah): A permissible act with no legal preference; its doing or leaving is equal in terms of blame.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification in this passage, under which type of 'azimah is the avoidance of makruh tahrimi included?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah
D) Nafal

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school integrates all legal categories (haram, makruh, mubah) into the four-type 'azimah classification by focusing on the aspect of abandonment (tark), ensuring a complete and logical taxonomy.

Definition of Fard and Its Legal Implications
Defining fard and explaining its binding nature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of fard and distinguish it from wajib on the basis of proof certainty.

Core Idea
Fard is an obligation proven by decisive proof (qat'i) that admits no increase, decrease, or doubt.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar defines fard — the most fundamental category of legal obligation in the Hanafi school. It not only provides a precise definition but also addresses potential objections about what counts as fard, especially regarding prohibitions (haram) and permissible acts (mubah). Understanding this definition is essential because it determines the gravity of an act: denial of a fard leads to disbelief (kufr), while denial of a wajib does not. The passage also introduces the important Hanafi distinction between fard and wajib based on the certainty of the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the classification of rulings based on blame
The passage begins by dividing legal rulings into two: those whose abandonment invites blame (sunnah) and those that do not (nafil). Then it includes haram under fard and makruh under wajib by virtue of their abandonment being obligatory.
Note that 'blame' here is a technical term; sunnah abandonment is blameworthy but not sinful.
2
Analyze the definition of fard
Fard is defined as something that does not admit increase or decrease, established by a proof that has no uncertainty (shubhah). This definition excludes acts like nawafil and mubahat because they lack the quality of being a firm resolve (azimah). The examples given are the fixed numbers of rak'ats in prayer and days of fasting.
The phrase 'does not admit increase or decrease' refers to the essential nature of the act as prescribed, not to individual variation.
3
Understand the inclusion of haram in fard by abandonment
An objection is raised that the enumeration of fard as only four pillars leaves out haram and makruh tahrimi. The response is that haram is fard in terms of abandonment: abandoning a haram act is obligatory because its prohibition is proven by a decisive proof. Similarly, makruh tahrimi is wajib by abandonment.
This expands the concept of fard to include negative obligations (prohibitions).
4
Clarify the status of mubah
Another objection concerns the exclusion of mubah. The passage offers two answers: (1) mubah is not legislated in the sense of being a prescribed act; (2) the more correct view is that mubah falls under nafil because it shares the characteristic of not incurring blame for abandonment.
The second answer reconciles mubah within the classification without disrupting the original division.
5
Distinguish fard from wajib on proof certainty
The passage implies that fard is proven by a proof with no uncertainty (qat'i), while wajib is proven by a proof with some uncertainty (zanni). This is because the definition emphasizes 'no uncertainty' for fard, and by contrast, wajib's evidence (like ahad hadith) has some doubt.
This is a key Hanafi distinction not shared by the Shafi'i school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الأحكام المشروعة تاركه الملامة أو لا، فالأول هو السنة، والثاني هو النفل والحرام داخل في الفرض باعتبار الترك، وكذا المكروه في الواجب والمباح مما ليس بمشروع بالمعنى الذي قلنا. أي تحريما تعريف الفريضة وحكمها ] فالأول: فريضة وهي ما لا يحتمل زيادة ولا نقصانًا ثبتت بدليل لاشبهة فيه، فأعداد الركعات والصيامات وكيفيتهما كلها متعيّن بتعيين لا ازدياد فيه ولا نقصان، وثابت مقطوع لا يحتمل الشبهة ولا يقال إنه يتناول بعض المباحات والنوافل الثابتتين كذلك؛ لأن كلمة "ما" عبارة عن عزيمة معهودة لم يتناولها قطّ. كالإيمان والأركان الأربعة وهي الصلاة والزكاة والصوم والحج. والحرام إلخ: دفع دخل مقدر تقريره أن الحصر في الأربعة باطل لخروج الحرام والمكروه تحريما؟ وحاصل الدفع: أن الحرام كشرب الخمر داخل في الفرض بحسب الترك؛ فإن تركه فضل؛ لأن دليل الحرمة قطعي، والمراد بالفرض أعم من أن يكون فعله فرضًا أو تركه فرضًا والمكروه تحريما كأكل الضب داخل في الواجب بحسب الترك؛ فإن تركه واجب؛ إذ في دليله شبهة، والمراد بالواجب أعم من أن يكون فعله واجبًا أو تركه واجبا، بقى الكلام في المكروه تنزيها فأقول: إنه داخل في السنة؛ لأن ترك المكروه تنزيها سنة. (القمر) والمباح إلخ: دفع دخل مقدر تقريره: أن الحصر في الأربعة باطل لوجود قسم آخر سواها وهو المباح؟ وحاصل الدفع: أن المباح ليس بداخل في القسم؛ فإن المقسم هو المشروع بمعنى الذي شرعه الله تعالى لعباده كما قد مرّ آنفا من الشارح، والمباح ليس كذلك، وفيه أن هذا القول منسوب إلى بعض المعتزلة والأشهر عندنا أن المباح أيضا داخل في الحكم الشرعي بناءً على صدق تعريفه عليه، وهو خطاب الله تعالى المتعلّق بأفعال المكلفين اقتضاء أو تخييرا، فالأصوب أن يجاب عن الدخل بأن المباح داخل في النفل؛ فإن النفل على التقسيم المذكور هو الذي لا يكفّر جاحده ولا يعاقب بتركه ولا يستحق تاركه الملامة وهذا صادق على المباح أيضًا؛ فلا ينتقض الحصر لخروجه.(القمر) قلنا: أي الكفر عند الإنكار المعاقبة بالترك والملامة فريضة: قد عرفت المعنى اللغوي للفرض فتذكره. (القمر) بدليل لا شبهة فيه : الظاهر المتبادر من حيث إن وقوع النكرة تحت النفي يفيد العموم، أن الشبهة المنفية أعم أن تكون شبهة ناشئة من من دليل أو شبهة غير ناشئة من دليل القمر كذلك أي بدليل لا شبهة فيه، ولا يحتمل زيادةً ولا نقصانًا. (القمر) لأن إلخ: دليل لقوله : لا يقال إلخ. (القمر) كالإيمان: فإنه لا يزيد ولا ينقص في غير زمان الوحي وإن كان يزيد في زمان الوحي بزيادة متعلقاته. (القمر)
Chapter on the legislated rulings: one who abandons it is blamed or not. The first is the sunnah, and the second is the nafil. The haram is included in the fard with respect to abandonment, and likewise the makruh in the wajib. The mubah is not legislated in the sense we said (i.e., prohibited). Definition of fard and its ruling: The first is fard, which is that which does not admit increase or decrease, established by a proof that has no uncertainty in it. The numbers of rak'ats and fasts and their modalities are all determined by specification with no increase or decrease, and are definitively established without admitting uncertainty. It cannot be said that it includes some mubahat and nawafil that are also established likewise, because the word 'ma' refers to a known resolve that does not apply to them. Like iman and the four pillars: prayer, zakat, fasting, and hajj. 'And the haram etc.': This is to rebut an anticipated objection, namely that the enumeration of four is invalid because haram and makruh tahrimi are left out. The gist of the rebuttal: haram like drinking wine is included in fard in terms of abandonment; for abandoning it is virtuous, because the proof of its prohibition is decisive. By 'fard' is meant inclusive of whether its doing is fard or its abandonment is fard. Makruh tahrimi like eating a lizard is included in wajib in terms of abandonment; for abandoning it is wajib, since there is uncertainty in its proof. By 'wajib' is meant inclusive of whether its doing is wajib or its abandonment is wajib. As for makruh tanzihi, I say it is included in sunnah; for abandoning makruh tanzihi is sunnah. (al-Qamar) 'And the mubah etc.': This is to rebut an anticipated objection that the enumeration of four is invalid because there is another category, the mubah. The gist of the rebuttal: mubah is not included in the category; for the division is of the legislated in the sense of what Allah prescribed for His servants as the commentator mentioned earlier, and mubah is not that. There is also a saying attributed to some Mu'tazila, but the more famous view with us is that mubah is also included in the legal ruling based on the truth of its definition: it is the address of Allah relating to the actions of the legally responsible persons, whether as a demand or a choice. So the more correct answer to the objection is that mubah is included in nafil; for nafil according to the mentioned division is that whose denier is not declared an unbeliever, nor is its abandoner punished, nor is its abandoner blameworthy, and this applies to mubah as well; thus the enumeration is not invalidated by its exclusion. (al-Qamar) 'We said': i.e., disbelief upon denial, punishment for abandonment, and blame are for fard: you have known the linguistic meaning of fard, so remember it. (al-Qamar) 'By a proof that has no uncertainty in it': the apparent meaning from the fact that a indefinite noun in the context of negation implies generality is that the negated uncertainty is inclusive of uncertainty arising from a proof and uncertainty not arising from a proof. (al-Qamar) Likewise, i.e., by a proof that has no uncertainty in it and does not admit increase or decrease. (al-Qamar) 'Because etc.': evidence for his saying: 'it cannot be said etc.' (al-Qamar) 'Like iman': for it does not increase or decrease in other than the time of revelation, although it increases in the time of revelation by increase of its correlatives. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of fard (obligatory act). The author begins by classifying legal rulings according to the consequence of abandoning them: if abandonment is blameworthy, it is sunnah (commendable) or nafil (supererogatory) if not blameworthy. Then he defines fard: it is an obligation proven by a decisive proof (qat'i) admitting no increase or decrease. The examples given are the numbers of rak'ats in prayer and days of fasting — they are fixed exactly. The definition excludes mubah and nawafil because they are not 'azimah (firm resolve). Fard includes iman and the four pillars. The text then addresses objections: (1) Why are haram and makruh tahrimi not listed? Answer: They are considered fard/wajib in terms of prohibition — abandoning them is obligatory. (2) Why is mubah included? The commentator clarifies that mubah is not legislated in the sense of being a prescribed act; but some count it as part of legal rulings. The safest answer is that mubah falls under nafil because it shares the characteristic of not incurring blame for abandonment. Finally, the passage emphasizes that the decisive proof for fard must be free from any uncertainty (shubhah), and that fard does not increase or decrease.

Key Terms
الفريضة (al-farīḍah): ما لا يحتمل زيادة ولا نقصانًا ثبتت بدليل لا شبهة فيه
السنة (al-sunnah): ما تاركه يلام عليه شرعًا لكن ليس بواجب

B) Fard is mentioned in the Quran; wajib in the Sunnah.
C) Fard is for acts; wajib is for abandoning acts.

Key Takeaway
Fard is defined by a decisive, doubt-free proof and includes both positive obligations and mandatory abandonment of prohibitions.

Definition of Wajib and Its Legal Consequences
Defining wajib and detailing consequences of denial/abandonment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between fard and wajib in Hanafi usul and apply the ruling on those who deny or abandon wajib, determining when it constitutes kufr, fisq, or neither.

Core Idea
Wajib is proven by a proof with uncertainty; its denier is not automatically a kafir.

Wajib is a key category in Hanafi fiqh, falling between fard and sunnah in binding force. This lesson clarifies its definition, the role of shubhah (uncertainty) in its proof, and the nuanced consequences for those who deny or abandon it. You will learn why a person who rejects the obligation of udhiyah is treated differently from one who rejects prayer.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the definition of wajib
Understand that wajib is 'that which is established by a proof containing uncertainty (shubhah)'. Identify the types of proofs that yield uncertainty: a general text partially specified (amm makhsus), a mujmal (ambiguous) text, and a khabar al-wahid (solitary hadith).
The shubhah must arise from the proof itself, not from personal doubt.
2
Identify the examples: sadaqat al-fitr and udhiyah
These are classic examples of wajib in Hanafi fiqh. Both are proven by solitary hadith, which have zanni thubut. Recognize that their obligation is at the level of wajib, not fard.
3
Examine the proof for udhiyah
Review the hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari: the Prophet's command 'Whoever sacrificed before the prayer, let him sacrifice another...' This imperative indicates obligation, but because the hadith is a khabar al-wahid, the certainty is lowered.
The imperative 'فليذبح' is the operative phrase.
4
Analyze the ruling on deniers
The passage outlines a four-level hierarchy: (1) Denial of self-evident fard (e.g., prayer) → kafir. (2) Denial of non-self-evident fard with a decisive proof and no shubhah → fasiq if weak ta'wil, kafir if no ta'wil? Actually the text says with ta'wil even weak is fasiq not kafir. (3) Denial of a proof with shubhah not from the dalil → with ijtihad-based ta'wil: neither kafir nor fasiq; without ta'wil: fasiq. (4) Denial of wajib (which inherently has shubhah in its proof) → same as (3).
The key factor is whether the denial stems from a legitimate ijtihad-based interpretation.
5
Apply the ruling on abandoners
Abandoning wajib without an excuse and without contempt for the law makes one a fasiq. If the abandonment shows contempt (istikhfaf), it becomes kufr.
Contempt is distinguished from mere negligence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الأحكام المشروعة تعريف الواجب وحكمه] والثاني: واجب، وهو ما ثبت بدليل فيه شبهة كالعام المخصوص البعض، والمجمل، وخبر الواحد. كصدقة الفطر والأضحية، فإنهما ثبتا بخبر الواحد من حتى يكفر جاحده : هذا الحكم ليس على إطلاقه، بل الفرائض التي علم فرضيتها في الشريعة المحمدية بالبداهة لكل أحد المحق والمبطل، فجاحدها كافر ألبتة، وأما الفرائض التي ليست فرضيتها بديهية جليّة، فإن كانت قطعيةً بمعنى أنها ثبت بدليل لا شبهة فيه أصلاً، فمنكرها مؤوّلاً وإن كان التأويل ركيكًا ليس بكافر بل هو فاسق، ولذا قال قدماء المشايخ: لا نكفّر أحدا من أهل القبلة مادام يتشبث بالكتاب والسنة، وإن كانت قطعية بمعنى أنها ثبتت بدليل ليست فيه شبهة ناشية من دليل، وإن كان فيه شبهة غير ناشية من دليل، فمنكرها مؤوّلاً بالتأويل الاجتهادي ليس بكافر ولا فاسق وإن كان خاطئًا غير مؤوّل بالتأويل الاجتهادي فاسق ألبتة وليس بكافر كذا أفاد بحر العلوم (القمر) ويفسق تاركه لأن في المعصية خروجًا عن الطاعة، والفسق هو الخروج عن الشيء. ثم المراد من الترك الترك بغير الاستخفاف با لشرائع كفر كذا قيل. (القمر) واجب الوجوب في اللغة اللزوم، فلا يخفي وجه المناسبة. ما ثبت أي لزم على ذمة المكلّف، فلا يرد السنن والمستحبات والمباحات الثابتة بالدلائل التي فيها شبهة. (القمر) فيه أي في ثبوت ذلك الدليل أو في دلالة ذلك الدليل شبهة فالنص العام المخصوص البعض والمجمل والمؤوّل في دلالتها شبهة وخبر الواحد في ثبوته شبهة، والمراد بالشبهة في تعريف الواجب الشبهة الناشئة من الدليل. (القمر) بخبر الواحد قد مرّ حديث صدقة الفطر فتذكر. وأما حديث الأضحية فهو ما روى البخاري عن جندب بن عبد الله قال صلى النبي يوم النحر ، ثم خطب، ثم ذبح وقال: "من كان ذبح قبل أن يصلي فليذبح أخرى مكانها، ومن لم يذبح فليذبح باسم الله". (القمر)
Chapter on the legislated rulings: Definition of wajib and its ruling. The second is wajib: it is that which is established by a proof in which there is uncertainty (shubhah), such as the general text that has been specified in part, the ambiguous (mujmal), and the solitary report (khabar al-wahid). Like sadaqat al-fitr and adha, for they are established by a solitary report. 'To the extent that its denier is declared an unbeliever': This ruling is not absolute. Rather, the fara'id whose obligation is known in the Muhammadan Shari'ah as self-evident to everyone, both the right and the wrong, the denier of them is an unbeliever absolutely. As for the fara'id whose obligation is not self-evident, if they are qat'i in the sense that they are established by a proof with absolutely no uncertainty, then one who denies them with a interpretation (ta'wil), even if the interpretation is weak, is not an unbeliever but a transgressor (fasiq). Therefore the early shaykhs said: we do not declare any of the people of the qibla as unbelievers as long as they adhere to the Book and Sunnah. And if they are qat'i in the sense that they are established by a proof in which there is no uncertainty arising from the proof, even if there is uncertainty not arising from the proof, then one who denies them with an ijtihad-based interpretation is neither an unbeliever nor a transgressor, and if he is mistaken without ijtihad-based interpretation, he is a transgressor but not an unbeliever. Thus taught the Ocean of Knowledge (Bahr al-Uloom). (al-Qamar) 'And its abandoner is a transgressor': because disobedience is a departure from obedience, and fisq is departure from a thing. Then what is meant by abandonment is abandonment without belittling the laws; otherwise it would be kufr. (al-Qamar) 'Wajib': obligation in language means binding, so the appropriateness is not hidden. 'That which is established' means that which is binding upon the liability of the legally responsible person, so not including the sunan, mustahabbat, and mubahat that are established by proofs that contain uncertainty. (al-Qamar) 'In it' i.e., in the establishment of that proof or in the indication of that proof there is uncertainty. Thus the general text that is specified in part, the mujmal, and the mu'awwal all have uncertainty in their indication, and the solitary report has uncertainty in its establishment. What is meant by uncertainty in the definition of wajib is the uncertainty arising from the proof. (al-Qamar) 'By a solitary report': the hadith of sadaqat al-fitr has already been mentioned, so remember it. As for the hadith of adha, it is what al-Bukhari narrated from Jundub ibn 'Abdullah: The Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed on the day of Nahr, then gave a sermon, then sacrificed, and said: 'Whoever sacrificed before the prayer, let him sacrifice another in its place; and whoever did not sacrifice, let him sacrifice in the name of Allah.' (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage defines wajib (obligatory but with a lesser certainty) and discusses its binding nature. The author states that wajib is proven by a proof that contains some uncertainty (shubhah), such as a general text that has been partially specified, a mujmal (ambiguous) text, or a khabar al-wahid (solitary hadith). Examples are sadaqat al-fitr (zakat al-fitr) and udhiyah (sacrifice). The commentary then clarifies the ruling on the denier: not every denier of a fard is a kafir; only those whose fard is self-evident (like the five pillars) are rendered kafir. If the obligation is not self-evident but proven by a decisive proof, the denier with a weak interpretation is a fasiq, not a kafir. If the proof is decisive but there is some uncertainty not from the proof, the denier with an ijtihad-based interpretation is not even a fasiq. The passage also explains that the abandoner of wajib without an excuse is a fasiq, but if abandonment shows contempt for the religion, it becomes kufr. Finally, the source of the udhiyah hadith is cited: from Sahih al-Bukhari.

Key Terms
الواجب (al-wājib): ما ثبت بدليل فيه شبهة كالعام المخصوص والمجمل وخبر الواحد
الشبهة (al-shubhah): التردد في ثبوت الدليل أو دلالته، ناشئة من الدليل نفسه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition, a person who denies the obligation of udhiyah (sacrifice) based on a valid ijtihad-based interpretation (ta'wil ijtihādi) is considered:
A) Kafir
B) Fasiq
C) Neither kafir nor fasiq
D) No ruling

Key Takeaway
Wajib is a binding obligation with a lesser proof; its denier is not automatically a kafir, and its abandoner without contempt is a fasiq.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Definition and Ruling of Wajib
Definition of wajib with examples and its legal consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define wajib according to the Hanafi school, explain the concept of shubha in its proof, and distinguish between the rulings on denial and abandonment.

Core Idea
Wajib is an obligation proven by a proof with shubha; it is binding in practice but not in certain knowledge, so denial does not make one a kafir.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between fard and wajib based on the certainty of the proof. This lesson unpacks the definition of wajib, exploring how shubha (ambiguity) in the evidence, such as in khabar al-wahid, leads to a distinct legal category. Understanding this distinction prevents erroneous takfir and ensures correct application of rulings.

Guided Path
1
Parse the Definition
Break down the definition 'ما ثبت بدليل فيه شبهة'. Identify the three components: the obligation (wajib), its establishment (thubut), and the proof with shubha.
2
Identify Shubha Types
Distinguish between shubha in tannnus al-dalala (indication) and thubut (establishment). Recognize examples: 'amm makhsoos', 'mujmal', 'mu'awwal' for dalala, and 'khabar wahid' for thubut.
3
Analyze Examples
Apply the definition to sadaqat al-fitr and udhiyah. Explain why they are wajib, not fard, due to reliance on khabar al-wahid.
4
Extract the Ruling (Hukm)
Understand that wajib is binding in practice (luzum 'amalan) but not in certain knowledge. Note the consequences: no takfir for denial, but tafsiq for abandonment without excuse, and exception for legitimate ta'wil.

فصل في الأحكام المشروعة
تعريف الواجب وحكمه
والثاني: واجب، وهو ما ثبت بدليل فيه شبهة كالعام المخصوص البعض، والمجمل، وخبر الواحد. كصدقة الفطر والأضحية، فإنهما ثبتا بخبر الواحد.
فيه أي في ثبوت ذلك الدليل أو في دلالة ذلك الدليل شبهة فالنص العام المخصوص البعض والمجمل والمؤوّل في دلالتها شبهة وخبر الواحد في ثبوته شبهة، والمراد بالشبهة في تعريف الواجب الشبهة الناشئة من الدليل.
وحكمه اللزوم عملاً لا علمًا على اليقين فهو مثل الفرض في العمل دون العلم. حتى لا يكفّر جاحده لعدم العلم. ويفسق تاركه إذا استخف بأخبار الآحاد بأن لا يرى العمل بها واجبًا لا أن يتهاون بها؛ فإن التهاون بالشريعة كفر، وإنما خص أخبار الآحاد بالذكر اعتبارا للغالب لا لأن الواجب لا يثبت إلا بأخبار الآحاد.
فأما متأوّلاً فلا أي فأما ترك العمل بأخبار الآحاد بطريق التأويل بأن يقول: هذا الخبر ضعيف أو غريب أو مخالف للكتاب فلا يفسق فيه؛ لأن هذا ليس للهوى والشهوة، بل مما توارث به العلماء لأجل الدقة والفطانة.
Chapter on the prescribed rulings. Definition of wajib and its ruling. The second: wajib, and it is what is established by a proof in which there is shubha, like the general text that is partially specified, the mujmal, and khabar al-wahid. Like sadaqat al-fitr and udhiyah, for they are established by khabar al-wahid. In it (i.e., in the establishment of that proof or in the indication of that proof) there is shubha. So the general text that is partially specified, the mujmal, and the mu'awwal have shubha in their indication, and khabar al-wahid has shubha in its establishment. The meaning of shubha in the definition of wajib is the shubha arising from the proof. Its ruling is bindingness in practice, not in knowledge with certainty, so it is like fard in practice without knowledge. Thus its denier is not declared an unbeliever due to lack of certain knowledge. And its abandoner is a transgressor if he belittles akhbar al-ahad by not considering acting upon them obligatory, not if he is negligent about them; for negligence about the Sharia is disbelief. He specifically mentioned akhbar al-ahad only considering the majority (of cases), not because wajib can only be established by akhbar al-ahad. As for one who interprets (i.e., does not act on khabar al-wahid due to interpretation by saying this hadith is weak or rare or contradicts the Book), then he is not a transgressor, because this is not due to desire or lust, but rather it is something transmitted by scholars for the sake of precision and intelligence.
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling of the Hanafi legal category 'wajib'. The author states that wajib is the second category (after fard), defined as an obligation proven by a proof containing shubha. Shubha here means ambiguity arising from the proof itself, either in its establishment (thubut) or its indication (dalala). Examples of such proofs are: a general text that has been partially specified (al-amm al-makhsoos al-ba'd), a mujmal text, a mu'awwal text, or a khabar al-wahid. The author gives sadaqat al-fitr and udhiyah as examples of wajib acts proven by khabar al-wahid. The ruling (hukm) of wajib is that it is binding in practice (luzum 'amalan) but not with certain knowledge ('ilman), unlike fard which is certain. Therefore, one who denies a wajib is not declared an unbeliever (kafir) because the proof is not certain. However, one who abandons a wajib without a valid excuse is a transgressor (fasiq), provided he does not belittle the proof. Belittling the Sharia is kufr. The author clarifies that failure to act due to legitimate interpretation (ta'wil) does not make one fasiq, as it is a scholarly exercise. The passage guards against extremes: not declaring takfir for denial of non-certain obligations, yet ensuring respect for wajib acts.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): ما ثبت بدليل فيه شبهة
شبهة (shubha): التردد بين الحظر والإباحة أو عدم الجزم في الدليل
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): الحديث الذي لم يبلغ التواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition, why is the denier of a wajib not declared an unbeliever (kafir)?
A) Because wajib is not obligatory in practice.
B) Because the proof for wajib contains shubha and does not provide certain knowledge.
C) Because wajib is abrogated.
D) Because the denier is always a mujtahid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, wajib is an obligation proven by a proof with shubha; it is binding in practice but not certain in knowledge, so denial does not befit kufr, but abandonment without excuse is fisq.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

The Hanafi Concept of Wajib and Its Evidentiary Basis
Defines wajib and its ruling, emphasizing the role of speculative evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define wajib according to the Hanafi school and explain how its ruling differs from fard in terms of certainty and consequence for denier and abandoner, especially when based on khabar wahid.

Core Idea
Wajib binds action but not belief – its denier is not a kafir, but its abandoner without valid interpretation is a fasiq.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi definition of wajib (obligatory) and its legal implications. The key distinction from fard lies in epistemological certainty: wajib demands action but does not require firm belief in its proof, allowing for speculative evidence like khabar wahid. The passage also clarifies the nuance of sin and disbelief when one abandons or denies a wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Definition
Isolate the sentence defining wajib: it is binding in action (luzum amalan) but not in knowledge (la ilman). This distinguishes it from fard, which requires both.
The phrase 'la ilman' indicates no certainty in belief, only in performance.
2
Analyze the Consequence of Denial
Understand that the denier of a wajib (jahid) is not declared kafir because the proof may not be definitive. Contrast with fard, where denial leads to kufr.
The text specifies 'la yakaffar jahiduhu li-adam al-ilm'.
3
Examine the Condition for Fisq
A person becomes fasiq only if he abandons wajib with disdain (istikhfaf) for ahad hadith by rejecting their obligatory nature. Neglect without disdain is not fisq.
Ijtihadi interpretation (ta'wil) excuses one from fisq, as in claims of weakness or contradiction.
4
Distinguish Shubha in Proof and Indication
Recognize that shubha (ambiguity) can affect either the proof's establishment (thubut) or its meaning (dalala). The witr prayer example illustrates both: the hadith is khabar wahid (shubha in thubut) and its wording may imply recommendation (shubha in dalala).
This nuanced approach justifies why wajib can be based on speculative evidence.
5
Generalize the Scope of Wajib Proofs
Note that wajib is not confined to ahad hadith; it can be established by general texts (amm makhsus), mujmal, qiyas, etc. The focus on ahad hadith is due to prevalence, not exclusivity.
The text says 'la li-anna al-wajib la yathbutu illa bi-akhbar al-ahad'.

Chapter on Prescribed Rulings. That which contains shubha, so both become wajib. Definition of Wajib and its ruling: Its ruling is necessity in action, not knowledge with certainty, so it is like fard in action but not in knowledge. Hence its denier is not declared kafir due to lack of certainty. And its abandoner becomes a fasiq if he shows disdain for ahad hadith by not considering action upon them obligatory, not by neglecting them; for neglect of the Sharia is kufr. Ahad hadith are specifically mentioned due to prevalence, not because wajib is only established by ahad hadith. That is, by ijtihadi interpretation. As for one who interprets, no: abandoning action upon ahad hadith through interpretation, saying this hadith is weak or strange or contradictory to the Book, he does not become fasiq; because this is not due to desire and lust, but something scholars inherited for the sake of precision and intelligence. That is, interpretation. In it, that it is considered shubha; shubha may be in the proof's establishment or its indication, like witr: it is wajib due to his saying: 'For you from the red camels is witr,' narrated by Tirmidhi. This is a khabar wahid, so in its establishment there is shubha. 'Indeed Allah supplied you with a prayer which is better than red camels.' And if established, its indication also has shubha; it may mean increase in voluntary prayer. (al-Qamar) 'not knowledge, etc': rather it is strong probability, not based on definitive proof. (al-Qamar) Like fard, its abandoner deserves punishment. (al-Qamar) 'and becomes fasiq, etc': because obligation of acting upon khabar wahid is established by definitive proofs, so whoever does not consider it obligatory is definitely a fasiq. (al-Qamar) 'by not considering, etc': explanation of disdain for ahad hadith. Then it was objected that declaring fasiq does not depend on disdain in this sense; because one who abandons action upon khabar wahid while considering it obligatory is also a fasiq. So apparent meaning is the abandonment with disdain, without interpretation. This fits his later statement: 'as for one who interprets, etc. (al-Qamar) 'by the Sharia': even if narrated via ahad. (al-Qamar) 'due to prevalence': for most obligatory acts are established by ahad hadith, not because wajib is only established by them; it is also established by general text specified in part, or mujmal, etc. (al-Qamar) 'this hadith is weak, etc': Know that sahih hadith is what is established by a reliable, fully precise narrator, not defective or irregular; weak is what lacks conditions of sahih, all or some; gharib is a sahih hadith with only one narrator. This is what the muḥaddith Shaykh al-Dahlawī 'Abd al-Haqq said, and details are in the field of hadith terminology. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of 'wajib' (obligatory) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author explains that wajib is binding in action but not in belief (like fard). Thus, denying a wajib does not make one a kafir if based on ijtihad, but abandoning it without valid interpretation leads to fisq. The discussion centers on ahad hadith as proofs for wajib; showing disdain for them by rejecting their obligatory nature is fisq, but interpreting them away (e.g., claiming weakness) is not. The text also clarifies that wajib can be established by various forms of evidence, not just ahad hadith. A example is given: the witr prayer is wajib based on a hadith that has shubha in its chain and meaning.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): An act whose performance is demanded in a binding manner, but its proof may be speculative; unlike fard which is definitive in belief.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A hadith narrated by one or a few individuals, not reaching tawatur, providing speculative knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He becomes a kafir.

C) He is not sinful.
D) He is rewarded for his ijtihad.

Key Takeaway
Wajib is an obligation in action only, not in belief, and its abandonment only incurs fisq when done with disdain for the proof, not with valid ijtihadi interpretation.

Definition and Ruling of Sunnah in Hanafi Usul
Defines sunnah and clarifies its ruling, distinguishes sunnat al-huda, and addresses a madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sunnah according to the Hanafi school, distinguish between sunnat al-huda and sunan al-zawa'id, and apply the Hanafi position that the term 'sunnah' extends to the practices of the Companions and others.

Core Idea
Sunnah is a requested path in religion, not obligatory; it includes both prophetic and non-prophetic practices that are good.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar defines sunnah, a key legal category between fard and nafl. The Hanafi school holds that sunnah is a recommended act that one is asked to perform without being sinful for omitting. A crucial distinction is made between sunnat al-huda (confirmed sunnah related to worship) and sunan al-zawa'id (habitual actions). The passage also addresses a dispute with al-Shafi'i over whether 'sunnah' can refer to the practices of the Companions. Understanding this definition and its scope is foundational for usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal category
Recognize that sunnah is the third category after fard and wajib. It is a requested path in religion.
2
Understand the definition's components
Break down the definition: 'a path followed in religion' and 'one is requested to perform it without it being fard or wajib'.
3
Distinguish sunnat al-huda from sunan al-zawa'id
Note that the definition strictly applies to sunnat al-huda (e.g., adhan, jama'ah) which are demanded in religion, not to habitual actions.
4
Examine the scope dispute
Learn the Hanafi position that the term 'sunnah' can apply to non-prophetic practices, supported by the hadith 'Whoever establishes a good sunnah' and the statement of Ali.
5
Evaluate the practical impact
Understand that this disagreement affects which practices are classified as sunnah, e.g., the sunnah of the caliphs is considered sunnah by Hanafis.

تعريف السنة وحكمها
والثالث : سنة، وهي الطريقة المسلوكة في الدين، وحكمها أن يطالب المرء بإقامتها من غير افتراض ولا وجوب فاحترز بقوله أن يطالب عن النفل، وبقوله: "من غير افتراض ولا وجوب" عن الفرض والواجب، وكان ينبغي أن يذكر هذه القيودات في التعريف، إلا أنه اكتفى عنها بالحكم، ولكن قالوا: إن هذا التعريف والحكم لا يصدقان إلا على سنة الهدى، والتقسيم الآتي إنما هو لمطلق السنة.

(القمر) هذاه القيودات أي كونها مطالبًا بها، وكون مطالبتها غير مطالبة الفرض والواجب. (القمر) ولكن قالوا إلخ لما كان يتوهم من الكلام السابق أن التعريف المذكور والحكم المسطور لمطلق السنة دفعه الشارح بقوله : ولكن قالوا إلخ (القمر) إلا على سنة الهدى فإنها طريقة مسلوكة في الدين ومطالب بها، وأما سنن الزوائد فمسلوكة على وجه العادة لا العبادة. (القمر) والتقسيم الآتي إلخ: دفع دخل مقدر تقريره أن هذا التعريف والحكم لما لم يصدقا إلا على سنة الهدى فكيف يصح تقسيم هذه السنة فيما سيأتي إلى نوعين سنة الهدى وسنن الزوائد؟ وحاصل الدفع: أن التقسيم الآتي ليس تقسيما لهذه السنة، بل هو تقسيم لمطلق السنة، وإليه أشار الشارح له فيما سيأتي بقوله: لمطلق السنة إلخ. (القمر) لمطلق السنة إلخ سواء كانت سنة الهدى أو سنة زائدة (السنبلي) إلا أن السنة إلخ توضيحه أنه لا خلاف بيننا و بين الشافعي له في تعريف السنة وحكمها المذكورين، إنما الخلاف بيننا و بينه أن لفظ السنة إذا أطلق هل يطلق على طريقة غير النبي ل أو لا؟ الثاني مختاره، والأول مختارنا، ودليلنا: قوله عليه من" سن سنةً حسنةً فله أجرها و أجر من عمل بها" فإن كلمة "من" تعمّ الناس. (القمر) وغيره إلخ أي لا خلاف في نفسها وحكمها، إنما الخلاف في إطلاقها، فعندنا يقع على طريقة النبي كما قال علي عليكم بسنتي وسنة الخلفاء الراشدين. (السنبلي)
وغيره
Chapter on Prescribed Rulings. Definition of Sunnah and its ruling. The third is sunnah: it is the path followed in religion. Its ruling is that one is requested to perform it without it being fard or wajib. He distinguished by his saying 'requested' from nafl, and by 'without fard or wajib' from fard and wajib. It would have been better to mention these restrictions in the definition, but he sufficed with them in the ruling. However, they said: this definition and ruling apply only to sunnat al-huda, while the upcoming division is for absolute sunnah. Except that the term sunnah applies to the way of the Prophet and others, meaning the Companions. (al-Qamar) 'It is the path followed, etc': that is, besides fard and wajib; the evidence for this restriction is that sunnah is contrasted with fard and wajib. What is meant by 'the path followed' is the good path that the Prophet and Companions followed, and one is requested to follow it. (al-Qamar) 'He is requested, etc': due to His saying: 'Whatever the Messenger gives you, take it, and whatever he forbids you, abstain from it' (59:7). (al-Qamar) 'without fard, etc': that is, the request is not like the request of fard and wajib such that its abandoner deserves punishment. (al-Qamar) 'these restrictions': that it is something requested, and its request is not like the request of fard and wajib. (al-Qamar) 'But they said, etc': because from the previous speech it might be misunderstood that the mentioned definition and ruling are for absolute sunnah, so the commentator rejected this by saying 'but they said, etc'. (al-Qamar) 'except on sunnat al-huda': for it is a path followed in religion and one is requested to follow it. As for sunan al-zawa'id, they are followed as a matter of habit, not worship. (al-Qamar) 'And the upcoming division, etc': to repudiate a presumed objection: that this definition and ruling apply only to sunnat al-huda, so how can it be correct to divide this sunnah into two types: sunnat al-huda and sunan al-zawa'id? The sum of the repudiation is that the upcoming division is not a division of this sunnah, but a division of absolute sunnah. The commentator pointed to this by his later statement: 'for absolute sunnah, etc'. (al-Qamar) 'for absolute sunnah, etc': whether sunnat al-huda or sunan al-zawa'id. (al-Sunbuli) 'Except that sunnah, etc': clarification that there is no dispute between us and al-Shafi'i regarding the definition and ruling of sunnah; rather, the dispute is whether the word 'sunnah' when used absolutely applies to the way of other than the Prophet or not? The second is his choice, the first is our choice. Our evidence: his saying: 'Whoever establishes a good sunnah has its reward and the reward of those who act upon it.' The word 'who' encompasses people. (al-Qamar) 'And other than him, etc': that is, no dispute regarding its essence and ruling, only dispute in its application; for us, it applies to the Prophet's way, as he said: 'Stick to my sunnah and the sunnah of the rightly guided caliphs.' (al-Sunbuli) And other than him.
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage defines 'sunnah' and clarifies its ruling. Sunnah is a recommended path in religion; one is requested to perform it, but it is not fard or wajib. The commentator highlights that the definition and ruling strictly apply to 'sunnat al-huda' (confirmed sunnah), not to 'sunan al-zawa'id' (additional sunnah like the Prophet's habits). An important point of dispute with al-Shafi'i is whether the term 'sunnah' can be applied to the practices of others besides the Prophet; the Hanafi school holds that it can, based on the hadith 'Whoever establishes a good sunnah...' and the saying of Ali regarding the sunnah of the caliphs. This passage thus explains both the legal category of sunnah and the scope of its application.

Key Terms
سنة الهدى (sunnat al-huda): The confirmed sunnah (like adhan and jama'ah) that is demanded in religion, as opposed to sunnan al-zawa'id which are habitual.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended path in religion, less than wajib; one is requested to follow it without being sinful for abandoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is an example of sunnat al-huda?
A) The Prophet's method of eating
B) The call to prayer (adhan)
C) The Prophet's way of sleeping
D) The Prophet's style of dressing

Key Takeaway
Sunnah is a demanded but non-obligatory act; its definition applies primarily to worship-related sunnah, and Hanafis extend the term to include good practices of the Companions.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
