Definition of Nafil and Its Hanafi Ruling: Obligation to Complete Once Begun
Usul definition with inter-madhhab proof and debate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the definition of nafil, explain the Hanafi proof for obligatory completion using Quran and qiyas, and evaluate the Shafi'i counterargument.

Core Idea
Starting a nafil act creates a binding commitment to complete it; abandoning it invalidates the part already performed.

What should a worshipper do if they begin a voluntary prayer but then wish to stop? The Hanafi school holds that once started, a nafil act becomes wajib to complete. This lesson examines the definition of nafil, the evidence for this ruling, and the inter-madhhab debate with the Shafi'i school. The key concept is siyana (preservation) of the performed portion.

Guided Path
1
Define nafil and its initial legal status
State the definition of nafil as a voluntarily initiated act that is rewarded if done and not punished if omitted. Note that this is the baseline ruling before any commencement.
Definition: 'yuqabu 'ala fi'lihi wa la yu'aqabu 'ala tarkihi'.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position
Understand the opposing view: since nafil is voluntarily begun, it should remain voluntary throughout; no new obligation arises upon starting. The principle is 'al-baqa' la yukhalif al-ibtida'' (continuation does not differ from commencement).
Shafi'i: no obligation to complete nor qada if spoiled.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof: Quran 47:33
Analyze the verse 'Do not invalidate your deeds' (Surah Muhammad 47:33). The Hanafi argument is that not completing a started nafil invalidates the portion already performed, which is prohibited. Classify this text as amm (general) and apply the usul principle: al-amm yufidu al-wujub.
Dalalat al-amm qat'iyya in Hanafi usul.
4
Apply qiyas to nadhr (vow) and ijma on hajj/umrah
Commencement of nafil is analogized to a verbal vow (nadhr): just as a vow makes the act wajib, starting a nafil creates a similar commitment to Allah. Strengthened by consensus on completing nafil hajj and umrah to preserve the ihram.
Analogy: asl = nadhr, illa = commitment to Allah, far' = shuru' fi al-nafl.
5
Derive the final Hanafi ruling
Synthesize the evidence: completion of a started nafil is wajib; if spoiled, qada is wajib. This is the mufta bihi position, deriving from siyana (preservation) of the act already performed.
Ruling: wajib al-ittimam; qada required upon ifsad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الأحكام المشروعة تعريف النفل وحكمه والزائد على الركعتين للمسافر نفل لهذا المعنى، أنه يُثاب على فعله ولا يُعاقب على تركه ولا يقال: إنه يخالف ما ذكر الفقهاء أنه لو صلّى أربعًا وقعد على الركعتين تم فرضه وأساء؛ لأن هذه الإساءة ليست باعتبار نفس الركعتين، بل لتأخير السلام واختلاط النفل بالفرض. وقال الشافعي له: لما شرع النفل على هذا الوصف وجب أن يبقى كذلك يعني أنه لا يلزم في حال البقاء كما كان لم يلزم قبل الابتداء، فإن شرع في النفل لا يلزم إتمامه، ولو أفسده لا يلزم قضاؤه، سواء كان صومًا أو صلاةً. قلنا: إن ما أدّاه وجبت صيانته ولا سبيل إليها إلا بإلزام الباقي؛ لأن الصلاة والصوم يفوت حكمه إلا إذا كان تامًا بكونه شفعًا أو صوم يوم، فإن أدى بعض الصلاة أو الصوم فعليه أن يُتمّه، وإلا يلزم إبطال عمله، وهو حرام؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلا تُبْطِلُوا أَعْمَالَكُمْ﴾ (محمد: 33) وإن أفسده يجب أن يقضيه؛ وذلك لقول عمر: صلاة المسافر ركعتان وصلاة الفجر ركعتان، وصلاة الضحى ركعتان على لسان نبيكم ولما كان صلاة المسافر ركعتين فالزائد عليها نفل كالزائد على ركعتي الفجر، وهذه الزيادة وإن كانت مكروهة، لكنها لما كانت صلاة وهي في نفسها مشروعة، لهذا يُثاب عليها، والكراهة من وجه آخر. هذا حاصل ما قال في "التنوير". ثم قال: ولكن بقاء الشيء لا يخالف ابتداءه، ولنا أن نمنع هذا. لم يلزم قبل الابتداء: لأن بقاء الشيء لا يخالف ابتداءه، وترك ما ليس واجبًا على العبد لا يسمى إبطالاً له فلا يضمن بالقضاء كالمظنون والنذر التزام فلا يعتبر به الشروع، وهما كالكفالة والقرض من "الدائر". وجبت صيانته أي عن البطلان لأن ما أدّي صار لله تعالى مسلما بنية القربة ألا ترى أنه لو مات كان مثاباً على ذلك القدر. بعض الصلاة أي التحريمة وما بعدها. لتكون فيه صيانة ولا يقال ليس فيه إبطال العمل بل امتناع عنه؛ لأنا نقول: إن الأجزاء المؤدية لما كان له عُرضة أن تصير عبادة بعد التمام، ولم يتمها فكأنه أبطلها. وهو كالنذر صار الله تسميةً لا فعلاً، أي الشروع مقيس على النذر؛ لأن النذر صار الله تعالى من حيث الذكر لا من حيث الفعل بأن قال: لله علي أن أصلي ركعتين. ثم لما وجب لصيانته ابتداء الفعل أي ثم وجب لصيانة هذا الذكر ابتداء الفعل بإجماع بيننا وبينكم، فإذا وجب لتعظيم ذكر اسم الله تعالى ابتداء الفعل في النذر بالاتفاق، فَلأَنْ يجب لصيانة ابتداء الفعل بقاؤه أولى بالاهتمام والدوام؛ لأن الدوام أسهل من الابتداء في اليسر، والفعل أولى من التسمية في الاهتمام. لتكون فيه صيانة أي لئلا يبطل الجزء المؤدّى، ألا ترى أن إتمام الحج النفل والعمرة واجب بالاتفاق؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَتِمُّوا الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ لِلَّهِ﴾ (البقرة: 196) وليس هذا الوجوب إلا لصيانة الإحرام، فكذا يجب الإتمام لصيانة الجزء الأوّل من آية عبادة، كانت وبالإفساد يلزم القضاء.
Chapter on Legal Rulings: Definition of Nafil and Its Ruling. The extra beyond two rak'ahs for the traveler is nafil in this sense: that he is rewarded for performing it and not punished for abandoning it. And it is not said that it contradicts what the jurists mentioned: that if he prayed four and sat after two rak'ahs, his obligatory prayer is complete and he commits wrong; because this wrongness is not due to the two rak'ahs themselves, but due to delaying the salutation and mixing the nafil with the obligatory. Al-Shafi'i said to him: When nafil is legislated with this description, it must remain as such, meaning it is not binding in the state of continuation just as it was not binding before commencement. So if one begins a nafil, its completion is not obligatory, and if he spoils it, its qada is not obligatory, whether fasting or prayer. We said: What he has performed must be preserved, and there is no way to do so except by binding him to complete the rest; because prayer and fasting lose their ruling unless they are complete, being an even number or a full day's fast. So if one performs part of prayer or fasting, he must complete it; otherwise he would be invalidating his deed, which is forbidden due to His saying: "Do not invalidate your deeds" (Muhammad 33). And if he spoils it, he must make it up, due to the saying of Umar: "The traveler's prayer is two rak'ahs, the dawn prayer is two rak'ahs, and the forenoon prayer is two rak'ahs, upon the tongue of your Prophet." Since the traveler's prayer is two rak'ahs, what is beyond that is nafil, like the extra beyond the two rak'ahs of dawn. This extra, though disliked, is a prayer and in itself legislated, so he is rewarded for it, and the dislike is from another aspect. This is the summary of what "al-Tanwir" said. Then he said: But the continuation of a thing does not differ from its commencement, and we can deny this. It was not binding before commencement: because continuation differs from commencement, and abandoning what is not obligatory on the servant is not called invalidation, so he does not owe qada, like a mistaken [act]; and a vow is a commitment, so commencement is not considered by it; both are like suretyship and loan from "al-Da'ir". Preservation is necessary, meaning from nullification, because what has been performed becomes for Allah, delivered with the intention of drawing near—do you not see that if he died, he would be rewarded for that amount? 'Part of prayer' means the tahrima and beyond. For it to have preservation, and it is not said there is no invalidation of action but rather abstention from it; because we say: The parts performed, since they are susceptible to becoming worship after completion, and he did not complete them, it is as if he invalidated them. It is like a vow: it becomes Allah's by name not by action, meaning commencement is analogized to a vow; because the vow becomes Allah's verbally not actually, by saying: "For Allah I must pray two rak'ahs." Then when for its preservation the beginning of the action became obligatory, I mean for the preservation of this verbal mention, the beginning of the action became obligatory by consensus between us and you. So if to honor the mention of Allah's name the beginning of action is obligatory in the vow by agreement, then to preserve the beginning of action, its continuation is more deserving of care and permanence; because continuation is easier than commencement, and action is more deserving than naming. For it to have preservation, i.e., lest the part performed be invalidated. Do you not see that completing the nafil hajj and umrah is obligatory by consensus, due to His saying: "Complete the hajj and umrah for Allah" (al-Baqarah 196)? And this obligation is only to preserve the ihram. So likewise, completion must be obligatory to preserve the first part of worship, and by spoiling it, qada becomes obligatory.
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage is a commentary defining nafil (supererogatory acts) and establishing the Hanafi ruling that once a nafil act is begun, it becomes obligatory to complete it. The text first defines nafil as an act for which one is rewarded but not punished for omitting (i.e., mandub). It then addresses a potential objection: that a traveler who prays four rak'ahs but sits after two has fulfilled his fard (obligatory prayer) but is sinful—the sin is not for the extra two rak'ahs but for delaying the salutation and mixing nafil with fard. The text then presents the Shafi'i position: since nafil is voluntarily begun, it should remain voluntary throughout; neither completion nor qada (make-up) of a spoiled nafil is required. The Hanafi response uses two proofs: first, the Quranic verse 47:33 prohibits invalidating one's deeds; having started a nafil, not completing it would invalidate the part already done, which is haram. Second, qiyas (analogy) to a nadhr (vow): if one says 'I vow to pray two rak'ahs,' the act becomes wajib. Similarly, starting a nafil makes the remaining part like a vow—the intention of starting creates a right of Allah over the worshiper. The text strengthens this analogy by noting that completing a nafil hajj/umrah is obligatory by consensus (based on 2:196) to preserve the ihram. Thus, preservation of the performed part requires completing the rest. The Shafi'i argument that continuation should mirror commencement is dismissed because the need to preserve what is already offered imposes a new obligation. This is a fundamental Hanafi usul principle: shuru' (commencement) is weighed with nadhr (vow) in terms of creating a liability.

Key Terms
النفل (al-nafl): Supererogatory worship; rewarded if performed, not punished if omitted, but obligatory to complete once begun.
صيانة (siyana): Preservation of the validity of a partially performed act of worship by completing it.
النذر (al-nadhr): A vow to perform an act of worship, making it obligatory even if originally nafil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul in this passage, what is the primary evidence for obligating completion of nafil?
A) Qiyas to hajj only
B) Quran 47:33 alone
C) Quran 47:33 and qiyas to nadhr
D) Consensus of the Sahaba

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, commencing a nafil act generates a binding obligation to complete it, based on the prohibition of invalidating deeds (Quran 47:33) and analogy to vows.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Obligation to Complete a Supererogatory Act: Qiyas on Nadhr
Deriving obligation to complete supererogatory act via qiyas on nadhr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi derivation of the obligation to complete a supererogatory act by applying qiyas to nadhr, and identify the textual evidence from Quran 2:196.

Core Idea
Starting a supererogatory act creates a binding obligation to complete it, analogous to a vow.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the ruling that a supererogatory (nafl) act must be completed once started is derived through a careful analogical reasoning (qiyas) on the vow (nadhr). This lesson unpacks the derivation chain, the effective cause (illah), and the Quranic support from the command to complete Hajj and Umrah. Understanding this process will sharpen your ability to trace Hanafi rulings back to their proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling under derivation
The claim is that it is wajib to complete any supererogatory act once initiated, and if invalidated, qada (make-up) is required.
This goes beyond the obligatory acts (fard); it concerns voluntary worship.
2
Locate the base case (asl) for qiyas
The base case is the vow (nadhr). When a person says 'For Allah upon me that I pray two rak'ahs', it becomes wajib by verbal dedication.
The vow creates an obligation by utterance (tasmīyah), not by the act itself.
3
Extract the effective cause (illah)
The illah is the 'protection' (siyānah) of the dedication to Allah—once something is consecrated to Allah, it must be completed to preserve that consecration.
In nadhr, the utterance itself creates the right of Allah; in nafl, the initial act (first part) creates that right.
4
Apply the illah to the new case (far')
When a person starts a nafl act, the first part (e.g., the first rak'ah of a voluntary prayer) becomes dedicated to Allah. To protect that dedication, completion becomes wajib, just as in nadhr.
This reasoning shows that continuity (al-dawām) is easier than initiation (al-ibtidāʾ) in the vow, but here both are analogous.
5
Confirm with supporting textual evidence
The verse 'And complete the Hajj and 'Umrah for Allah' (2:196) is cited. That obligation arises from protecting the ihram, the initial consecration. The same principle applies to any supererogatory act.
The verse is qaṭʿī al-thubūt but ẓannī al-dalāla; the Hanafi school interprets it as a general command to complete what is begun in worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الأحكام المشروعة. تعريف النفل وحكمه. لتكون فيه صيانة ولا يقال ليس فيه إبطال العمل بل امتناع عنه؛ لأنا نقول: إن الأجزاء المؤدية لما كان له عُرضة أن تصير عبادة بعد التمام، ولم يتمها فكأنه أبطلها. وهو كالنذر صار الله تسميةً لا فعلاً، أي الشروع مقيس على النذر؛ لأن النذر صار الله تعالى من حيث الذكر لا من حيث الفعل بأن قال: لله علي أن أصلي ركعتين. ثم لما وجب لصيانته ابتداء الفعل بإجماع بيننا وبينكم، فإذا وجب لتعظيم ذكر اسم الله تعالى ابتداء الفعل في النذر بالاتفاق، فَلأَنْ يجب لصيانة ابتداء الفعل بقاؤه أولى بالاهتمام والدوام؛ لأن الدوام أسهل من الابتداء في اليسر، والفعل أولى من التسمية في الاهتمام. ألا ترى أن إتمام الحج النفل والعمرة واجب بالاتفاق؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَتِمُّوا الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ لِلَّهِ﴾ [البقرة: 196] وليس هذا الوجوب إلا لصيانة الإحرام، فكذا يجب الإتمام لصيانة الجزء الأوّل من آية عبادة، كانت وبالإفساد يلزم القضاء.
Chapter on prescribed rulings. Definition of supererogatory act and its ruling. So that there is protection in it, and it is not said that there is invalidation of the action but rather abstention from it; for we say: The performed parts, since they are susceptible to becoming worship after completion, and if he does not complete them, it is as if he invalidated them. And it is like a vow, making it a verbal designation not an actual act, meaning initiation is measured analogically to a vow; because the vow makes it a designation to Allah in terms of utterance not in terms of action, by saying: For Allah upon me that I pray two rak'ahs. Then when the initiation of the act became obligatory for its protection by consensus between us and you, so when the initiation of the act became obligatory for the glorification of mentioning the name of Allah in the vow by agreement, then that the continuation of the initiation of the act should be obligatory for its protection is more deserving of concern and continuity; because continuity is easier than initiation in ease, and the act is more deserving than the designation in concern. Do you not see that completing the supererogatory Hajj and 'Umrah is obligatory by agreement due to His statement: 'And complete the Hajj and 'Umrah for Allah' [al-Baqarah 2:196], and this obligation is only for the protection of ihram, so likewise completion is obligatory for the protection of the first part of an act of worship, and by nullification, making up is required.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage is an istinbat (derivation of a ruling) concerning a supererogatory (nafl) act. The main claim is that once a person begins a nafl act of worship (e.g., prayer, Hajj), it becomes obligatory (wajib) to complete it. The reasoning is through qiyas (analogy) on a vow (nadhr). In a vow, the person verbally dedicates an act to Allah, making it obligatory to fulfill. Here, the act of starting the worship is like a vow because the first part of the worship becomes dedicated to Allah. Thus, to protect that dedication, completion is required. Further evidence is provided by the Quranic command to complete Hajj and 'Umrah (2:196), which is understood to protect the ihram. Similarly, the first part of any nafl act must be protected by completing it. The passage also addresses an objection: that there is merely abstention (imtina') from the act, not invalidation (ibtaal). The response is that the incomplete parts would have become worship if completed, so leaving them is like invalidating them. The weight of this ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah, as it is a well-established principle in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
النفل (al-nafl): Supererogatory act of worship, not obligatory in origin but becomes obligatory upon initiation.
النذر (al-nadhr): A vow where one obligates an act upon oneself by utterance, making it wajib.
صيانة (siyanah): Protection; here, the purpose of completing the act to protect the initial dedication to Allah.
الإبطال (al-ibṭāl): Invalidation; in the text, not completing is likened to ibtāl because the potential worship is lost.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, what is the ruling on completing a supererogatory prayer after one has begun it?
A) It is optional to continue or stop.
B) It is obligatory (wajib) to complete.
C) It is recommended (mandub) to complete.
D) It is prohibited to stop if one intends to complete.

Key Takeaway
A supererogatory act once initiated becomes wajib to complete by analogy to a vow; the Quranic command to complete Hajj and Umrah (2:196) provides the textual anchor through the illah of protecting the initial consecration.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

The Definition and Types of Rukhsah (Legal License)
Definition and types of rukhsah with commentary and examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define rukhsah, distinguish it from 'azimah, classify its types (haqiqi vs. majazi), and apply the Hanafi conditions for its validity to concrete cases.

Core Idea
Rukhsah is a concession that suspends punishment while the prohibition remains—it is not permissibility.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi classification of rukhsah as a distinct category of hukm shari. The text explains that rukhsah is not a lifting of the prohibition (hurmah) but a dispensation from punishment under specific conditions. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying legal rulings in cases of necessity and duress. The commentary delves into the two types of rukhsah—haqiqi (real) and majazi (metaphorical)—and provides examples from the sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of rukhsah in the Hanafi school
Locate the commentator's statement that defines rukhsah as 'what is treated like mubah in terms of dropping punishment, not that it is mubah in itself, while the prohibition (hurma) and its ruling both remain.' Note the critical distinction: rukhsah does not make the act halal; it only removes the liability for punishment.
The term 'mubah' here refers to the act being free from punishment, not from sin.
2
Distinguish between the two categories of rukhsah relative to 'azimah
The text explains two types: (1) where 'azimah is completely absent in all aspects, making the rukhsah a 'most complete metaphor' (a'tamm al-majaz); (2) where 'azimah is present in some materials, making the rukhsah 'less metaphorical.' Understand that the first type has no resemblance to the original ruling at all, while the second retains some connection.
These categories are analytical; the actual application is in the examples.
3
Analyze the examples given for rukhsah haqiqiyyah
The commentator provides four key examples: one coerced to utter kufr (with inner faith), a fasting person coerced to break the fast, one coerced to destroy another's property, and one who abandons commanding good due to fear. For each, note that the prohibition remains (e.g., shirk, fasting violation, property violation, abandoning wajib), but punishment is waived because the actor's right or necessity overrides.
These are classic Hanafi cases illustrating rukhsah with conditions like ikrah (duress) and khawf (fear).
4
Examine the glosses on defining characteristics
The hashiyah (marginal commentary) clarifies that rukhsah does not imply ibahah (permissibility)—citing that even if a sinner is forgiven, the sin is not made halal. Also, it distinguishes between mulji' (compelling) and ghayr mulji' (non-compelling) duress; only the former qualifies for rukhsah in the examples given.
This reinforces the precision required in applying rukhsah: severe duress with inner aversion.
5
Synthesize the legal principle and its scope
From this passage, derive the principle: When a prohibition conflicts with a greater harm (e.g., loss of life, limb, or essential rights), the sharia grants rukhsah by suspending punishment, while the prohibition remains a sin. This applies across ibadat and muamalat under conditions of genuine necessity.
This is a key usul principle for solving conflicts between darurah and hukm.

A chapter on the rulings of legal licenses and the two other categories. Since 'azimah (original ruling) is absent from consideration and not present, rukhsah (license) in its place is metaphorical, meaning that applying the term rukhsah to these two is metaphorical; for it has become in the position of 'azimah in the last two categories—i.e., the rukhsah stands in its place. Then in the first of these, since 'azimah is absent from the entire aspect and not present in any single material (case) in contrast to 'azimah in the last two categories, the rukhsah is the most complete metaphor, having no resemblance to reality at all, unlike the second category, where 'azimah is found in some materials, so the rukhsah is less metaphorical. As for the most deserving type of reality (actual license): it is what is deemed permissible—i.e., treated like permissible in terms of dropping punishment, not that it is permissible in itself, while the prohibition and its ruling (unlawfulness) both remain. Since the prohibited act and its unlawfulness are both present, caution and 'azimah lie in refraining from it, yet despite that, a license is given to engage in the opposite action. Thus, this type is most deserving of the name 'rukhsah' over the remaining aspects. [Commentary: 'i.e., 'azimah' refers to this type for one coerced to utter the word of kufr, i.e., like the license given to one coerced to utter the word of kufr out of fear for his life or a limb, not less than that; for he is permitted to utter it on his tongue provided his heart is steadfast in faith, even though the prohibited act (shirk) and its unlawfulness are both present. And the creation of the world is the cause of faith and prohibition of shirk.] The two metaphorical categories: i.e., those two where one is more complete than the other. (Al-Muhashi) 'In some materials': i.e., in other than the place of license. (Al-Qamar) [continues with glosses]
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the legal definition and types of rukhsah (license) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author, a commentator (sharh), explains that rukhsah is of two categories relative to 'azimah: one where 'azimah is completely absent (thus the rukhsah is a pure metaphor), and another where 'azimah is present in some cases but not others (less metaphorical). The most authentic type of rukhsah is that which is treated like mubah (permissible) in that the actor is not punished, even though the prohibition and its ruling (unlawfulness) remain in effect. This is called 'rukhsah haqiqiyyah' (real license). The commentator gives examples: one coerced to utter kufr under threat of death or loss of limb (with inner faith retained), a fasting person coerced to break his fast under duress, one coerced to destroy another's property (with liability remaining), and one who fears for his life and abandons commanding good to a tyrannical ruler. In each case, the prohibition remains, but by rukhsah the act is excused from punishment. The glosses clarify that rukhsah is not ibahah (permissibility) and that duress must be compelling (mulji') to justify the license.

Key Terms
الرخصة (al-rukhsah): A legal concession that treats an act as permissible in terms of punishment while the original prohibition remains unchanged.
العزيمة (al-'azimah): The original, permanent ruling that applies in normal circumstances without any concession.
الإكراه الملجئ (al-ikrah al-mulji'): Compelling duress that threatens life or limb (e.g., threat of death, amputation), sufficient to justify rukhsah in Hanafi law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi usul, what is the effect of a rukhsah (license) on the original prohibition (hurmah) of the act?
A) The prohibition is completely removed and the act becomes permissible (mubah).
B) The prohibition remains, but the person is not punished for committing the act.
C) The prohibition is temporarily lifted for the duration of the necessity.
D) The prohibition is transferred from the act to the intention.

Key Takeaway
Rukhsah is a concession that drops punishment while preserving the prohibition—a crucial distinction from permissibility.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
The Most Complete Type of Concession: Lifting of Hardships
Defines the most complete type of rukhsa as lifting of isr and aghlal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the most complete type of rukhsa in Hanafi usul, distinguish between the concession and the heavy obligations it removes, and apply this definition to examples like the reduction of fifty daily prayers to five.

Core Idea
The most complete concession is the lifting of crushing obligations, not the easing itself.

In Hanafi usul, concessions are of two types: incomplete (permitting something otherwise prohibited) and complete. This passage defines the most complete type as the removal of the heavy burdens (al-isr wa al-aghlal) that were imposed on previous communities. Understanding this distinction is critical for correctly applying the concept of rukhsa and avoiding the common error of conflating the burden with its removal.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two types of rukhsa
Recall that rukhsa (concession) comes in two categories: an incomplete concession permits what was originally prohibited (e.g., eating carrion in necessity), while a complete concession involves the removal or lightening of an existing obligation. Identify which type this passage describes.
The complete concession removes the very obligation itself, not just provides an alternative.
2
Locate the linguistic metaphor
Examine the terms 'isr' and 'aghlal'. They are metaphors (kinaya) for heavy, restrictive obligations. 'Isr' literally means a weight that confines movement; 'aghlal' are fetters that bind. Understand how these terms characterize the pre-Islamic laws as burdensome.
The metaphors emphasize the crushing nature of the original obligations.
3
Correct the potential misunderstanding
The text warns: 'isr and aghlal are not the concession; they are the heavy obligations themselves. The concession is their removal (wad'). A student might mistakenly think the burdens themselves are the rukhsa. Clarify that the rukhsa is the act of lifting, not the thing lifted.
The commentary (al-Qamar) explicitly corrects this possible misreading.
4
Apply the definition to the example of prayer
Consider the well-known example: the original obligation of fifty prayers per day and night was lifted, leaving only five. The fifty prayers were the 'isr and aghlal' (heavy burden); their reduction to five is the complete rukhsa. Trace how this illustrates the definition.
This example is from the hadith of Mi'raj and is standard in Hanafi usul.
5
Summarize the legal effect
The athar (legal effect) of this complete rukhsa is that the heavy obligations no longer bind this umma. They are replaced by lighter obligations. Recognize that the concession is a divine mercy (yusr) for this community.
This effect is permanent (naskh), not situational like other rukhas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما أتم نوعي المجاز فما وضع عنا من الإصر والأغلال أي سقط عنا ولم يشرع في حقنا ما كان في الشرائع السابقة من المِحَن الشاقة، والأعمال الثقيلة، والإصر هو الشدة، والأغلال جمع غُل أي المواثيق اللازمة كالغُل، والأظهر أنهما جميعًا كناية عن الأمور الشاقة

الله
فإن البلية إذا عمّت إلخ ) وفي كل لغة هذا المثل شائع. (السنبلي) إلا أن يضعفه الصوم إلخ: ليس المراد مطلق الضعف فإنه لازم للصوم عادة، بل الضعف الذي يخاف منه الهلاك أو يفوت منه أمر أهم كالجهاد. (القمر) فإن صام: أي حين كان يضعفه الصوم. (القمر) يموت آما: لأنه صار قاتلاً لنفسه.(القمر) يموت آتما إلخ لأن الإفطار لزمه في هذه الحالة، فلو بذل نفسه لإقامة الصوم صار قتيلاً بالصوم، وهو المباشرة لفعل الصوم، فيصير قاتلاً نفسه بما صار به مجاهدًا، وهو الصوم من غير تحصيل المقصود، وهو إقامة حق تعالى؛ لأنه أخر عنه، وذلك حرام كما قتل نفسه بالسيف الذي يجاهد به مع الكفار كان حراما، وفيه تغير للمشروع أيضًا؛ لأن المشروع في حقه إما التأخير أو جواز التعجيل على وجه تضمّن يسرا، وأما التعجيل على وجه يؤدّي الهلاك فليس بمشروع؛ فكان فعله تغيرًا للمشروع؛ فيكون حراما. (السنبلي) من الإصر إلخ بيان لما في قوله ما وضع عنّا وحينئذٍ فصار المعنى "وأما أتم نوعي المجاز فالإصر والأغلال" وهذا ليس بصحيح؛ فإن الإصر والأغلال هي التكاليف الشاقة، وهي ليست من الرخصة؛ فلا بد من أن يقال: إن في الكلام حذف مُضافين، أي فمحل وضع ما وُضع عنا من الإصر والأغلال كالصلاة مثلاً كانت خمسين في يوم وليلة، ثمّ وضع عنا ما زاد على الخمس، فالصلاة محل وضع ما وضع عنا، وقس على هذا. (القمر) أي سقط تفسير لقوله: وضع عنا . (القمر) والإصر هو الشدة الإصر بالكسر أصله الثقل الذي يأصر صاحبه، أي يحبسه من التحرك لثقله، كذا قال البيضاوي. (القمر) والإصر إلخ كذا قال في عين المعاني، وقال في "الكشاف": الإصر الثقل الذي يأصر صاحبه أي يحبسه من الحِراك لثقله، وهو مثل لثقل تكليفهم. (السنبلي)
And as for the most complete of the two types of concession (mujaz), it is what was removed from us of 'isr and aghlal, i.e., it has fallen from us, and what was in previous laws of severe trials and heavy works was not legislated for us. 'Isr is severity, and aghlal is the plural of ghull, i.e., binding pledges like a fetter. The most apparent is that both are metaphors for difficult things. Then the commentary: 'If calamity becomes widespread, etc.' And in every language this proverb is common. (al-Sanbali) 'Except that fasting weakens him, etc.' is not meant absolute weakness, for it is necessary for fasting usually, but weakness that fears destruction or causes loss of a more important matter like jihad. (al-Qamar) 'If he fasts': i.e., when fasting weakens him. (al-Qamar) 'He dies sinful': because he becomes a killer of himself. (al-Qamar) 'He dies sinful, etc.' because breaking the fast became necessary in this situation; if he offered himself to perform fasting, he becomes killed by fasting, and that is directly performing the act of fasting, so he becomes a killer of himself by what he made himself strive in—and that is fasting without achieving the objective, which is fulfilling the right of Allah Most High; because he delayed it, and that is forbidden just as killing oneself with the sword he uses to fight the disbelievers is forbidden. It also involves changing what is legislated; because what is legislated for him is either postponement or permissibility of hastening in a way that includes ease. As for hastening in a way that leads to destruction, it is not legislated; so his action is a change to what is legislated, thus it is forbidden. (al-Sanbali) 'Of isr, etc.' is an explanation of what is in His saying 'what was placed from us.' When that is the case, the meaning becomes 'And as for the most complete of the two types of concession, it is isr and aghlal.' But this is not correct; because isr and aghlal are the heavy obligations, and they are not from the concession; so it must be said that in the speech there is deletion of two genitive constructions, i.e., the place of what was removed from us of isr and aghlal—like prayer, for example, was fifty in a day and night, then what exceeded five was removed from us—so prayer is the locus of what was removed from us. Analogize based on this. (al-Qamar) i.e., 'falling' is interpretation of His saying 'He placed from us.' (al-Qamar) 'Isr is severity'—isr, with kasra, originally means the weight that imprisons its owner, i.e., prevents him from moving due to its heaviness. Thus said al-Baydawi. (al-Qamar) 'Isr, etc.' thus said in 'Ayn al-Ma'ani, and in al-Kashshaf: 'isr is the weight that imprisons its owner, i.e., prevents him from movement due to its heaviness, and it is a metaphor for the heaviness of their obligation.' (al-Sanbali)
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage defines the most complete type of concession (atammu naway al-mujaz) as the lifting of 'isr and aghlal from the Muslim community. These terms refer to the severe burdens and heavy obligations that existed in previous religious laws (shara'i' salifa), such as the original obligation of fifty daily prayers. The 'isr is literally the weight that confines, and aghlal are fetters, both metaphorically representing the severe trials ('mihan shaqqa') and heavy works (a'mal thaqila) that were abrogated for this umma. The commentary clarifies an important nuance: 'isr and aghlal themselves are not the concession; rather, the concession consists in their removal (wad'). The locus (mahall) of the removal is the acts of worship themselves (like prayer) that were originally heavy and then lightened. The marginal note (al-Qamar) corrects a misunderstanding: one might think 'isr and aghlal are the concession, but they are the heavy obligations, not the relaxation. The linguistic analysis confirms that 'isr means hardship (shidda) and aghlal means binding bonds, both used as kinaya (metaphor) for difficult matters. The passage also repeats the earlier point about weakness and dying sinful, but in the context of explaining the condition for prefering breaking the fast.

Key Terms
الإصر (al-isr): Severity (shidda); literally a weight that confines a person; metaphor for the heavy trials in previous laws
الأغلال (al-aghlal): Plural of ghull, meaning fetters or binding pledges; metaphor for obligations that restrict freedom
المجاز (al-mujaz): Concession or dispensation; here the most complete type is the lifting of severe burdens
الوضع (al-wad'): Removal or setting aside; the act of abrogating the heavy obligation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the most complete type of concession (rukhsa) according to this passage?
A) The permission to break the fast during travel
B) The lifting of severe obligations like the original fifty prayers from previous communities
C) The permissibility of eating carrion in dire need
D) The reduction of prayers while traveling

Key Takeaway
The most complete rukhsa is the permanent removal of a heavy past obligation, illustrated by the reduction of fifty prayers to five.

Cause of Obligation of Iman: Creation as Sabab
Explanation of the cause for wajib al-iman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the sabab (cause) for the obligation of faith (wajib al-iman) and explain the rational proof (dalil) that the creation of the world necessitates a Creator.

Core Idea
The duty to believe in the Creator arises from the world's createdness; effects prove their cause.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar establishes a foundational usul principle: the sabab (cause) for the obligation of faith (wajib al-iman) is the createdness of the world (huduth al-alam). The text uses a powerful Bedouin analogy to illustrate that observable effects point to their cause. The commentary clarifies that the world's occurrence is the cause of the obligation, not the inner act of belief itself. Understanding this sabab is crucial for grasping how the Lawgiver attaches obligations to manifest signs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the explicit sabab
Locate the phrase 'لا يجب إلا لحدوث العالم' – it states that faith in the Maker is not obligatory except due to the occurrence of the world. That is the sabab.
The sabab is huduth al-alam, the temporal creation of the universe.
2
Distinguish sabab of obligation vs. sabab of the act
The commentary stresses that huduth al-alam is not the cause of the act of faith itself but of its obligation. The ruling (wajib) is attached to a cause (sabab), not the act's essence.
In Hanafi usul, sabab is a manifest attribute that the Lawgiver linked to the hukm.
3
Analyze the rational dalil (Bedouin proverb)
The Bedouin saying 'al-ba'ratu tadullu 'ala al-ba'ir' (dung leads to camel) is an analogy: observable effects indicate their cause. Similarly, the structured world indicates a Creator.
This is a rational proof (dalil 'aqli) – the text uses it to show that huduth necessitates a muhdith.
4
Connect to the attributes of the Maker
The passage mentions 'al-Sani’' and commentary adds 'existence, oneness, and all attributes.' The cause of obligation also entails knowing these attributes.
The sabab triggers the obligation to know the Creator with His attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في أسباب الأحكام المشروعة بيان الأحكام والأسباب ثم شرع بعدها في بيان المسببات على طريق اللف والنشر المرتب، فقال: للإيمان هذا مسبب لحدوث العالم، فإن الإيمان بالصانع لا يجب إلا لحدوث العالم؛ إذ لو لم يكن حادثا لما احتجنا إلى الصانع كما قال الأعرابي : البعرة تدل على البعير وآثار الأقدام على المسير، فسماء ذات أبراج وأرض ذات فجاج كيف لا تدل على اللطيف الخبير. بالصانع: أي بوجوده وتوحيده وسائر صفاته. (القمر) لا يجب هذا إيماء إلى أن حدوث العالم ليس سببا لنفس الإيمان بل لوجوب الإيمان ففي كلام المصنف له "للإيمان" المضاف محذوف، أي لوجوب الإيمان. (القمر) إلا لحدوث إلخ : فإن حدوث العالم دليل على تحقق المؤمن به ؛ إذ لو لم يكن إلخ. (القمر) ميداً إلى الصانع أي الصانع الموجود الموصوف بصفات الكمال كالعلم والقدرة والإرادة وغيرها. (القمر)
Chapter on the causes of legislated rulings, explaining the rulings and the causes. Then he began after them to explain the consequences in the style of ordered wrapping and unwrapping, and said: For faith, this is a consequence of the occurrence of the world. Indeed, faith in the Maker is not obligatory except due to the occurrence of the world; for if it were not occurring, we would not need the Maker, as the Bedouin said: The dung leads to the camel, and the footsteps to the traveler. So a sky with constellations and an earth with ravines—how could they not indicate the Kind, the Aware? (Commentary:) "By the Maker": i.e., by His existence, oneness, and all His attributes. (Al-Qamar) "It is not obligatory"—this indicates that the occurrence of the world is not a cause for faith itself, but for the obligation of faith. Thus in the author's statement, the added word in "for faith" is omitted, i.e., for the obligation of faith. (Al-Qamar) "Except due to occurrence, etc.": For the occurrence of the world is proof of the existence of the One believed in; for if it were not, etc. (Al-Qamar) "...to the Maker": i.e., the existing Maker described with attributes of perfection such as knowledge, power, will, and others. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 494

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the cause (sabab) for the obligation of faith (iman). The text states that the occurrence of the world (huduth al-alam) is the sabab for wajib al-iman. The author explains that without the world's createdness, there would be no need for a creator. The Bedouin proverb illustrates that effects point to causes. The commentary clarifies that the world's occurrence is not the cause of faith itself but of its obligation—i.e., it makes it necessary to believe in God. The term 'Maker' (al-Sani') here includes existence, tawhid, and all attributes. This is a foundational usul principle: the empirical fact of creation rationally necessitates the obligation to know the Creator.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): That which makes the obligation of a ruling exist, i.e., a cause in the sense of 'sabab' in usul al-fiqh.
حدوث العالم (huduth al-alam): The creation of the world from non-existence; it is the cause for the obligation of faith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the cause ('sabab') for the obligation of faith (iman)?
A) The existence of the Quran
B) The occurrence of the world
C) Prophetic miracles
D) Rational thinking

Key Takeaway
The sabab for wajib al-iman is huduth al-alam; the rational proof shows that effects necessitate a cause, making the duty to know the Creator universal.

Time as the Cause of Prayer's Obligation
Defines time as sabab for wajib al-salat with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why time (waqt) is considered the cause (sabab) for the obligation of prayer according to Hanafi usul, and identify the evidentiary basis for this ruling.

Core Idea
Time is the manifest sign of Allah's hidden command, making it the sabab for the obligation of prayer.

In Hanafi usul, the obligation of the five daily prayers is tied to specific times. But how do we know that time itself is the cause, not just a condition? This passage from Noor al-Anwar clarifies that because Allah's command is hidden from direct perception, time—which is observable—stands in its place as the indicator (sabab). We will explore the evidence and wisdom behind this foundational rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Cause
The passage states that prayer is related to time and that time is the cause (sabab) for its obligation. Note that the author uses the term 'sabab' in a technical usul sense: a manifest attribute that indicates the presence of a hidden ruling.
2
Analyze the Evidence for Time as Sabab
The author cites as evidence that prayers are named after times (e.g., 'Fajr prayer'). In Hanafi usul, this linguistic convention (إضافة الصلاة إلى الوقت) is considered a strong indicator (dalil) that time is the cause. Reflect on why naming alone suffices as evidence.
3
Understand the Wisdom (Hikma) Behind the Cause
The passage explains that Allah's blessings are continuous, requiring gratitude. If gratitude were obligatory at every moment, worldly order would break. Therefore, Allah appointed specific times for prayer—times of renewed blessings: night, dawn, midday, and afternoon. Two prayers are assigned to midday (Zuhr and Asr) and one to the middle of the night (Isha). This is a divine mercy.
The wisdom does not constitute the cause but confirms its appropriateness.
4
Apply the Hanafi Usul Principle
Hanafi usul teaches that when the ruling is hidden, its sabab is made manifest. Here, the command (ijab) is hidden, so time serves as the sabab. This principle is called 'إقامة السبب مقام السبب' or substitution of cause. Trace how the passage explicitly states this substitution.
This applies to other worship acts where time is also a sabab (e.g., fasting for Ramadan).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والصلاة هذا متعلّق بالوقت؛ فإن الوقت سبب وجوب الصلاة بإيجاب الله تعالى في هذا الوقت، والإيجاب غِيْبَ عنا، فأقيم الوقت مقامه. (القمر) سبب إلخ بدليل إضافة الصلاة إلى الوقت يقال: صلاة الفجر وغير ذلك.(القمر) بإيجاب الله تعالى أي بأمره تعالى؛ إذ نِعَم الله تعالى تصل إلى العباد كل وقت؛ فلا بد لهم من شكر، وهو بالصلاة أكمل، فلو استوعب العبد الليل والنهار بالشكر لاختل مصالح العالم، فعين الله تعالى له أوقاتا هي الليل ومبدأ النهار ووسط النهار، فإن هذه الأوقات أوقات تجدّد النعم، وجعل في وسط النهار صلاتين، وفي وسط الليل صلاة؛ لأن النهار لليقظة والليل للنوم، وهذا رحمة وفضل من الله تعالى لمعرفة أسرار الأحكام الإلهية مقام آخر. (القمر)
And prayer—this is related to time. Indeed, time is the cause of the obligation of prayer due to Allah's making it obligatory in this time, and the obligation is hidden from us, so time is set in its place. (Al-Qamar) "Cause, etc."—by the evidence of adding prayer to time: it is said 'the dawn prayer' and so on. (Al-Qamar) "Due to Allah's making it obligatory"—i.e., by His command. Indeed, Allah's blessings reach the servants at every time, so they must show gratitude, and it is most perfect through prayer. If the servant occupied night and day with gratitude, the world's interests would be disrupted. So Allah appointed for him times: the night, the beginning of the day, and the middle of the day. For these are times of renewed blessings. He made two prayers in the middle of the day and one in the middle of the night because the day is for wakefulness and the night for sleep. This is mercy and grace from Allah. Understanding the secrets of divine rulings is another station. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 494

Commentary
This passage defines the sabab for the obligation of salat as time (waqt). The author clarifies that Allah's command (ijab) is hidden from us, so time—which is manifest—is made its substitute. The commentary elaborates: the evidence is that prayers are named after times (e.g., Fajr). The wisdom is that Allah's blessings are constant, requiring gratitude; prayer is the best form. If thanksgiving were required constantly, worldly order would collapse, so specific times are fixed based on the renewal of blessings: night, dawn, mid-day (two prayers), and midnight (one). This reflects divine mercy. The passage is a typical Hanafi usul exposition linking a manifest attribute ('alamah) to a ruling.

Key Terms
الوقت (al-waqt): The specific time period designated for each prayer; it is the cause (sabab) for wajib al-salat.
سبب (sabab): A manifest attribute that indicates a hidden ruling; here, time is the sabab for the obligation of prayer.
إيجاب (ijab): The act of making something obligatory; here it refers to Allah's hidden command.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what evidence is cited to support that time is the cause (sabab) for prayer's obligation?
A) The Quranic verse 'Establish prayer at the decline of the sun'
B) The fact that prayers are named after times, e.g., 'Fajr prayer'
C) The hadith 'Prayer is a duty on believers at fixed times'
D) Consensus of the Companions on this matter

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, time is the manifest cause (sabab) for the obligation of prayer, established through linguistic evidence that prayers are named after times.

The Cause (Sabab) of Zakat in Hanafi Usul
Defines ownership of growing wealth as the sabab for zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three components of the sabab for zakat (mal nami hawli exceeding need) and apply them to determine when zakat is wajib.

Core Idea
Zakat is caused by ownership of growing annual wealth beyond basic need.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, a sabab is the visible cause that triggers a hukm. This passage from a commentary on a classical usul text defines the sabab for zakat with precision: it is not mere ownership, but ownership of wealth that is growing (actual/potential), passed a lunar year, and beyond personal need. Understanding this definition is key to deriving the rulings of zakat correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hukm being triggered
Zakat is an obligation. The sabab is what makes it wajib. Look for the term 'cause of its obligation'.
2
Extract the sabab definition
The text says: 'the growing, annual wealth that exceeds the amount of need is the cause.' Write down the three qualifiers: growing, annual, exceeding need.
3
Understand 'growing' (nami)
Growth means wealth that can increase, e.g., trade goods, livestock, gold/silver used for trade. Pure personal use items are not nami.
Hanafis include potential growth, e.g., money kept for trade has potential.
4
Understand 'annual' (hawli)
A full lunar year must pass on the wealth while it remains in the owner's possession above nisab.
The commentary says the obligation renews yearly because wealth is considered renewed each year.
5
Understand 'exceeding need'
Wealth used for basic necessities does not trigger zakat. Only surplus wealth is subject.
This is a condition (shart) for the sabab to be effective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والزكاة هذا ناظر إلى ملك المال، فإن المال النامي الحولي الذي هو زائد على قدر الحاجة سبب وجوبها. (القمر) فإن المال إلى آخره أي فإن ملك المال إلى آخره. (القمر) سبب وجوبها : فالمال النامي نعمة لا بد لها من شكر، وهو مؤاساة الفقير على حسب أمر المنعم، ويتجدد المال تقديرًا بتجدد الحول، فيتكرر الوجوب بتكرر المال تقديرًا (القمر)
And zakat—this looks to ownership of wealth. Indeed, the growing, annual wealth that exceeds the amount of need is the cause of its obligation. (Al-Qamar) "For wealth, etc."—i.e., for ownership of wealth, etc. (Al-Qamar) "Cause of its obligation": For growing wealth is a blessing that must be thanked, and that is aiding the poor as per the command of the Benefactor. Wealth is renewed in estimation with the renewal of the year, so the obligation is renewed with the renewal of wealth in estimation. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 494

Commentary
This passage identifies the sabab for zakat as 'ownership of growing, annual wealth that exceeds basic need.' The commentary explains that such wealth is a blessing requiring gratitude, and that gratitude is expressed by giving to the poor as commanded. The obligation recurs yearly because wealth is considered renewed with each passing year (hawl). This illustrates the Hanafi principle that zakat is a recurring obligation tied to the cause of ownership of niṣāb over a lunar year. The sabab is not just ownership but ownership of a specific type of wealth: namā' (growing) and ḥawlī (annual).

Key Terms
المال النامي الحولي (al-mal al-nami al-hawli): Wealth that grows (actual or potential) and has a full lunar year passed over it; this is the cause for zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Any wealth owned for a year
B) Wealth that is growing and annual and exceeds need
C) Wealth that is purely for trade
D) Wealth that is inherited

Key Takeaway
The sabab for zakat is precise: it is ownership of growing annual wealth beyond basic need.

The Sabab for Fasting: The Month of Ramadan
Defines the sabab for fasting obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the sabab for the obligation of fasting and explain the Hanafi evidence of idafa and takarrur.

Core Idea
The month of Ramadan itself is the sabab for fasting, not the moon sighting.

In Hanafi usul, every obligation has a sabab (cause) that triggers it. This passage clarifies that the sabab for fasting is the month of Ramadan, specifically its days. It uses two arguments: the linguistic attribution of fasting to the month (idafa) and the recurrence of the obligation with the month's recurrence. Understanding this helps distinguish the sabab from the means of knowing it (e.g., moon sighting).

Guided Path
1
Identify the sabab
Read the first sentence: 'Fasting is related to the days of the month of Ramadan.' The text explicitly states that the obligation of fasting is due to the month of Ramadan. This is the sabab.
The sabab is a defined time period, not an act.
2
Analyze the first evidence: idafa
The phrase 'attribution of fasting to Ramadan' means we say 'sawm Ramadan' – the fasting of Ramadan. In Arabic, idafa can indicate causality (e.g., 'hubb al-watan' meaning love for the homeland). Here, the idafa shows that fasting belongs to Ramadan, implying Ramadan is the cause.
Idafa is a linguistic indicator of connection.
3
Analyze the second evidence: takarrur
Fasting repeats with the repetition of Ramadan; it occurs annually. This shows the obligation is tied to the month, not to a one-time commandment.
Takarrur suggests a permanent link.
4
Recognize the exclusion
Allah excluded nights from being a place for fasting, so the sabab applies only to the days (daylight hours). This is a divine specification.
The sabab is the month, but the mahall (locus) is the day.
5
Differentiate from means of knowledge
The moon sighting or calendar calculation is not the sabab; it is merely a way to know that the month has begun. The sabab remains the month itself.
This distinction is crucial for usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والصوم هذا متعلق بأيام شهر رمضان، فإن وجوب الصوم بسبب شهر رمضان بدليل إضافته إليه، وتكرّره، بتكرره لكن الله تعالى أخرج الليالي عن محلية الصوم؛ فتعين له النهار. (القمر) بسبب شهر رمضان: فالنفس طاغية لا تميل إلى الشكر، ففرض العموم قهرا عليها. (القمر) إضافته إليه أي إضافة الصوم إلى رمضان يقال: صوم رمضان، ويتكرر الصوم بتكرر رمضان. (القمر) أخرج إلخ وقد مرّ تفصيل هذا المبحث في الشرح والحاشية، فتذكر.(القمر)
And fasting—this is related to the days of the month of Ramadan. Indeed, the obligation of fasting is due to the month of Ramadan, evidenced by its attribution to it, and it repeats with its repetition. But Allah, exalted, excluded the nights from being a place for fasting, so the day is specified for it. (Al-Qamar) "Due to the month of Ramadan": For the soul is rebellious, not inclined to gratitude, so the general obligation was imposed upon it forcibly. (Al-Qamar) "Its attribution to it"—i.e., the attribution of fasting to Ramadan: it is said 'fasting of Ramadan', and fasting repeats with the repetition of Ramadan. (Al-Qamar) "Excluded, etc."—the detail of this discussion has passed in the commentary and gloss, so remember. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 494

Commentary
This passage states that the sabab for the obligation of sawm is the month of Ramadan itself, specifically its days. Evidence: fasting is attributed to Ramadan (e.g., 'sawm Ramadan'), and it recurs annually. Allah excluded nights, so only daylight hours are for fasting. The commentary explains that the soul is rebellious, so an obligatory act is imposed forcibly to discipline it. This highlights that the cause (sabab) is a specific time period (the month), not a person's action or other factor. The nights are excluded by divine designation, so the ruling applies only to the days.

Key Terms
شهر رمضان (shahr Ramadan): The lunar month of Ramadan; it is the sabab for the obligation of fasting.
الإضافة (al-idafa): Linguistic attribution; in this context, the phrase 'sawm Ramadan' indicates a causal relationship.
التكرر (al-takarrur): Recurrence; the fact that fasting repeats with the repetition of Ramadan shows the obligation is tied to the month.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is presented as evidence that the month of Ramadan is the sabab for fasting?
A) The reward for fasting is multiplied in Ramadan
B) Fasting is attributed to Ramadan in speech and repeats annually
C) The Prophet fasted the whole month
D) Ramadan is the month the Quran was revealed

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the sabab for fasting is the month of Ramadan itself, not the sighting or any other factor.

Identifying the Sabab for Sadaqat al-Fitr: The Supported Head
Defines the supported head as the sabab for sadaqat al-fitr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Hanafi school identifies the sabab of sadaqat al-fitr as the 'head' under one's authority and apply this to determine for whom the obligation applies.

Core Idea
Sadaqat al-fitr is wajib for those you fully support and hold wilaya over—self, minor children, slaves—not for dependents without your authority.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar explains the cause (sabab) of sadaqat al-fitr according to the Hanafi school. Unlike other schools, the Hanafis tie the obligation to the concept of 'ra's' (head) – the person for whom one provides maintenance (nafaqa) and holds legal authority (wilaya). Understanding this causal link helps you see the inner logic of the ruling and its scope.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its sabab
State the hukm (sadaqat al-fitr is wajib) and note the sabab given: the 'ra's' that one 'supports and has authority over' (يمونه ويلي عليه).
The sabab is the reason for the obligation in Hanafi usul.
2
Analyze the definition of 'ra's'
Break down the definition: it includes oneself (primary), then one's minor children and slaves, because they are under full maintenance and authority.
Authority (wilaya) is key: it distinguishes included persons from excluded ones.
3
Apply the exclusion clause
Apply the text's negative examples: wife and adult children are excluded because the husband/father lacks wilaya over them in the required sense.
This is a direct application of the condition of authority.
4
Link to the annual repetition
Note the commentary: because the 'head' is renewed each year (survival), the sabab repeats, making sadaqat al-fitr annual from the day of Fitr.
The sabab's continuity determines the frequency of the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والصدقة الفطر هذا ناظر إلى الرأس الذي يمونه ويلي عليه، فإنه سبب لوجوب هذه الصدقة، والأصل في ذلك هو رأسه فإنه يمونه ويلي عليه ثم أولاده الصغار وعبيده، فإنه المتصدق يمونهم ويلي عليهم، بخلاف الزوجة والأولاد الكبار، فإنه لا يلي عليهم. (القمر) فإنه سبب إلخ ولما كانت الرأس باعتبار البقاء في كل سنة متجدّدة وجب الصدقة أيضا متكررة، واعتبر الشارع الابتداء من يوم الفطر. (القمر) بخلاف الزوجة فلا يجب صدقة الفطر على الزوج من الزوجة، وعلى الأب من أولاده الكبار. (القمر)
And the charity of Fitr—this looks to the head (ra's) that he supports and over whom he has authority. For it is the cause for the obligation of this charity. The origin in this is his own head, for he supports it and has authority over it, then his young children and his slaves, for he as the giver supports them and has authority over them. Unlike the wife and adult children, for he does not have authority over them. (Al-Qamar) "For it is the cause, etc.": Since the head is considered renewed with survival each year, the charity also becomes obligatory repeatedly, and the Lawgiver considered the beginning from the day of Fitr. (Al-Qamar) "Unlike the wife": so sadaqat al-fitr is not obligatory from the husband for the wife, nor from the father for his adult children. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage defines the sabab for sadaqat al-fitr as 'the head (ra's) that one supports and has authority over' (i.e., the person one maintains). The primary head is oneself, then minor children and slaves. The cause is the relationship of maintenance and authority. The commentary clarifies that since the head is 'renewed' annually (survival), the charity is also due annually, starting from the day of Eid al-Fitr. Exclusion is made for wives and adult children because the husband does not have authority (wilaya) over the wife, and the father does not have authority over adult children. This reflects Hanafi fiqh where sadaqat al-fitr is obligatory on a person for himself and those he supports with full authority.

Key Terms
الرأس (al-ra's): The head (person) that one supports and has authority over; the sabab for sadaqat al-fitr.
سبب (sabab): The cause or reason that triggers a legal obligation. In usul, it is a clear attribute that the Lawgiver has tied to the ruling.
ولاية (wilaya): Legal authority or guardianship over another person, especially in matters of maintenance and control.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is sadaqat al-fitr not obligatory on a husband for his wife?
A) Because the wife is not a Muslim.
B) Because the husband does not have authority (wilaya) over his wife.
C) Because the wife is considered a 'head' for herself.
D) Because the wife is not dependent.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the sabab for sadaqat al-fitr is the 'head' under one's maintenance and authority; this restricts the obligation to self, minor children, and slaves.

The Cause of Hajj: The House, Not Time
Defines the Bayt as the sabab for hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the cause (sabab) of the obligation of Hajj in the Hanafi school and distinguish it from its condition (shart).

Core Idea
The House is the cause of Hajj; time is only a condition, not a cause.

In this short passage from Noor al-Anwar, we explore why Hajj is obligatory only once in a lifetime. The text clarifies that the Ka'bah itself is the cause (sabab) of the obligation, while the appointed months are merely a condition (shart) for performance. This distinction affects the repetition of the obligation and is supported by the Quranic verse 'Hajj of the House.'

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is Hajj. The ruling is that it is obligatory (wajib) once in a lifetime. Why once? Because the cause is one.
The Hanafi position is that Hajj is wajib immediately upon capability, but the obligation is a single lifetime duty.
2
Distinguish cause from condition
The passage states that time (the months of Hajj) is a condition (shart) for the validity of performance, not the cause. If time were the cause, Hajj would be repeated each year.
This is a key usul distinction: sabab triggers the obligation; shart enables valid performance.
3
Analyze the Quranic evidence
The verse 'And for Allah is upon the people the Hajj of the House' (3:97) attributes Hajj to the House, not to time. This shows the House is the cause.
The Hanafi principle: idafah (construct phrase) indicates causation.
4
Apply the implication
Since the cause is singular (one House), the obligation is not repeated. If it were time, it would repeat annually.
This reasoning uses talil: identifying the illah (cause) to derive the hukm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحج هذا ناظر إلى البيت، فإنه سبب وجوب الحج، ولهذا لم يتكرّر في العمر؛ لأن البيت واحد والوقت شرطه وظرفه. (القمر) فإنه سبب إلخ بدليل إضافة الحج إلى البيت قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حج البيت آل عمران: ۹۷) (القمر) شرطه أي شرط جواز الأداء، وليس الوقت سبب الحج وإلا يتكرر الحج بتكرر الوقت. (القمر)
And Hajj—this looks to the House. For it is the cause of the obligation of Hajj, and for this reason it is not repeated in a lifetime because the House is one, and time is its condition and container. (Al-Qamar) "For it is the cause, etc."—by evidence of attributing Hajj to the House. Allah said: {And for Allah is upon the people the Hajj of the House} (Al-Imran 3:97). (Al-Qamar) "Its condition"—i.e., the condition for the validity of performance. Time is not the cause of Hajj; otherwise, Hajj would be repeated with the repetition of time. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage identifies the sabab for hajj as the Bayt (Ka'bah). Since the cause is a single entity (one House), hajj is obligatory only once in a lifetime. Time (the appointed months) is a condition (shart) for performing the hajj, not the cause. The commentary cites the Quranic verse 'Hajj of the House' to show the attribution. If time were the cause, hajj would be repeated annually, but it is not. This is a standard Hanafi position: hajj is wajib once upon fulfillment of conditions, and the cause is the Bayt itself, not the season.

Key Terms
البيت (al-bayt): The Ka'bah; it is the cause (sabab) for the obligation of Hajj.
سبب (sabab): Legal cause that triggers an obligation.
شرط (shart): Condition for the validity of an act, not the cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is Hajj not repeated in a lifetime?
A) Because it is physically too demanding
B) Because its cause is a single entity, the House
C) Because time is not a condition
D) Because it is only for the wealthy

Key Takeaway
The House (Ka'bah) is the unique cause of Hajj, making the obligation a once-in-a-lifetime duty, with time serving only as a condition for performance.

The Cause (Sabab) of 'Ushr: Actual Land Produce
Defines the cause (sabab) for 'ushr as actual produce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the cause of obligation for 'ushr according to the Hanafi school and explain why the obligation falls if the crop is destroyed by a pestilence.

Core Idea
The obligation of 'ushr depends on actual produce, not land's potential; if crop is destroyed, no 'ushr is due.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, every hukm has a sabab (cause) that triggers it. This passage from Noor al-Anwar defines the sabab for 'ushr as actual produce from the land. The commentary clarifies that the obligation recurs with every harvest and falls if the crop is destroyed. Understanding this cause is essential for distinguishing 'ushr from kharaj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hukm and its sabab
Read the passage to find what ruling is being discussed (wujub al-ushr) and what triggers it ('actual produce from the land'). Write down the exact phrase that defines the sabab.
The sabab is 'al-ard al-namiyah bil-kharij tahqiqan'.
2
Note the condition for the sabab
The sabab is actual produce, not potential. The passage uses 'tahqiqan' to emphasize this — the produce must truly occur.
Contrast with kharaj which is based on estimation.
3
Understand the consequence of destruction
If a pestilence destroys the crop before harvest, the sabab is not realized, so the obligation falls. The passage says 'falls if a pestilence destroys the crop'.
This shows the sabab is contingent on actual existence.
4
Recognize recurrence
The obligation recurs with each instance of growth. If a land produces multiple yields in a year, 'ushr is due each time.
This differs from annual taxes based on land value.
5
Connect to kharaj
The commentary notes that kharaj also recurs with growth, but kharaj is based on estimation, not actual produce. Understand the difference between the two levies.
Kharaj is due even if the land is left fallow, but 'ushr is not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعشر هذا ناظر إلى الأرض النامية بالخارج تحقيقا؛ فإنه إذا حدث الخارج من الأرض تحقيقاً يجب العشر، وسقط إذا اصطلمت الزرع آفةً، ويتكرر الوجوب بتكرر النماء. (القمر) ويتكرر الوجوب إلخ : أي يتكرر وجوب العشر، وكذا وجوب الخراج بتكرر النماء، وهو تكرر الأرض النامية تحقيقاً أو تقديرًا ، فصار تكرر هما بتكرر السبب. (القمر)
And 'ushr—this looks to the land that grows [produce] externally in actuality. For when external [produce] occurs from the land in actuality, 'ushr is obligatory, and it falls if a pestilence destroys the crop. And the obligation recurs with the recurrence of growth. (Al-Qamar) "And the obligation recurs, etc.": i.e., the obligation of 'ushr recurs, and likewise the obligation of kharaj recurs with the recurrence of growth, which is the recurrence of land producing [growth] either in actuality or in estimation. So both recur with the recurrence of the cause. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage defines the sabab for 'ushr as land that actually produces (al-ard al-namiyah bil-kharij tahqiqan). Ushr is due only when actual produce occurs; if the crop is destroyed by a calamity, the obligation falls. The obligation recurs as often as produce recurs (e.g., multiple harvests per year). The commentary connects this to kharaj (land tax), noting that both 'ushr and kharaj recur with recurring growth, but 'ushr is based on actual produce, while kharaj is based on estimation (potential).

Key Terms
العشر (al-ushr): A tithe of one-tenth on produce of land; its cause is actual produce from the land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the obligation of 'ushr fall according to the passage?
A) If the land is fallow
B) If a pestilence destroys the crop
C) If the owner is non-Muslim
D) It never falls

Key Takeaway
The cause of 'ushr is actual produce from the land; without actual produce, no obligation arises.

The Cause of Kharaj: Land's Potential Productivity
Expands the phrase 'or in estimation' to define the cause of kharaj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the cause (sabab) of kharaj and explain why it is based on estimated land capability rather than actual cultivation.

Core Idea
Kharaj is due on land capable of cultivation, even if idle — the sabab is potential, not actual produce.

In Hanafi usul, every ruling has a cause (sabab) that triggers its obligation. This passage clarifies that kharaj is tied to the land's capacity for growth, not the owner's effort. Understanding this distinction is key to differentiating kharaj from 'ushr and to applying the ruling when the land is uncultivated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hukm and its sabab
The text states that kharaj is wajib. Its sabab is the land's tamakkun — its suitability for cultivation, even if not actually farmed.
Tamakkun here is objective potential, not the owner's ability to pay expenses.
2
Distinguish kharaj from 'ushr
'Ushr is based on actual produce; kharaj is based on land potential. This explains why kharaj is due even if the land is idle.
This distinction is critical for land tax classification in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Analyze the practical consequence when owner cannot cultivate
If the owner lacks means to farm, the Imam steps in to arrange sharecropping or leasing, collects kharaj from the yield, and returns surplus.
If no partner is found, the land is sold to satisfy the kharaj obligation.
4
Understand the ruling's rationale (hikmah)
The text notes this ruling is 'more suitable to the condition of the disbeliever deeply engrossed in worldly life' — a policy consideration (siyasah shar'iyyah) to ensure tax collection.
The cause (sabab) is the land's potential, but the wisdom behind it is not the same as the cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخراج هذا ناظر إلى قوله: "أو تقديرًا" ؛ فإن الأرض النامية بالخارج تقديرًا بالتمكن من الزراعة سبب للخراج، سواء زرعها أو عطلها، وهو الأليق بحال الكافر المتوغل في الدنيا. (القمر) بالتمكن متعلّق بقوله: تقديرًا، والمراد بالتمكن صلاحية الأرض للزراعة، لا استطاعة المالك مؤنة الزراعة، فإنه إذا لم يتمكن المالك من الزراعة ناب الإمام منابه في المزارعة والإجارة، ويأخذ الخراج من الغلة، ويردّ الفضل على المالك، وإن لم يجد من يعطيه من مزارعة أو إجارة يبيع الأرض، كذا نقل أعظم العلماء مولانا عبد السلام الأعظمي له. (القمر) وهو : أي أخذ الخراج وإن عطّل المالك الأرض. (القمر)
And kharaj—this looks to His statement: "or in estimation." For the land that grows externally in estimation due to capability of cultivation is the cause for kharaj, whether he cultivates it or leaves it idle. And it is more suitable to the condition of the disbeliever deeply engrossed in worldly life. (Al-Qamar) "Due to capability" is attached to His statement: "in estimation." What is meant by capability is the suitability of land for cultivation, not the owner's ability to afford cultivation expenses. For if the owner is not able to cultivate, the Imam takes his place in sharecropping and leasing, takes the kharaj from the yield, and returns the surplus to the owner. If he finds no one to give it to via sharecropping or leasing, he sells the land. This is transmitted by the greatest scholar, our master 'Abd al-Salam al-A'zami, to him. (Al-Qamar) "And it is"—i.e., taking kharaj even if the owner leaves the land idle. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage defines the sabab for kharaj as 'land that is capable of cultivation in estimation' (i.e., its potential productivity). Unlike 'ushr, kharaj is due even if the land is not cultivated, based on the land's capability. This is considered suitable for non-Muslim landowners (dhimmis) who are deeply attached to worldly gain. The commentary explains that 'capability' (tamakkun) refers to the land's suitability for agriculture, not the owner's financial ability. If the owner cannot cultivate, the Imam steps in to lease or sharecrop the land, collect kharaj from the produce, and return any surplus. If no partner is found, the land is sold. This reflects the Hanafi view that kharaj is a duty on the land itself, not conditioned on actual cultivation.

Key Terms
الخراج (al-kharaj): A land tax imposed on kharaji land (often owned by non-Muslims); its cause is the land's capacity for cultivation.
التمكن (al-tamakkun): Capability or suitability; here refers to the land's potential for cultivation, not the owner's ability to farm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the cause (sabab) for the obligation of kharaj according to the passage?
A) Actual produce from the land
B) The land's capability for cultivation (tamakkun)
C) The owner's intention to farm
D) The market value of the land

Key Takeaway
Kharaj is wajib because the land is capable of cultivation, not because it is actually cultivated — the sabab is potential productivity.
